; hitopadesha-slp1_p.txt
; Begun 07-24-2019 as copy of hitopadesha-slp1.txt
; Incorporates the 'marma-prakASikA' commentary of Kale -- these are
; the Sanskrit notes at the bottom of each page.
; These notes are inserted below the Analyzed Sandhi lines
; Format is ###.##P: <slp1 text>
;  There may be more than one ###.##P line, if a given line of text has
;  comments on more than one word. For example, see line 001.04 below.
; Also, use ###.##PE: <English translation of the prakASikA>
; ------------------------------------------------
; A convention of this file is that lines starting with semicolon are comments
; Begun approx. Apr 2016
; Each line is represented in two forms:
;  F  is the final sandhi form; this is the version one sees printed
;  A  is the analyzed sandhi form.  Here words are separated, if needed,
;     and word endings are changed to their original (pre-sandhi) form.
;     This step of analysis facilitates the further analysis of grammatical
;     form
; ------------------------------------------------------------------
; 2018-12-02   hitokale_slp1_v0.txt
; Begin a new phase. Previous version hitopadesha-slp1.txt
;  The aim now is to use the exact text of Kale's edition:
;      The Hitopadesha of Narayana by M.R. Kale,
;      6th edition Aug 15, 1967. Motilal Banarsidass.
; Reason: We have previously been using the version from Sanskrit Documents (SD)
;   website  (reference elsewhere: TODO)
; However, there are various differences between Kale's version and this
; version.  These differences make difficult the correlation between
; the Sanskrit text and Kale's English translation.
; Large chunks of the SD text are identical to Kale, but many small and
; some large variances appear.  I've been handling these differences in
; various ways, but am now thinking that it would be better to have the
; text of Kale exactly.
; The line numbers of form #### currently relate to the original SD document.
; Preliminary format of Kale line numbers will be as '###.##'  (page.line)
; and some lines will have form '###.## ####' with both line numbers.
; Kale's comments at the bottom of pages are NOT included currently.
; ------------------------------------------------------------------
; hitokale_slp1_v1.txt  12/25/2018
; This replaces the xxxxF: or xxxxA: line numbering of original hitopadesha-slp1.txt
; Instead, the line numbering PPP.LLF: (or PPP.LLF:) is used.
; The PPP is Kale page number, and is believed to agree with the page number of the Kale text.
; The line number (LL) is less accurately related to the lines of a page of Kale text.
; The difference is believed to be almost entirely within the 'prose' (non-verse) sections.
; Also, the verse text should almost entirely correspond to the Kale text.
; In particular, the verse numbering should agree;
; and the number of lines per verse should agree  (most verses take 2 lines, and the
; second line has the verse number at the end (form .. VVV .. ; sometimes the space between
; V and ending '..' is missing).
; PA :  sandhi analyzed form of marma-prakASikA
; ° : marker for undisplayed text.
; ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
; in anuzwup,  
; akzara (syllable) 5 is light in all 4 padas
; akzara 6 is heavy in all 4 padas
; akzara 7 is light in  padas 1 and 3, but heavy in padas 2 and 4
; https://www.learnsanskrit.org/tools/sanscript/
; NOTE: śloka means anuṣṭup śloka 
; श्लोके षष्ठं गुरु ज्ञेयं सर्वत्र लघु पञ्चमम्।
; द्विचतुष्पादयोर्ह्रस्वं सप्तमं दीर्घमन्ययोः॥
; śloke ṣaṣṭhaṃ guru jñeyaṃ sarvatra laghu pañcamam।
; dvicatuṣpādayorhrasvaṃ saptamaṃ dīrghamanyayoḥ॥
;  or ? dvicatuḥpādayorhrasvaṃ
; ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

;
001.01F: .. hitopadeśaḥ ..
001.01A: .. hita-upadeśaḥ ..
; hita good, useful; upadeSa advice
001.01P: hitasya upadeśaḥ: hitopadeśaḥ . hitaścāsau upadeśaśca iti vā . sa eva lakṣaṇayā tatsaṃjñaḥ granthaḥ .
;001.01PA: hitasya upadeSaH: hitopadeSaH . hitaH ca asO upadeSaH ca iti vA . saH eva lakzaRayA tatsaMjYaH granTaH .

001.02F: prastāvikā
001.02A: prastāvikā
; prastu = stu to praise
; prastAva introduction; prastAvikA same sense but not in dictionaries
001.01-02E: Good advice.  Introduction.

001.03F: siddhiḥ sādhye satāmastu prasādāt tasya dhūrjaṭeḥ .
001.03A: siddhiḥ sādhye satām astu prasādāt tasya dhūrjaṭeḥ .
; sidDi success; sADya an object to be accomplished;
; sat good person; prasAda grace (graciousness)
; DUr in comp. for Dur; Dur burden, top; jawi twisted hair (dreadlocks?)
; DUrjawi N. of Rudra-Siva
001.03P: dhūḥ bhārabhūtā jaṭā yasya asau dhūrjaṭiḥ . tasya dhūrjaṭeḥ prasādāt satāṃ sādhye abhimataviṣaye siddhiḥ astu .

001.04F: jāhnavīphenalekheva yanmūrdhni śaśinaḥ kalā .. 1..
001.04A: jāhnavī-phena-lekhā iva yad-mūrdhni śaśinaḥ kalā .. 1..
; jahnu ; jAhnavI daughter of jahnu (= gaNgA) ; Pena foam; leKa scratch, drawing
; SaSin containing a hare (= moon);
; kalA a small part, a digit or 1/16 of moon's diameter
001.04P: jāhnavī-phena-lekheva -- jahnoḥ apatyaṃ strī jāhnavī tasyā phenasya lekhā .
;001.04PA: jAhnavIPenaleKA iva -- jahnoH apatyam strI jAhnavI tasyAH Penasya leKA .
001.04P: yanmūrdhni -- yasya mūrdhā yanmūrdhā tasmin .

001.03-04E: May success attend the good in their undertakings (in the object they wish to accomplish) by the favour of that Dhurjati, on whose head there is a digit of the moon looking like a streak of the foam of the Ganges.

001.05F: śruto hitopadeśo'yaṃ pāṭavaṃ saṃskṛtoktiṣu .
001.05A: śrutaḥ hitopadeśaḥ ayam pāṭavam saṃskṛta-uktiṣu .
; Sruta heard, studied; pAwava sharpness, cleverness
; saMskft used as name of language by daRqin in daSakumAracarita (800 CE).
001.05P: śrutaḥ samyagadhītaḥ ityarthaḥ .
;001.05PA: SrutaH samyak aDItaH iti arTaH .
001.05P: pāṭavaṃ -- paṭoḥ bhāvaḥ .

001.06F: vācāṃ sarvatra vaicitryaṃ nītividyāṃ dadāti ca .. 2..
001.06A: vācām sarvatra vaicitryam nītividyām dadāti ca .. 2..
; vEcitrya variety (citra = vicitra = various, diverse)
; nIti wise conduct, political science.
001.06P: vaicitryam -- vicitrasya bhāvaḥ .
001.06P: nītividyām -- nītiśāstrajñānam .

001.05-06E: This Hitopadesa (the work inculcating salutary instruction) when studied (lit., carefully attended to) gives (the student) proficiency in elegant speeches, a variety of expression in every department and a knowledge of the conduct of human affairs.
;
; 05-16-2022
;
001.07F: ajarāmaravat prājño vidyāmarthaṃ ca cintayet .
001.07A: ajara-amara-vat prājñaḥ vidyām artham ca cintayet .
; a-jara ageless; amara immortal; prAjYa wise man
; vidyA knowledge; arTa wealth
001.07P: ajarāmaravat -- jarayā niṣkrāntaḥ ajaraḥ , nāsti jarā yasya iti vā . na mriyate asau amaraḥ ca ajarāmaraḥ tena tulyam .

001.08F: gṛhīta iva keśeṣu mṛtyunā dharmamācaret .. 3..
001.08A: gṛhītaḥ iva keśeṣu mṛtyunā dharmam ācaret .. 3..
; Darma good works, duties; Acar to practice

002.07-08E: A wise man should think of (acquiring) knowledge and money as though he were not subject to old age or death: but he should perform his religious duties as if Death had seized him by the hair.

001.09F: sarvadravyeṣu vidyaiva dravyamāhuranuttamam .
001.09A: sarvadravyeṣu vidyā eva dravyam āhuḥ an-uttamam .
; dravya A thing, a possession, wealth;
; anuttama unsurpassed (bahuvrihi)
001.09P: anuttamam -- nāsti uttamam yasmāt .

001.10F: ahāryatvādanarghyatvādakṣayatvācca sarvadā .. 4..
001.10A: a-hārya-tvāt an-arghya-tvāt a-kṣaya-tvāt ca sarvadā .. 4..
; hArya to be taken away; a-hArya-tva (non-stealable-ness - cannot be stolen);
; arGya price; an-arGya-tva pricelessness; sarvadA always
; a-kzaya-tva non-decaying-ness
001.10P: ahāryatvāt -- hartuṃ yogyaṃ śakyaṃ vā na bhavatīti ahāryaṃ tasya bhāvaḥ ahāryatvam . evam anarghyatvādi .

001.09-10E: Learning, of all things, (the wise) declare to be without a superior (the best of them all ), because of its incapability of being taken away, or valued or exhausted.

; Muller has saMgamayati. 
001.11F: saṃyojayati vidyaiva nīcagāpi naraṃ sarit .
001.11A: saṃyojayati vidyā eva nīcagā api naram sarit .
; saMyuj to join; nIca ni (down) +aYc; nIca-ga going low; sarit river
; implicit nIcagam
001.11P: vidyā eva nīcagāpi [satī] naraṃ durdharṣaṃ nṛpaṃ saṃyojayati nīcagāpi sarit durdharṣaṃ samudramiva .
;
;
; Muller uses 'durDarzaM', which makes more sense; this text so changed.
; Kale also 'durDarzaM'
001.12F: samudramiva durdharṣaṃ nṛpaṃ bhāgyamataḥ param .. 5..
001.12A: samudram iva durdharṣam nṛpam bhāgyam ataḥ param .. 5..
; samudra ocean; Dfz to be bold, to assail; dur-Darza inaccessible
; BAgya good fortune; ataH thence; para highest.
001.12P: durdarṣamiti pāṭhaḥ . ataḥ nṛpātsamudrācca paraṃ mahat bhāgyaṃ ataḥparaṃ narasya bhāgyamiti vā .

001.11-12E: Learning, although possessed by a low man, introduces him to the king who is (ordinarily) inapproachable, just as a river, although flowing through a low region, takes one to the inaccessible sea : (sources) from which floweth great fortune (or, the future rests with fortune).

; 05-17-2022

001.13F: vidyā dadāti vinayaṃ vinayādyāti pātratām .
001.13A: vidyā dadāti vinayam vinayāt yāti pātra-tām .
; vinaya modesty; pAtra vessel, capability; pAtra-tA worthiness (competence), eligibility
001.13P: vidyeti -- atra kāraṇamālālaṃkāraḥ .
001.13P+: tallakṣaṇaṃ yathā -- yathottaraṃ cetpūrvasya pūrvasyārthasya hetutā . tadā kāraṇamālā syāt. kā . pra . (sāhi . da . 10.76)
; MW kAraRa-mAlA = 'a series or chain of causes' ref. sAhitya-dArpaRa

001.14F: pātratvāddhanamāpnoti dhanāddharmaṃ tataḥ sukham .. 6..
001.14A: pātratvāt dhanam āpnoti dhanāt dharmam tataḥ sukham .. 6..
; Darma religious merit;

001.13-14E: Learning endows one with modesty ; from (having) modesty one passes on to (gets) worthiness ; being worthy one obtains riches ; from riches religious merit and from that happiness.

001.15F: vidyā śastrasya śāstrasya dve vidye pratipattaye .
001.15A: vidyā śastrasya śāstrasya dve vidye pratipattaye .
; Sastra weapon; SAstra scripture (?)
; pattaye case 4s; prati-patti fame (ap90), action (?) 'conduce to glory'?
001.15P: śastrasya vidyā , śāstrasya vidyā , ete dve vidye pratipattaye kīrtaye bhavataḥ .

001.16F: ādyā hāsyāya vṛddhatve dvitīyādriyate sadā .. 7..
; Kale typo: ditIyA -> dvitIyA
001.16A: ādyā hāsyāya vṛddhatve dvitīyā ā-driyate sadā .. 7..
; AdyA Adi (f. 1s) first; dvitIya 2nd; A-df pres. pass. 3s to respect

001.15-16E: The knowledge of arms and that of the Sastras - these two lores conduce to glory: but the former exposes one to ridicule in old age, while the latter is ever respected.

001.17F: yannave bhājane lagnaḥ saṃskāro nānyathā bhavet .
001.17A: yad nave bhājane lagnaḥ saṃskāraḥ na anyathā bhavet .
; yad as; nava new; BAjana vessel, pot; lagna attached (lag to adhere)
; saMskAra impression (put together); anyaTA otherwise;
001.17P: yathā nave bhājane āmabhājane ityarthaḥ .
; Ama raw, unbaked
; pracyAvayitum, pramArzwum ? inf. of what?  causal infinitives of pracyu
001.17P+: lagnaḥ saṃskāraḥ anyathā na bhavet svasthānātpracyāvayituṃ pramārṣṭuṃ vā na śakyate
001.18F: kathācchalena bālānāṃ nītistadiha kathyate .. 8..
001.18A: kathācchalena bālānām nītiḥ tad iha kathyate .. 8..
; kaTA-Cala story-guise; nIti science of conduct; tad so
001.18P: tathā bālā api nītimadhyāpitāścetsā teṣāṃ cetasi dṛḍhaṃ padaṃ kuryāditi hetoḥ sā kathāmiṣeṇa bālānāmiha kathyate  .
;001.18PA: taTA bAlAH api nItim aDyApitAH cet sA tezAm cetasi dfQam padam kuryAt iti hetoH sA kaTAmizeRa bAlAnAm iha kaTyate .

001.17-18E: As an impression made upon a raw (earthen or so) pot can undergo no change afterwards -- so (following the same principle) in this work the science of conduct (or policy) is taught to youths under the guise of stories.
;
; 05-18-2022

002.01F: mitralābhaḥ suhṛdbhedo vigrahaḥ saṃdhireva ca .
002.01A: mitra-lābhaḥ suhṛdbhedaḥ vigrahaḥ saṃdhiḥ eva ca .
; mitra-lABa obtaining friend; suhfd-Beda separation (breaking);
; vigraha separation, war; saMDi alliance, peace.

002.02F: pañcatantrāttathānyasmādgranthādākṛṣya likhyate .. 9..
002.02A: pañcatantrāt tathā anyasmāt granthāt ākṛṣya likhyate .. 9..
; granTa literary production; Akfz to extract (kfz to drag, plough)
; taTA similarly
002.01-02E:   [The subjects of] "The acquisition of friends", "The separation of friends", "Making war" and "Concluding peace" are written upon, extracts being made from Panchatantra and other works.

002.03F: asti bhāgīrathītīre pāṭaliputranāmadheyaṃ nagaram . tatra sarvasvāmiguṇopetaḥ sudarśano
002.03A: asti bhāgīrathī-tīre pāṭali-putra-nāmadheyam nagaram . tatra sarva-(svāmi-guṇa)-upetaḥ sudarśanaḥ
; BagIraTa 'have a glorious chariot' (vAlmiki rAmayaRa). In India there are several ramayanas!
; pAwali (a red flower) is like a son to the place.
; BAgIraTI name of a river, perhaps the Ganges; tIra a shore;
; svAmi ruler, master; guRa attribute; upeta endowed with
; su-darSana (proper name) easily seen, keen sighted
002.03P: sarvasvāmi -- svāminaḥ guṇāḥ svāmiguṇāḥ . sarve ca te svāmiguṇāśca (karma) taiḥ upetaḥ .
002.03P+: (tṛ. ta.) sudarśanaḥ -- śobhanaṃ darśanaṃ yasya (bahu.) .

002.04F: nāma narapatirāsīt . sa bhūpatirekadā kenāpi pāṭhyamānaṃ ślokadvayaṃ śuśrāva --
002.04A: nāma nara-patiḥ āsīt . saḥ bhūpatiḥ ekadā kena api pāṭhyamānam śloka-dvayam śuśrāva --
; nara-pati lord of men, king. BU-pati lord of earth;
; pAWyamAna ca. ppr. ps. paW (Huet) being recited.
; Sloka-dvaya a pair of shlokas (verses)

002.03-04E: On the bank of the Bhagirathi there is a city named Pataliputra. In it there was a king, Sudarshana by name, endowed with all princely qualities. That king once heard a couple of Slokas (stanzas) chanted by some one ; (viz.)

002.05F: anekasaṃśayocchedi parokṣārthasya darśakam .
002.05A: aneka-saṃśaya-ucchedi parokṣa-arthasya darśakam .
; aneka many; saMSaya doubt; ucCedin cutting off.
; darSaka seeing;  para, away and akza ifc. for akzi, eye;
; arTa thing, object;  parokza-arTa imperceptible object
002.05P: anekasaṃ° -- aneke ca te saṃśayāḥ tān ucchettuṃ śīlamasya .
002.05P+: parokṣārthasya -- akṣṇoḥ paraḥ parokṣaḥ tasya .

002.06F: sarvasya locanaṃ śāstraṃ yasya nāstyandha eva saḥ .. 10..
002.06A: sarvasya locanam śāstram yasya na asti andhaḥ eva saḥ .. 10..
; SAstra = Sruti (Veda) + smfti (Darma-SAstra) +  purARa (incl. itihAsa =  rAmayaRa + mahABArata)))
; locana (loc to see) the eye; anDa blind

002.05-06E: He who does not possess (a knowledge of) Sastra, the universal eye, which totally removes various doubts and discusses things hidden from view, is surely blind.
;
; 05-20-2022
;
002.07F: yauvanaṃ dhanasampattiḥ prabhutvamavivekitā .
002.07A: yauvanam dhana-sampattiḥ prabhu-tvam avivekitā .
; yOvana youth; Dana-sampatti wealth attainment;
; praBu-tva king-ness, powerful-ness;
; vic to divide, discriminate; vivekin judicious;
; vivekitA discrimination, a-vivekitA lack of discrimination
002.07P: yauvaneti -- vayorūpavibhūtīnāmekaikaṃ madakāraṇam . iti samānārthaḥ ślokāṃśaḥ raghuvaṃśe (sa. 17. ślo 13.)

; kim -> kimu  (Kale print smudge).
002.08F: ekaikamapyanarthāya kimu yatra catuṣṭayam .. 11..
002.08A: ekaikam api anarthāya kimu yatra catuṣṭayam .. 11..
; kim-u how much more?
; eka-eka one by one; an-arTa dangerous (worthless object, misfortune); yatra where
; catuzwaya group of four
002.07-08E: Youth, abundance of wealth, sovereignty and inconsiderateness are the source of calamity even singly; what then, where all these four are combined !

002.09F: ityākarṇyātmanaḥ putrāṇāmanadhigataśāstrāṇāṃ nityamunmārgagāmināṃ
002.09A: iti ākarṇya ātmanaḥ putrāṇām an-adhigata-śāstrāṇām nityam unmārga-gāmināṃ
; aDigata studied; unmArga wrong-path  (ut = out, cf. ucCinna cut 'out')
002.09P: anadhigata -- anadhigatāni anadhītāni śāstrāṇi yaiḥ .
002.09P+: unmārgagāmināṃ -- udgataḥ mārgaḥ unmārgaḥ tena gantuṃ śīlaṃ yeṣāṃ .

002.10F: śāstrānanuṣṭhānenodvignamanāḥ sa rājā cintayāmāsa .
002.10A: śāstra-an-anuṣṭhānena udvigna-manāḥ saḥ rājā cintayāmāsa .
; anuzWAna practice,; vij to shake, udvigna-manas whose mind was 'shaken' 
002.10P: śāstrānanuṣṭhānena -- śāstrasya ananuṣṭhānaṃ śāstrājñollaṃghanaṃ tena svairavartanena iti yāvat .

002.09-10E: On hearing this, the king, who was distracted at heart, on account of the non-attendance to (the commands of the) Sastras of his sons who had no knowledge of the Sastras and who always followed the wrong path, thought to himself:

002.11F: ko'rthaḥ putreṇa jātena yo na vidvān na dhārmikaḥ .
002.11A: kaḥ arthaḥ putreṇa jātena yaḥ na vidvān na dhārmikaḥ .
; arTa purpose; jAta born; (Why case 3?)
; vidvAn wise (nom. s. m. of vidvas (in Huet declension as 'part'?))
; DArmika righteous

002.12F: kāṇena cakṣuṣā kiṃvā cakṣuḥpīḍaiva kevalam .. 12..
002.12A: kāṇena cakṣuṣā kim vā cakṣuḥ-pīḍā eva kevalam .. 12..
; kARa blind;  cakzus eye; pIqA pain (pIq to squeeze, to hurt)
; kevalam only

002.11-12E: What is the good of (what benefit can accrue from) having a son who is neither learned nor pious (dutiful); (for) what is the use of an eye that is blind? It simply causes occular pain.

002.13F: ajātamṛtamūrkhāṇāṃ varamādyau na cāntimaḥ .
002.13A: ajāta-mṛta-mūrkhāṇām varam ādyau na ca antimaḥ .
; varam better; Adya du. first (two); antima last

002.14F: sakṛdduḥkhakarāvādyāvantimastu pade pade .. 13..
002.14A: sakṛt duḥkha-karau ādyau antimaḥ tu pade pade .. 13..
; sakft at once; 
002.14P: sakṛdekavāram .

002.13-14E: Of sons, not born, (born and) dead and foolish, the first two are to be preferred and not the last: (for) the first two cause pain (but) once ; the last at every step.

002.15F: kiṃ ca . sa jāto yena jātena yāti vaṃśaḥ samunnatim .
002.15A: kim ca . saḥ jātaḥ yena jātena yāti vaṃśaḥ samunnatim .
; vaMSa lineage; sam-ud-nati rising, elevation

002.16F: parivartini saṃsāre mṛtaḥ ko vā na jāyate .. 14..
002.16A: parivartini saṃsāre mṛtaḥ kaḥ vā na jāyate .. 14..
; parivartin ever-recurring, revolving; saMsAra the (secular) world; 
002.15-16E: Moreover . He is (really) born by whose birth the family is exalted. In this revolving world who does not die and is not born again?

002.17F: guṇigaṇagaṇanārambhe na patati kaṭhinī susambhramādyasya .
002.17A: (guṇi-gaṇa)-gaṇana-ārambhe na patati kaṭhinī susambhramāt yasya .
; guRi-gaRa count of virtuous (persons); gaRana counting;
; AramBa beginning; kaWinI little finger (Ap90) ('chalk' in MW)
; susamBramma great hurry
002.17P: guṇigaṇaga° -- guṇāḥ eṣāṃ vidyante iti guṇinaḥ teṣāṃ gaṇaḥ tasya gaṇanā tasyāḥ arambhe
002.17P: kaṭhinī -- kaniṣṭhikā

002.18F: tenāmbā yadi sutinī vada vandhyā kīdṛśī nāma .. 15..
002.18A: tena ambā yadi sutinī vada vandhyā kīdṛśī nāma .. 15..
; ambA mother; sutinI mother (of a son); vanDyA barren (woman) [cf. ap90 baMDya]
; nAma (after an interr.) what then?

017.23-24E: Although friendship be at an end, the qualities (behaviour) of good men suffer no change: even when lotus-stalks are broken, the fibres remain sticking (to them) yet.

017.30-33E: Not a bath with very cool water, not a necklace of pearls, not (even) sandal-wood-pigment applied to each and every limb, delights a man, oppressed with heat, so much, as the words of the good, uttered with affection, advanced with wise arguments (or full of wise thoughts) and comparable to (fascinating like) the charm of attraction, have power over (are able to gratify) the mind of the virtuous.

018.01-02E: Again.  Divulging a secret, begging, hard-heartedness, fickleness of mind, anger, faithlessness and gambling -- these are the faults in a friend.

018.10-13E: Therefore let your wish be done. Having said so, Hiranyaka formed friendship with the crow, pleased him with choice eatables and entered his hole. The crow, too, repaired to his residence. Thenceforward the two passed their time in making presents of food to each other, in inquiries after good health and in confidential discourses.

023.16-20E: Manthara said . Riches are comparable to (as unsteady as) the dust of the feet; youth flies away with the rapidity of a mountain river; life is as fleeting as a rolling drop of water, and existence as evanascent as foam. (such being the case) he, who, with his judgment deprived, does not perform his religious duties, which unfasten the bolt of the gate of heaven, being overtaken by old age and full of contrition, is burnt by the fire of sorrow.

024.18-19E: There was a hunter, Bhairava by name, residing in the province of Kalyana. He, one day, went to the Vindhya forest in search of a deer. As he passed carrying the deer that he had killed, he saw a boar of a formidable form.

Hence I say -- A hoard should be made every day &c. So also,

025.26-29E: To a high-minded hero, what is his own and what is a foreign country? Whatever country he resorts to, the same he acquires by the might of his arms : whichever forest the lion, armed with his jaws, claws and tail, enters, in the same he quenches his thirst with the blood of the lordly elephants he kills.

026.05-06E: Again. The goddess of wealth goes, of her own Accord, for residence, to him who is endowed with energy, who is prompt in action, who knows the theory and practice of a thing, who is not addicted to vices, and who is brave, grateful and firm in friendship.

032.10F: yo dhruvāṇi parityajya adhruvāṇi niṣevate .

; upari higher; daridrati poor; 3rd pl. of intensive of drA to be poor;

032.35P: kiṃtu laghupadabhāgapi ya ātmānaṃ uccapadasthaṃ manyate sa daridra eva bhavati .
032.35P+: ayaṃ bhāvaḥ -- prabhūtadhano'pi ya ātmānamalpadhanaṃ manyate sodhikadravyaprāptaye yatnaṃ vidadhāti dhanāṭhyaśca bhavati . evaṃ tasya mahimā upacīyate . yaḥ kaścitpunaḥ svalpadhanopi ātmānaṃ vipuladhanaṃ manyate sorthaprāptaye na vyavasati ātmānaṃ tathā darśayituṃ prayatamānaśca ṛṇādinā'kiṃcanatāṃ yāti evaṃ tasya mahimā'pakṣīyate . taduktam kālidāsena 'riktaḥ sarvo bhavati hi laghuḥ pūrṇatā gauravāya .' iti meghadūte . ayamaryaḥ purastāt 'saṃpadā susthitaṃmanyaḥ' ityatra granthakṛtaiva sphuṭakṛtaḥ .

032.34-35E: The greatness of what man that looks lower and lower (i. e. looks upon himself as a very small man or looks at those who are in a humbler station) does not increase? But every one who looks higher and higher (i. e. considers himself as very great, or turns his eyes upon those who are in a higher station) becomes poor.

033.01F: aparaṃ ca . brahmahāpi naraḥ pūjyo yasyāsti vipulaṃ dhanam .

; brahmahan brahmana killing; vipula large;

033.02F: śaśinastulyavaṃśo'pi nirdhanaḥ paribhūyate .. 3..

; SaSin 'containing a hare', the moon; tulya comparable; vaMSa lineage;
; nirDana without wealth; pariBU to defeat, despise;
033.02P: śaśinaḥ vaṃśasya iti śeṣaḥ .  

033.01-02E: Moreover. A man who has abundant wealth, although he be a Brahmana-killer, is respected; while one, although claiming a pedigree as noble as that of the moon, is despised, if without wealth.

; nor anuzwuB meter.

035.01-04E: Once the lion being troubled by thirst went down to the bank of the Yamuna to drink water. 035.01-12E: Friend Damanaka, he is not served at all according to our counsel (or, according to my advice he should not be served at all). If that is the case, what is the good of our observing his doings?  For, we, who have been long despised by this king without any fault of ours, have suffered great anguish.

035.13-14E: See what servants who wish to acquire wealth by means of service have done : those fools have allowed even the independence of their body to be lost!

035.15-16E: Moreover. A wise man will practise penance and be happy with even a portion of those sufferings caused by cold, wind and heat which those who are dependent on others undergo.

035.17-18E: Again. The fruitfulness of life lies in this much, that one lives a life of independence: if those who are in a state of dependence (be said to) live, then, who are the dead ?

035.19-20E: Come, go away, fall down, rise, speak, observe silence -- thus do the wealthy sport with those who are in the grip of the evil spirit of desire.

; doza fault; avijYatA ignorance; sADu jeweller
042.19P: sādhoḥ -- alaṃkāradhāriṇaḥ .
042.19P+: avijñatā -- aviśeṣajñatā avicakṣaṇatā . mūrkhatā iti yāvat .

042.18-19E: Again. A piece of glass is set in a diadem and a jewel placed in a foot-ornament : the blame does not lie with the gem, but it is the want of discretion on the part of the setter.

042.20F: paśya . buddhimānanurakto'yamayaṃ śūra ito bhayam .

; vicAra discrimination; ApUryate (passive A-pF) is filled;

042.20-21E: See. A king who knows how to discriminate between servants -- e.g., this is talented, this is attached to me, this is brave, while there is danger from this -- is surrounded to fullness by servants.

042.24F: anyacca . kiṃ bhaktenāsamarthena kiṃ śaktenāpakāriṇā .

; avajYA to despise;

042.26-27E: For. By being despised by a king the servants turn out dullheaded; then on account of their predominance no wise man approaches him.

043.01-02E: When the kingdom is abandoned by wise men, policy does not become efficacious; and policy having failed the whole world falls a helpless victim to misery.

043.03-04E: Moreover. People always honour the man respected by the king, but he who is despised by the king is slighted by all.

043.05-06E: And further. Wise men should accept what is well said even by a child; is not the light of a lamp acceptable when (or where) the sun is not shining ?

043.13-14E: Why does my lord stand here, as if amazed, without drinking water, although thirsty ? Pingalaka replied -- You have spoken well.  But there is no one trustworthy to whom this secret can be confined. You are such a one. Therefore I will communicate it to you.

043.15-17E: Listen. This forest has now been inhabited by some beast, unheard of before, and must for that reason, be left by us. I am perplexed on this account. Similarly you too have heard that strange loud sound. Great must be the strength of this animal corresponding to his voice.

043.07-21E:  Damanaka replied -- My lord, this is, indeed, a great cause for fear. We too have heard the sound. But he is a bad minister who first counsels the quitting of land and then a fight. At this crisis when it is difficult to know what steps to take, the use of servants alone is to be known. For,

; sAra-tA firmness

043.22-23E: A man knows (tests) on the touch-stone of adversity the strength of his relatives, wife and servants, as also of his intellect and mental calibre.

043.24-26E: The lion said -- Friend, a great terror has overtaken me. Damanaka said again (To himself --) How, else, can you talk to me of leaving the pleasures of a kingdom and going to another place. (Aloud)

043.30-35E: Then Damanaka and Karataka, on whom every honour was bestowed by the king, set out having promised to ward off the danger. On the way Karatake said to Damanaka -- Friend, without ascertaining whether the cause of fear is possible to be averted or not, why did you accept this great favour having undertaken the removal of the fear? For unless one has done a service one should not accept a reward from anybody, especially from a king. Observe,

; tejas splendor (tij to be sharp;

044.16A: lūnam dṛṣṭvā kupitaḥ vivarāntar-gatam mūṣikam alabhamānaḥ acintayat --
; lU to cut; vivara-antar hole-inside alaBamAna not gaining
044.13-16E: On the mountain called Arbudasikhara in the northern region lived a lion, Mahavikrama by name. A certain mouse gnawed the tips of his mane as he slept in his mountain-den. Then seeing the points of his mane bitten off he got angry, but not being able to catch the mouse that was in his hole, he meditated --

044.17F: kṣudraśatrurbhavedyastu vikramānnaiva labhyate .
044.17A: kṣudra-śatruḥ bhavet yaḥ tu vikramāt na eva labhyate .
; kzudra-Satru tiny enemy

044.18F: tamāhantuṃ puraskāryaḥ sadṛśastasya sainikaḥ .. 84..
044.18A: tam āhantum puraskāryaḥ sadṛśaḥ tasya sainikaḥ .. 84..
; sEnika army-man; puras-kArya to be 'done' before, to be appointed;

044.17-18E: When an enemy is insignificant and cannot be overcome by valour, a warrior of his rank should be set forth to kill him.

044.19F: ityālocya tena grāmaṃ gatvā viśvāsaṃ kṛtvā
044.19A: iti ālocya tena grāmam gatvā viśvāsam kṛtvā
; viSvAsa-kf  to 'do' (secure) confidence;

044.20F: dadhikarṇanāmā biḍālo yatnenānīya māṃsāhāraṃ dattvā svakandare
044.20A: dadhikarṇanāmā biḍālaḥ yatnena ānīya māṃsāhāram dattvā svakandare

044.21F: sthāpitaḥ . anantaraṃ tadbhayānmūṣiko'pi bilānna niḥsarati .
044.21A: sthāpitaḥ . anantaram tad-bhayāt mūṣikaḥ api bilāt na niḥsarati .
; bila hole;

044.19-21E: Having thus reflected he went to a village and having brought a cat, named Dadhikarna, with effort, after securing his confidence, placed him in his den, feeding him on flesh. Thereafter the mouse did not come out of his hole through fear of the cat.

044.22F: tenāsau siṃho'kṣatakesaraḥ sukhaṃ svapiti . mūṣikaśabdaṃ yadā yadā śṛṇoti

; kzata wounded (cut)

; saMvfD to satisfy
044.23P: saviśeṣam -- samadhikam .

044.24F: kṣudhāpīḍito bahiḥ saṃcaranbiḍālena prāpto vyāpāditaśca . 
044.24A: kṣudhā-pīḍitaḥ bahiḥ saṃcaran biḍālena prāptaḥ vyāpāditaḥ ca . 
; kzuDA hunger, pIqita oppressed (pIq to squeeze); vyApAdita kipped

044.22-24E: and the lion slept comfortably, his mane not being bitten. Whenever he heard the noise of the mouse he fed the cat with flesh with greater attention. Once the mouse, as he moved out being oppressed with hunger, was caught by the cat and killed.

044.25F: kadācidapi tasya mūṣikasya śabdaṃ vivarānna śuśrāva tadopayogābhāvādbiḍālasya anantaraṃ sa siṃho yadā
; upayogABAvAt = upayoga + aBAvAt:  from absence of use

; upayoga use - aBAva non-existence

044.25-27E: After that the lion did not hear the sound of the mouse at any time and took little care to feed the cat, as he was no longer useful to him. Then that Dadhikarna, wasting away for want of food, died. Hence my observation –- The master should not be made &c.

044.28F: tato damanakakaraṭakau saṃjīvakasamīpaṃ gatau . tatra karaṭakastarutale sāṭopamupaviṣṭaḥ .

; sAwpopam proud (sa + Awopa)

; rakzArTam for sake of protection;

; niyukta appointed; samAjYA causal to order, command

044.28-30E: Then Damanaka and Karataka went to Samjivaka. Of the two Karataka sat under a tree in a dignified manner. Damanaka went forward to Samjivaka and said -- O bull, this general Karataka here, appointed to keep guard over the forest by king Pingalaka, orders you -- Come here at once.

044.31F: no cedasmād araṇyāddūramapasara . anyathā te viruddhaṃ phalaṃ bhaviṣyati .

; viDA to do

044.31-32E:  or, retire to a distance from this wood: else the consequence will be disastrous (adverse) to you. I don't know what our royal master, if angry, will do.

; praRatavat bowing

044.33-34E: Then Samjivaka, ignorant of the ways and manners of the country, advanced with fear and made a profound bow to Karataka. For it is said,

044.35F: matireva balād garīyasī yadabhāve kariṇāmiyaṃ daśā .

044.35-36E: Talent, indeed, is of greater consequence than physical strength, for the lack of which such is the condition of elephants -- this, as it were, the kettle-drum, sounding, proclaims, when beaten by the elephant-driver.

045.03-04E: Kesava returned not a reply to the king of Chedi who was abusing him: the lion roars in response to the thunder of clouds and not to the howlings of jackals.

045.05-07E: Again. A hurricane does not uproot grass, soft and bending humbly all round; but it works havoc upon the lofty trees -- a great man exerts his might only upon the great.

045.08-10E: Now the two, having posted Samjivaka at some distance, repaired into the presence of the lion. Then being received with respectful attention by the king they bowed and sat down. The king asked (Damanaka) -- Did you see the beast ?

045.11F: damanako brūte -- deva .

045.11-14E: Damanaka said in reply -- Yes, Your Highness. But what Your Highness conjectured is quite so (correct). He is certainly huge and seeks an interview with Your Highness. But as his strength is great, Your Highness should receive him, after putting yourself in a defensive position. Let not Your Highness be alarmed at the mere sound. For it is said --

045.15-16E: One should not be alarmed at a mere sound, without knowing its cause. Having found out the cause of the sound, a procuress attained honour.

045.20-23E: There is a city, called Brahmapura, on the mountain Sriparvata. A rumour had got current there that its peak was haunted by a giant, called Ghantakarna. One day, a robber who was running away with a bell, was killed by a tiger and devoured. The bell, fallen from his hands, was picked up by monkeys.

045.24F: te ca vānarāstāṃ ghaṇṭāmanukṣaṇaṃ vādayanti . tato nagarajanaiḥ sa manuṣyaḥ

045.24-25E: Those monkeys used to ring that bell every moment. Now the inhabitants of the city found the man eaten there. And the sound of the bell too was constantly heard.

046.26-29E: Thereupon, saying that Ghantakarna being angry devours men and rings the bell, all people fled from the city. 045.30F: yadi kiyaddhanopakṣayaḥ kriyate tadāhamenaṃ ghaṇṭākarṇaṃ sādhayāmi .

045.32-33E: The procuress drew a magic circle, and after a great display of the worship of Ganesa and others, herself entered the forest taking with her such fruits as the monkeys like and scattered them.

045.34-35E: Thereupon, the monkeys, having left off the bell busied themselves with the fruit. The procuress, too, having taken the bell, returned to the city and became an object of respect to all.

045.36-37E: Therefore I say -- One should not be alarmed at the mere sound &c. Then, Samjivaka was brought and presented (to the lion). Afterwards he lived there in great joy.

046.02F: tasyātithyaṃ kṛtvā samupaveśya piṅgalakastadāhārāya paśuṃ
; veSya is Causal from viS (enter). samupaveSya = ask (cause) to be seated
046.02A: tasya atithyam kṛtvā samupaveśya piṅgalakaḥ tadā āhārāya paśum

046.03F: hantuṃ calitaḥ . atrāntare
046.03A: hantum calitaḥ . atra antare

046.04F: saṃjīvako vadati -- deva adya hatamṛgāṇāṃ māṃsāni kva .
046.04A: saṃjīvakaḥ vadati -- deva adya hatamṛgāṇām māṃsāni kva .

046.01-04E: Now, one day, the lion's brother, Stabdhakarna by name, came there (on a visit). Having received him hospitably and asked him to sit down, Pingalaka set out to hunt a beast to feed him with. Just then Samjivaka asked -- My lord, where is the flesh of the deer killed to-day?

046.05F: rājāha damanakakaraṭakau jānītaḥ .
; jAnItaH 2d pre-9a of jYA (they two know)
046.05A: rājā āha damanakakaraṭakau jānītaḥ .

046.06F: saṃjīvako brūte -- jñāyatāṃ kimasti nāsti vā .
; jYAyatAM ipv-p 3s jYA  (let it be known)
046.06A: saṃjīvakaḥ brūte -- jñāyatām kim asti na asti vā .

046.07F: siṃho vimṛśyāha -- nāstyeva tat .
046.07A: siṃhaḥ vimṛśya āha -- na asti eva tat .

046.05-07E: The king said -- Damanaka and Karataka know that. Sanjivaka said -- Let it be known whether or not there is any left. The lion after reflecting said -- No, there is nothing left.

046.08F: saṃjīvako brūte -- kathametāvan māṃsaṃ tābhyāṃ khāditam .
046.08A: saṃjīvakaḥ brūte -- katham etāvat māṃsam tābhyām khāditam .

046.09F: rājāha -- khāditaṃ vyayitamavadhīritaṃ ca . pratyahameṣa kramaḥ .
046.09A: rājā āha -- khāditam vyayitam avadhīritam ca . pratyaham eṣaḥ kramaḥ .
046.09P: vyayitam -- anyebhyo dattam .
046.09P+: avadhīritam -- anavekṣaṇena apadhvastam .

046.08-09E: Samjivaka asked -- How could they eat so much flesh? The king replied -- It was eaten, used someway or wasted. This is the daily course.

046.10F: saṃjīvako brūte -- kathaṃ śrīmaddevapādānāṃ agocareṇaiva kriyate .
046.10A: saṃjīvakaḥ brūte -- katham śrīmaddevapādānām agocareṇa eva kriyate .
046.10P: agocareṇa -- anivedya . anujñāmalabdhvā iti yāvat .

046.11F: rājāha -- madīyāgocareṇaiva kriyate .
; madIyAgocara = madIya+agocara ('not in my cow field' = without my knowledge)
046.11A: rājā āha -- madīyāgocareṇa eva kriyate .

046.12F: atha saṃjīvako brūte -- naitaducitam . tathā coktam .
046.12A: atha saṃjīvakaḥ brūte -- na etad ucitam . tathā ca uktam .

046.11-12E:   Samjivaka observed -- How is this done without the knowledge of Your Highness ? The king replied -- It is done quite without my knowledge. Samjivaka remarked -- This is not proper. For it is said --

046.13F: nānivedya prakurvīta bhartuḥ kiṃcidapi svayam .
; prakurvIta = opt 3s of pra-kf
046.13A: na anivedya prakurvīta bhartuḥ kim cid api svayam .

046.14F: kāryamāpatpratīkārādanyatra jagatīpateḥ .. 89..
046.14A: kāryam āpatpratīkārāt anyatra jagatīpateḥ .. 89..
046.14P: āpatpratīkāraṃ vipadāṃ nivāraṇaṃ vihāya anyatra .

046.13-14E: One should not do any business on one's own responsibility without informing the master of it, except it be to ward off a calamity befalling the king.

046.15F: anyacca . kamaṇḍalūpamo'mātyastanutyāgo bahugrahaḥ .
; kamaRqalUpamaH = kamaRqalu + upamaH  (like a gourd).
046.15A: anyat ca . kamaṇḍalūpamaḥ amātyaḥ tanutyāgaḥ bahugrahaḥ .
046.15P: kamaṇḍalūpamaḥ -- kamaṇḍaluḥ upamā yasya . kamaṇḍaluryathā bahūdakamantargṛhṇāti alpaṃ ca bahiryacchatyetraṃ koṣavyavasthāyāmamātyaḥ syādityarthaḥ .

046.16F: nṛpate kiṃkṣaṇo mūrkho daridraḥ kiṃvarāṭakaḥ .. 90..
046.16A: nṛpate kim kṣaṇaḥ mūrkhaḥ daridraḥ kim varāṭakaḥ .. 90..
046.16P: kiṃkṣaṇa -- kṣaṇasya kiṃ mahattvamiti vadatīti kiṃkṣaṇaḥ . yaḥ kṣaṇasyāpi bahumūlyatāṃ na jānāti sa vṛthākālakṣepāt ajña eva tiṣṭhati iti bhāvaḥ .
046.16P+: evaṃ kiṃvarāṭakaḥ . yaḥ varāṭakasyāpi bahumūlyatāṃ na jānāti sa dravyāpavyayādakiṃcanatāmeti .

046.15-16E: Moreover. A minister is like a gourd that gives out little and takes in much. A man who talks lightly* [* i. e., does not care for them and so wastes them,] of a moment remains a fool, O king, while one who talks lightly of a cowri remains a pauper.

046.17F: sa hyamātyaḥ sadā śreyānkākinīṃ yaḥ pravardhayet .
046.17A: saḥ hi amātyaḥ sadā śreyān kākinīm yaḥ pravardhayet .
046.17P: kākinī -- varāṭakānāṃ viṃśatiḥ . varāṭakānāṃ daśakadvayaṃ yatsā kākinī tāśca paṇaścatasraḥ . iti līlāvatī .

046.18F: koṣaḥ koṣavataḥ prāṇāḥ prāṇāḥ prāṇā na bhūpateḥ .. 91..
; koza == koSa = treasury
046.18A: koṣaḥ koṣavataḥ prāṇāḥ prāṇāḥ prāṇāḥ na bhūpateḥ .. 91..
046.18P: koṣavataḥ bhūpateḥ koṣaḥ eva prāṇāḥ , prāṇāḥ na prāṇāḥ .
046.18P+: 'prāṇopānaḥ samānaścodānavyānau ca vāyavaḥ '. iti pañca prāṇāḥ . ata eva ayaṃ śabdaḥ nityaṃ bahuvacanaḥ . eṣāṃ sthānāni -- 'hṛdi prāṇo gude'pānaḥ samāno nābhisaṃsthitaḥ . udānaḥ kaṇṭhadeśastho vyānaḥ sarvaśarīragaḥ .'

046.17-18E: That minister is the best (for a king) who every day adds (at least) a kakini (to the treasury); for the treasury is the (real) life of a king, and not his own life so.

046.19F: kiṃ cānyairna kulācāraiḥ sevyatāmeti pūruṣaḥ .
046.19A: kim ca anyaiḥ na kulācāraiḥ sevyatām eti pūruṣaḥ .
046.19P: anyaiḥ -- anyaiḥ dhanavyatiriktaiḥ .
046.19P+: kulācāraiḥ kuladharmaiḥ puruṣaḥ sevyatāṃ naiti . naraḥ dhanaireva sevyate ityarthaḥ .

046.20F: dhanahīnaḥ svapatnyāpi tyajyate kiṃ punaḥ paraiḥ .. 92..
046.20A: dhanahīnaḥ svapatnyā api tyajyate kim punaḥ paraiḥ .. 92..

046.19-20E: Again, a man does not attain a position of being served by reason of other family-observances (such as polite conduct &c. other than the possession of wealth); a man without wealth is abandoned even by his wife; how much more then by others ?

046.21F: etacca rājñe pradhānaṃ dūṣaṇam .
046.21A: etad ca rājñe pradhānam dūṣaṇam .

046.21-21E: And this is the cardinal defect in the administration of a state.
; END HERE 07/09/2021
046.22F: ativyayo'napekṣā ca tathārjanamadharmataḥ .
046.22A: ativyayaḥ anapekṣā ca tathā arjanam adharmataḥ .
046.22P: anapekṣā -- rājakāryāṇāmanavekṣaṇam .

046.23F: moṣaṇaṃ dūrasaṃsthānaṃ koṣavyasanamucyate .. 93..
046.23A: moṣaṇam dūrasaṃsthānam koṣavyasanam ucyate .. 93..
; koza = koSa (in MW). cask, here treasury
046.23P: moṣaṇam -- apahāraḥ .
046.23P+: dūrasaṃsthānaṃ -- dūre sthitiḥ nṛpasya svarājyādvā śāsanīyasaṃsthānāṃ vā .

046.22-23E: Over-expenditure, want of supervision, as also raising money by unfair means, plundering and distant situation -- these are the evils of the treasury.

046.24F: yataḥ . kṣipramāyamanālocya vyayamānaḥ svavāñchayā .
046.24A: yataḥ . kṣipram āyam anālocya vyayamānaḥ svavāñchayā .
046.24P: kṣipraṃ vyayamānaḥ -- kṣipraṃ śīghraṃ avicāritaṃ dhanavyayaṃ kurvan .

046.25F: parikṣīyata evāsau dhanī vaiśravaṇopamaḥ .. 94..
046.25A: parikṣīyate eva asau dhanī vaiśravaṇopamaḥ .. 94..
046.25P: parikṣīyate ityatra śramaṇāyate iti kvacitpāṭhaḥ . śramaṇaḥ bhikṣukaḥ tadvadācarati daridraḥ bhavati iti tasyārthaḥ .
046.25P+: vaiśravaṇopamaḥ kuberatulyaḥ .

046.24-25E: For. A man of wealth, who spends his money at his will recklessly without looking to his income, is reduced to poverty although as rich as Kubera.

047.01F: stabdhakarṇo brūte -- śṛṇu bhrātaḥ cirāśritāvetau
; cirASrita = cira+ASrita (long-time servants)
047.01A: stabdhakarṇaḥ brūte -- śṛṇu bhrātaḥ cirāśritau etau

047.02F: damanakakaraṭakau saṃdhivigrahakāryādhikāriṇau ca kadācidarthādhikāre na
; saMDivigrahakAryADikAriRO = saMDi+vigraha+(kAryADikArin)
047.02A: damanakakaraṭakau saṃdhivigrahakāryādhikāriṇau ca kadā cid arthādhikāre na
047.02P: arthādhikāre koṣādhyakṣatāyām .

047.03F: niyoktavyau . aparaṃ ca niyogaprastāveyātkecinmayā śrutaṃ tat kathyate .
; niyogaprastAveyAt? niyoga+prastAva +? iyAt   OR  (Since Ave at end of line)
; niyogaprastAveyAtkecinmayA =? niyogaprastAve yAt ke cid mayA  (
;  yAt = inasmuch as.  Why 'ke' = f1d of kim ?
;   ke also 7s of 'ka' maybe can be 7s m. agreeing with prastAve
047.03A: niyoktavyau . aparam ca niyogaprastāveyāt ke cid  mayā śrutam tat kathyate .

047.01-03E: Stabdhakarna observed--Listen, brother. These two, Damanaka and Karataka, your servants of long standing, who are the ministers of war and peace, must not at all be appointed to supervise the treasury. I will also tell you what little I have heard on the subject of making appointments.

047.04F: brāhmaṇaḥ kṣatriyo bandhurnādhikāre praśasyate .
; praSasyate  pra-SaMs  (passive): proclaim
047.04A: brāhmaṇaḥ kṣatriyaḥ bandhuḥ na adhikāre praśasyate .
047.04P: bandhuḥ -- pitṛvyaputrādiḥ .

047.05F: brāhmaṇaḥ siddhamapyarthaṃ kṛcchreṇāpi na yacchati .. 95..
047.05A: brāhmaṇaḥ siddham api artham kṛcchreṇa api na yacchati .. 95..
047.05P: siddhaṃ -- niṣpannam .
047.05P+: kṛcchreṇa -- kaṣṭena .

047.04-05E: A Brahmana, a Kshatriya and a relative should not preferably be appointed as treasury-officers. A Brahmana does not deliver up even under pressure the money though realized.

047.06F: niyuktaḥ kṣatriyo dravye khaḍgaṃ darśayate dhruvam .
047.06A: niyuktaḥ kṣatriyaḥ dravye khaḍgam darśayate dhruvam .
047.06P: khaḍgaṃ darśayate -- ugratāṃ pradarśayati . yuddhāyāpi niścitamatiḥ sahasā dravyaṃ na dadāti ityarthaḥ .

047.07F: sarvasvaṃ grasate bandhurākramya jñātibhāvataḥ .. 96..
; jYAtiBAvataH = jYAti+BAvatas  : in consequence of kinship
; Akramya : having seized
047.07A: sarvasvam grasate bandhuḥ ākramya jñātibhāvataḥ .. 96..
047.07P: bandhuḥ jñātibhāvataḥ ekakulajatvādātmanopi sarvasminsvāmyaṃ mānyamānaḥ iti bhāvaḥ .

047.06-07E: A Kshatriya having charge of money-matters is sure to show his sword (defy his master); while a relative, on the strength (by virtue) of his kinship, swallows the whole thing, having seized it.

047.08F: aparādhe'pi niḥśaṅko niyogī cirasevakaḥ .
047.08A: aparādhe api niḥśaṅkaḥ niyogī cirasevakaḥ .
047.08P: niḥśaṅkaḥ -- ciraparicitatvāditi bhāvaḥ .

047.09F: sa svāminamavajñāya carecca niravagrahaḥ .. 97..
047.09A: saḥ svāminam avajñāya caret ca niravagrahaḥ .. 97..
047.09P: niravagrahaḥ -- niraṅkuśaḥ nirargalaḥ . svacchandānuvartī iti yāvat .

047.08-09E: An officer who has been a servant of long standing is fearless even when he has committed a fault; and having despised his master will act freely (lit. without any restraint).
; END 07/15/2021
047.10F: upakartādhikārasthaḥ svāparādhaṃ na manyate .
047.10A: upakartādhikārasthaḥ svāparādham na manyate .

047.11F: upakāraṃ dhvajīkṛtya sarvameva vilumpati .. 98..
047.11A: upakāram dhvajīkṛtya sarvam eva vilumpati .. 98..
047.11P: dhvajīkṛtya puraskṛtya .
047.11P+: vilumpati -- grasate, apaharati .

047.10-11E: A benefactor (one who has done a service) when appointed to an office is regardless of his own offence and putting forward his obligation will appropriate the whole thing.

047.12F: sapāṃśukrīḍito'mātyaḥ svayaṃ rājāyate yataḥ .
; rAjAyate : Nom. verb rAjAya : to act like a king
; sapAMSukrIqitaH 'play-friend from childhood' (Kale)
; pAMSu: sand
047.12A: sapāṃśukrīḍitaḥ amātyaḥ svayam rājāyate yataḥ .
047.12P: sapāṃśukrīḍitaḥ samānāyāṃ pāṃśau kṛtakrīḍaḥ bālyādeva paricita ityarthaḥ . upāṃśukrīḍitaḥ iti pāṭhe rahasi krīḍāsahāyaḥ . vayasyabhāvāpanna ityarthaḥ .

047.13F: avajñā kriyate tena sadā paricayād dhruvam .. 99..
047.13A: avajñā kriyate tena sadā paricayāt dhruvam .. 99..

047.12-13E: Since a play-friend from childhood, if appointed a minister, himself acts as a king, he is sure always to despise (his master) on account of his familiarity.

047.14F: antarduṣṭaḥ kṣamāyuktaḥ sarvānarthakaraḥ kila .
; sarvAnarTakaraH = sarva + anarTa+karaH   (doing all worthless )
047.14A: antarduṣṭaḥ kṣamāyuktaḥ sarvānarthakaraḥ kila .
047.14P: antarduṣṭaḥ abhyantare pāpāśayaḥ durbuddhiḥ .
047.14P+: kṣamāyuktaḥ -- bahiḥ kṣamāśīlaḥ .
047.14P++: kila prasiddhau . etādṛśaḥ amātyaḥ tyājyaḥ iti śeṣaḥ .

047.15F: śakuniḥ śakaṭāraśca dṛṣṭāntāvatra bhūpate .. 100..
; dfzwAntAvatra -> dfzwAntO atra
047.15A: śakuniḥ śakaṭāraḥ ca dṛṣṭāntau atra bhūpate .. 100..
047.15P: śakuniḥ -- saubalaḥ duryodhanasya mātulaḥ .
047.15P+: śakaṭāraḥ -- nandarājasacivaḥ .

047.14-15E: He who is perverse in the mind but outwardly forbearing, verily brings on ruin of every kind: Sakuni and Sakatara, O king, will serve as instances of this.

047.16F: sadāyatyāmasādhyaḥ syātsamṛddhaḥ sarva eva hi .
; sadAyatyAmasADyaH = sadA AyatyAm asADyaH
047.16A: sadāyatyāmasādhyaḥ syāt samṛddhaḥ sarve eva hi .
047.16P: āyatyām -- uttarakāle .
047.16P+: asādhyaḥ anivāryaprasaraḥ .

047.17F: siddhānāmayamādeśaḥ ṛddhiścittavikāriṇī .. 101..
047.17A: siddhānām ayam ādeśaḥ ṛddhiḥ cittavikāriṇī .. 101..
047.17P: ṛddhiḥ -- dhanasaṃpattiḥ .

047.16-17E: All ministers when grown great are incorrigible in the end. It is a saying of the Siddhas (sages, perfect seers) that abundance perverts the mind.

047.18F: prāptārthāgrahaṇaṃ dravyaparīvarto'nurodhanam .
047.18A: prāptārthāgrahaṇam dravyaparīvartaḥ anurodhanam .
047.18P: prāptārthāgrahaṇam -- prāptasya upasthitasya arthasya rājadravyasya agrahaṇaṃ anādānam . prāptārthagrahaṇamitipāṭhe utkocagrahaṇamityarthaḥ .
047.18P+: dravyaparīvartaḥ -- rājadravyavinimayaḥ .
047.18P++: anurodhanam -- svajanānāmanuvartanaṃ iṣṭārthasaṃpādanamiti yāvat . rājacchandānuvartanaṃ vā .

047.19F: upekṣā buddhihīnatvaṃ bhogo'mātyasya dūṣaṇam .. 102..
047.19A: upekṣā buddhihīnatvam bhogaḥ amātyasya dūṣaṇam .. 102..
047.19P: upekṣā audāsyam .
047.19P+: bhogaḥ -- viṣayabhoge abhiniveśaḥ . nṛpadravyasyopabhogo vā .

047.18-19E: Not accepting the money coming to hand, misappropriation of money, easy compliance, neglect, want of judgment, absence of perception (taking a right view of things), and enjoyment (habit of luxury)--these are the faults in a minister.

047.20F: niyogyarthagrahopāyo rājñāṃ nityaparīkṣaṇam .
047.20A: niyogyarthagrahopāyaḥ rājñām nityaparīkṣaṇam .
047.20P: niyogyartha -- niyogināṃ kāryādhikṛtānāmarthasya anyāyenopārjitadravyasya grahopāyaḥ grahaṇopāyacintanam . tathā ca manuḥ -- 'ye kāryikebhyo'rthameva gṛhṇīyuḥ pāpacetasaḥ . teṣāṃ sarvasvamādāya rājā kuryātpravāsanam .' iti .
047.20P+: nityaparīkṣaṇam -- niyoginaḥ apramattāḥ svaṃ svaṃ niyogamanutiṣṭhantīti vā neti parīkṣaṇam .

047.21F: pratipattipradānaṃ ca tathā karmaviparyayaḥ .. 103..
047.21A: pratipattipradānam ca tathā karmaviparyayaḥ .. 103..
047.21P: pratipattipradānam -- ye ātmanaḥ kāryaṃ sādu nirvāhayanti tebhya unnatapadadānam .
047.21P+: karmaviparyayaḥ -- niyogaparivartanam . rājñāṃ ucitaṃ karma iti śeṣaḥ .
047.20-21E: Finding out means to seize the money (illegally) obtained by an officer, daily supervision (over the officers' work), bestowing honours (according to merit) and change of duties, -- this is the duty of kings.

048.01F: nāpīḍitā vamantyuccairantaḥsāraṃ mahīpateḥ .
048.01A: na āpīḍitāḥ vamanti uccaiḥ antaḥsāram mahīpateḥ .
048.01P: mahīpateḥ niyoginaḥ apīḍitāḥ akleśitāḥ santaḥ uccaiḥ antaḥsāraṃ nigīrṇaṃ mahāntamarthaṃ na vamanti udguranti .

048.02F: duṣṭavraṇā iva prāyo bhavanti hi niyoginaḥ .. 104..
048.02A: duṣṭavraṇāḥ iva prāyaḥ bhavanti hi niyoginaḥ .. 104..
; prAyaH = prAyas (ind.) mostly
048.02P: duṣṭavraṇāḥ tepi apīḍitā amarditāḥ antaḥsāraṃ pūyādikaṃ na niṣkāmayanti .

048.01-02E: Officers, unless hard pressed, will not disgorge the royal money embezzled by them for they are mostly like malignant ulcers (which also do not give out the putrid matter without being pressed).

048.03F: muhurniyoginaḥ bādhyā vasudhārā mahīpate .
048.03A: muhur niyoginaḥ bādhyāḥ vasudhārāḥ mahīpate .
; muhur = at every moment;  sakft = once only
048.03P: vasudhārāḥ -- vasūnāṃ dhārāḥ santi eṣāṃ chadmāpahatamahādhanāḥ niyoginaḥ mahīpateḥ bādhyā mahīpatinā pīḍanīyāḥ . nigīrṇadravyodgiraṇārthamiti śeṣaḥ . bādhyā ityatra rodha iti pāṭhe niyoginaḥ rodhaḥ vasunaḥ dravyasya dhārā pravāha iti yojanīyam .

048.04F: sakṛtkiṃ pīḍitaṃ snānavastraṃ muñcedbahūdakam.. 105..
048.04A: sakṛt kim pīḍitam snānavastram muñcet bahu udakam .. 105..

048.03-04E: A king should fine* [* Or, ought to fine officers who have misappropriated sums of money.] repeatedly (corrupt) officers large sums of money: for does the garment used at the time of bathing yield up (give out) much water when wrung out only once?

048.05F: etatsarvaṃ yathāvasaraṃ jñātvā vyavahartavyam .
048.05A: etat sarvam yathā avasaram jñātvā vyavahartavyam .

048.06F: piṅgalako brūte --
048.06A: piṅgalakaḥ brūte --

048.07F: asti tāvad evam . kiṃtvetau sarvathā na mama vacanakarau .
048.07A: asti tāvat evam . kim tu etau sarvathā na mama vacanakarau .

048.08F: stabdhakarṇo brūte -- etatsarvathānucitaṃ sarvathā . yataḥ .
048.08A: stabdhakarṇaḥ brūte -- etat sarvathā anucitam . yataḥ .

048.05-08E: One should remember all this and act accordingly, as an emergency may arise. Pingalaka said -- It is just so. But these two never obey my order. Stabdhakarna observed –- This is not at all proper. For,

048.09F: ājñābhaṅgakarānrājā na kṣameta sutānapi .
048.09A: ājñābhaṅgakarān rājā na kṣameta sutān api .

048.10A: viśeṣaḥ kaḥ nu rājñaḥ ca rājñaḥ citragatasya ca .. 106..
048.10P: citragatasya -- ālekhye niveśitasya citrapaṭe likhitasya .

048.09-10E: A king should not forgive those who disobey orders, even though they be his sons: for (in that case) what difference can there be between such a king and one drawn in a picture?

048.11F: anyacca . stabdhasya naśyati yaśo viṣamasya maitrī

048.12P: arthaparasya -- dhanārjanaikarasasya , dhanololupasya . sa hi dharmādharmau na gaṇayatīti suprasiddham .

048.13F: vidyāphalaṃ vyasaninaḥ kṛpaṇasya saukhyaṃ
048.13A: vidyāphalam vyasaninaḥ kṛpaṇasya saukhyam

048.14F: rājyaṃ pramattasacivasya narādhipasya .. 107..
048.14A: rājyam pramattasacivasya narādhipasya .. 107..
048.14P: pramattasacivasya -- pramattāḥ svakartavyasyopekṣākāriṇaḥ sacivāḥ yasya .

048.11-14E: Moreover. The fame of one who is inactive comes to an end; so does the friendship of one of unsettled conduct; the family of one who has lost the vigour of his senses; the sense of duty of one intent on acquiring wealth; the fruit of the learning of one who is addicted to vices; the happiness of a miser, and the sovereignty of one whose ministers are careless.

048.15F: viśeṣataśca . taskarebhyo niyuktebhyaḥ śatrubhyo nṛpavallabhāt .
048.15A: viśeṣataḥ ca . taskarebhyaḥ niyuktebhyaḥ śatrubhyaḥ nṛpavallabhāt .
048.15P: niyuktebhyaḥ adhikāribhyaḥ . anyathā te balavatparasvāpaharaṇaṃ kuryuḥ .

048.16F: nṛpatirnijalobhācca prajā rakṣetpiteva hi .. 108..
048.16A: nṛpatiḥ nijalobhāt ca prajāḥ rakṣet pitā iva hi .. 108..

048.15-16E: More especially. A king should, like a father, protect his subjects from robbers, from his officers, from enemies, from his favourites and from his own avarice.

048.17-18E: Brother, let my advice be always acted upon. I too have transacted business. Let this Samjivaka who eats corn be appointed to superintend the treasury.

048.19-20E: That being done, from that time onward, Pingalaka and Samjivaka passed their time in great friendship, having left off all other connexions.

048.21-24E: .  Then Damanaka and Karataka, finding that there was a relaxation in dealing out food even to the servants, consulted mutually. Then Damanaka said to Karataka-Friend, what is to be done? This is our own fault. And it is not proper to lament over an evil of one's own making. For it is said--

048.30-35E: In the city of Kanchanapura lived a king named Viravikrama. As his officer of justice was leading a barber to the place of execution, the latter was held by the skirt of his garment by a certain recluse, Kandarpaketu by name, accompanied by another man, Sadhu (a mendicant), with the words "This barber should not be killed." The king's officers asked why he should not be killed. He said, hear--He repeated--I having touched Svarnarekha &c. They asked--How is this?

049.02-04E: One day as I sat in the pleasure-garden I heard from a sea-faring merchant, that, on the fourteenth day of the month, there was to be seen on the sea, under a desire-granting tree that appeared then - seated upon a sofa variegated with a ring of the rays of gems and decorated with ornaments of all kinds -- a maiden, like the goddess Lakshmi, playing upon a lyre.

049.05-06E: Then I, in company with the sea-merchant, got on board his ship, and sailed for the place. On going there I saw, as described, on a sofa, the damsel, half submerged.

049.07-07E: Then charmed with her beauty I gave a jump after her.

049.08-10E: After that on reaching a golden city, I saw her seated on a couch, in the same manner, in a gold palace, and attended by Vidyadhara women. She too, having seen me from a distance, sent her friend and (through her) addressed me with respect.

049.16-19E: So the Gandharva marriage being concluded I lived there enjoying the sweets of her company. One day she said to me in private -- Lord, you may enjoy everything here according to your wishes; but you should never touch this Vidyadhara female, Svarnarekha by name, painted here.

049.32-36E: After that was done the cowkeeper awoke and said to her -- Why dost thou not go to your gallant now? But as she returned no reply, he saying, How is it that you, in your vanity, do not even give me an answer!, seized a pair of scissors in a rage and cut off her nose. This done, the cowherd again lay down and sank into sleep. Now the cowherd's wife, returning, asked the barber's wife what the news was.

050.01-03E: The procuress replied-- Look here, my face will tell you the news. Thereafter the cowherdess tied herself to the post and stood as before. The procuress, too, took up her nose and having gone home lay there.

050.04F: tataḥ prātarevānena nāpitena kṣurabhāṇḍaṃ yācitā satīyaṃ
050.04A: tataḥ prātaḥ eva anena nāpitena kṣurabhāṇḍam yācitā satī iyam
; iyam = f1s idam

050.05F: kṣuramekaṃ prādāt . tato'samagrabhāṇḍe prāpte samupajātakopo'yaṃ
050.05A: kṣuram ekam prādāt . tataḥ asamagrabhāṇḍe prāpte samupajātakopaḥ ayam

050.06F: nāpitastaṃ kṣuraṃ dūrādeeva gṛhe kṣiptavān . atha kṛtārtanādeyaṃ vināparādhena
050.06A: nāpitaḥ tam kṣuram dūrāt eva gṛhe kṣiptavān . atha kṛtārtanādeyam vinā aparādhena
050.06P: kṛtārtanādā kṛtaḥ ārtanādaḥ karuṇasvanaḥ yayā .

050.07F: me nāsikānena chinnetyuktvā dharmādhikārisamīpamenamānītavatī .
050.07A: me nāsikā anena chinneti uktvā dharmādhikāri samīpam enam ānītavatī .

050.04-07E: Then in the morning when this barber asked her for the razor-case, she gave him one razor only. Thereupon, this barber, going into a passion as the whole case was not handed over to him threw the razor from some distance into the house. Upon this setting up a cry of pain and saying 'Without any provocation he has cut off my nose' she brought him to the officer of justice.

050.08F: sā ca gopī tena gopena punaḥ
050.08A: sā ca gopī tena gopena punaḥ

050.09F: pṛṣṭovāca -- are pāpa ko māṃ mahāsatīṃ virūpayituṃ samarthaḥ .
050.09A: pṛṣṭā uvāca -- are pāpa kaḥ mām mahāsatīm virūpayitum samarthaḥ .

050.10F: mama vyavahāramakalmaṣamaṣṭau lokapālā eva jānanti . yataḥ .
050.10A: mama vyavahāram akalmaṣam aṣṭau lokapālāḥ eva jānanti . yataḥ .
050.10P: akalmaṣam -- niṣpāpam .

050.08-10E: In the meanwhile, the cowherd's wife being again asked by the cowherd exclaimed -- Who, vile wretch, is able to disfigure me who am so very chaste. The eight guardians of the world alone know how free from sin all my actions are. For,

050.11F: ādityacandrāvanilo'nalaśca dyaurbhūmirāpo hṛdayaṃ yamaśca .
050.11A: ādityacandrau anilaḥ analaḥ ca dyauḥ bhūmiḥ āpaḥ hṛdayam yamaḥ ca .
; 
050.12F: ahaśca rātriśca ubhe ca saṃdhye dharmaśca jānāti narasya vṛttam .. 110..
050.12A: ahaḥ ca rātriḥ ca ubhe ca saṃdhye dharmaḥ ca jānāti narasya vṛttam .. 110..
; ahaH = ahar (day)

050.11-12E: The sun and the moon, wind and fire, heaven and earth, water, the heart, Yama, day and night, both the twilights and the deity Dharma-—these know the actions of a man.
; 07/17/2020 END
050.13F: tatohaṃ yadi paramasatī syāṃ nijasvāminaṃ tvāṃ vihāya nānyaṃ manasāpi cintayāmi
050.13A: tataḥ aham yadi paramasatī syām nijasvāminam tvām vihāya na anyam manasā api cintayāmi

050.14F: tadā mama mukhamakṣataṃ bhavatu . paśya manmukham . tato yavadasau gopīṃ dīpaṃ prajvālya
050.14A: tadā mama mukham akṣatam bhavatu . paśya manmukham . tato yavat asau gopīm dīpam prajvālya

050.15F: tanmukhamavalokate tāvadunnasaṃ mukhamavalokya taccaraṇayoḥ patitaḥ -- 
050.15A: tat mukham avalokate tāvat unnasam mukham avalokya tat caraṇayoḥ patitaḥ -- 
; "Danyo'haM yasyedrSI" moved from end of 15 to beginning of 16.

050.13-15E: If then, I am perfectly chaste, and have never even so much as thought of a man other than yourself, let my face be free from its wound. Look at my face. Then as soon as the cow-keeper lighted a lamp, looked at her face and found that it had the nose restored, he fell at her feet saying --

050.16F: dhanyo'haṃ yasyedrśī bhāryā paramasādhvī iti . yoyamāste sādhuretadvṛttāntamapi śṛṇuta . ayaṃ svagṛhānnirgato
050.16A: dhanyaḥ aham yasya idrśī bhāryā paramasādhvī iti . yaḥ ayam āste sādhuḥ etat vṛttāntam api śṛṇuta . ayam svagṛhāt nirgataḥ

050.17F: dvādaśavarṣamalayopakaṇṭhādimāṃ nagarīmanuprāptaḥ . atra ca veśyāgṛhe suptaḥ . 
; dvAdaSavarza-malaya-upakaRWAt : after 12 years from Malaya-vicinity
050.17A: dvādaśavarṣamalayopakaṇṭhāt imām nagarīm anuprāptaḥ . atra ca veśyāgṛhe suptaḥ . 
; move 'tasyAH' from end of 17 to beginning of 18

050.16-17E: Blessed am I whose wife is thus perfectly virtuous. Now attend to the story of the mendicant who is here. He, having left his house, came to this city after twelve years, from the vicinity of mount Malaya. He slept in the house of a courtesan.

050.18F: tasyāḥ kuṭṭanyā gṛhadvāri sthāpitakāṣṭhaghaṭitavetālasya mūrdhani ratnamekamutkṛṣṭamāste . tad
050.18A: tasyāḥ kuṭṭanyāḥ gṛhadvāri sthāpitakāṣṭhaghaṭitavetālasya mūrdhani ratnam ekam utkṛṣṭam āste . tat
050.18P: kāṣṭhaghaṭitavetālasya dārunirmitavetālamūrtyāḥ .

050.19F: dṛṣṭvārthalubdhenānena sādhunā rātrāvutthāya ratnam grahītuṃ yatnaḥ kṛtaḥ . tadā tena vetālena
050.19A: dṛṣṭvā arthalubdhena anena sādhunā rātrau utthāya ratnam grahītum yatnaḥ kṛtaḥ . tadā tena vetālena

050.20F: sūtrasaṃcāritabāhubhyāṃ pīḍitaḥ sannārtanādamayaṃ cakāra . paścādutthāya kuṭṭanyoktam --
050.20A: sūtrasaṃcāritabāhubhyām pīḍitaḥ sannārtanādamayam cakāra . paścāt utthāya kuṭṭanyā uktam --
; sannArta = sat + Arta (sandhi) ?

050.18-20E: At the door of the harlot's house there stood the wooden image of a spirit, on whose head there was a jewel of the best sort. Seeing that, this mendicant, being impelled by avarice, got up in the middle of the night and attempted to take the jewel. Then being pressed by the arms of the spirit which were moved by wires, he uttered a cry of pain. Thereupon the harlot, having got up, said --

050.21F: eva malayopakaṇṭhādāgato'si . tatsarvaratnāni prayacchāsmai . no cedanena na tyaktavyo'si .
050.21A: eva malayopakaṇṭhāt āgataḥ asi . tat sarvaratnāni prayaccha asmai . no cet anena na tyaktavyaḥ asi .

050.22F: itthamevāyaṃ ceṭakaḥ . tato'nena sarvaratnāni samarpitāni . 
050.22A: ittham eva ayam ceṭakaḥ . tataḥ anena sarvaratnāni samarpitāni . 
; aDunA moved from 22 to 23

050.21-22E: Holloa, son, you have come from the neighbourhood of Malaya. Deliver, therefore, all the jewels you have to him, else he will not release you. Such is this wily fellow. Then this merchant gave up all his jewels.

050.23F: adhunā cāyamapi hṛtasarvasvo'smāsu militaḥ . etatsarvaṃ śrutvā rājapuruṣairnyāye dharmādhikārī
050.23A: adhunā ca ayam api hṛtasarvasvaḥ asmāsu militaḥ . etat sarvam śrutvā rājapuruṣaiḥ nyāye dharmādhikārī

050.24F: pravartitaḥ . nāpitavadhūrmuṇḍitā gopī niḥsāritā kuṭṭanī ca daṇḍitā . sādhordhanāni
050.24A: pravartitaḥ . nāpitavadhūḥ muṇḍitā gopī niḥsāritā kuṭṭanī ca daṇḍitā . sādhoḥ dhanāni

050.25F: pradattāni . nāpitaśca gṛhaṃ gataḥ . ato'haṃ bravīmi -- svarṇarekhāmahaṃ spṛṣṭvā ityādi ..
050.25A: pradattāni . nāpitaḥ ca gṛham gataḥ . ataḥ aham bravīmi -- svarṇarekhām aham spṛṣṭvā ityādi ..
; 'ityAdi' left as is.

050.23-25E: And now, he too, being robbed of all his wealth, has joined our party. On hearing all this the king's officers got the judge to do justice. The barber's wife was shaved, the cowherdess expelled the city, the harlot fined and the merchant restored to all his wealth. The barber too went home. Therefore I say- I for having touched Svarnarekha &c.

050.26F: atha svayamkṛto'yaṃ doṣaḥ . atra vilapanaṃ nocitam . (kṣaṇaṃ vimṛśya .) mitra sahasaiva
050.26A: atha svayamkṛtaḥ ayam doṣaḥ . atra vilapanam na ucitam . (kṣaṇam vimṛśya .) mitra sahasā eva

050.27F: yathānayoḥ sauhārdaṃ mayā kāritaṃ tathā mitrabhedo'pi mayā kāryaḥ . yataḥ .
050.27A: yathā anayoḥ sauhārdam mayā kāritam tathā mitrabhedaḥ api mayā kāryaḥ . yataḥ .

050.26-27E: Now this fault is ours, and lamentation is out of place in this case. Having reflected for a moment -- Friend, just as I brought about the friendship of these too, so should I effect the disunion of the two friends also. For,

050.28F: atathyānyapi tathyāni darśayanti hi peśalāḥ .
050.28A: atathyāni api tathyāni darśayanti hi peśalāḥ .
050.28P: peśalāḥ -- caturāḥ .

050.29F: same nimnonnatānīva citrakarmavido janāḥ .. 111..
050.29A: same nimnonnatāni iva citrakarmavidaḥ janāḥ .. 111..
050.29P: nimnonnatāni natonnatabhāgān .
050.29P+: citrakarmavidaḥ ālekhyakuśalāḥ .

050.28-29E: Very clever men represent even untruth as truth (if required), as persons versed in the art of painting represent depressions and prominences on an even surface.

050.30F: aparaṃ ca . utpanneṣvapi kāryeṣu matiryasya na hīyate .
050.30A: aparam ca . utpanneṣu api kāryeṣu matiḥ yasya na hīyate .
050.30P: kāryeṣu gahanakāryeṣu ityarthāt .
050.30P+: hīyate lupyate .

050.31P: durgāṇi saṃkaṭāni .

050.32A: karaṭakaḥ pṛcchati -- katham etat . damanakaḥ kathayati --

050.30-32E: Moreover, he whose intellect does not fail him even under fresh occurrences, surmounts difficulties just as the cowherd's wife got clear of her two lovers. Karataka asked how it was. Damanaka related.

050.34F: asti dvāravatyāṃ puryāṃ kasyacidgopasya vadhūrbandhakī . sā grāmasya daṇḍanāyakena

050.34-35E: The wife of a certain cowherd who lived in Dvaraka was of a bad character. She had an intrigue with the magistrate of the place, as also with his son. For it is said --

051.01F: nāgnistṛpyati kāṣṭhānāṃ nāpagānāṃ mahodadhiḥ .
051.01A: na agniḥ tṛpyati kāṣṭhānām na āpagānām mahodadhiḥ .
051.01P: tṛpyati kāṣṭhānām . tṛtīyārthe ṣaṣṭhī . ma.bhā.u.pa. 40,7; a.pa.38.25.

051.02F: nāntakaḥ sarvabhūtānāṃ na puṃsāṃ vāmalocanā .. 113..
051.02A: na antakaḥ sarvabhūtānām na puṃsām vāmalocanā .. 113..

051.01-02E: Fire is not satisfied with fuel, the ocean with rivers, the god of death with all creatures and a beautiful woman with men.

051.03F: anyacca . na dānena na mānena nārjavena na sevayā .
051.03A: anyat ca . na dānena na mānena na ārjavena na sevayā .
051.03P: mānena mānadānena .
051.03P+: ārjavena ṛjorbhāvaḥ ārjvaṃ tena saralatāprakāśanena .

051.04F: na śastreṇa na śāstreṇa sarvathā viṣamāḥ striyaḥ .. 114..

051.04P: śastreṇa -- śastraprahārabhayenetyarthaḥ .
051.04P+: śāstreṇa -- śāstravākyopadeśena .
051.04P++: striyaḥ vaśīkriyante iti . ata eva tāḥ sarvathā sarvaprakāreṇa viṣamāḥ durārādhyāḥ .

051.03-04E: Moreover, Not by gifts, not by honour, not by simplicity, not by attendance, not with a weapon (fear of punishment) and not with scriptural advice, can women be won over: — they are hard to please in every way.

051.05F: yataḥ . guṇāśrayaṃ kīrtiyutaṃ ca kāntaṃ patiṃ ratijñaṃ sadhanaṃ yuvānam .

051.05P: guṇāśrayam praśaṃsanīyaguṇānāmādhāram .
051.05P+: kāntaṃ kamanīyam .

051.06F: vihāya śīghraṃ vanitā vrajanti naraṃ paraṃ śīlaguṇādihīnam .. 115..
051.06A: vihāya śīghram vanitāḥ vrajanti naram param śīlaguṇādihīnam .. 115..
051.06P: paraṃ naraṃ jāram .

0551.05-06E: For, Having forsaken a husband who is the abode of merits, endowed with fame, amiable, versed in the erotic art, wealthy and youthful, women quickly resort to another man (although) destitute of character, good qualities and the like.

051.07F: aparaṃ ca . na tādṛśīṃ prītimupaiti nārī vicitraśayyāṃ śayitāpi kāmam .
051.07A: aparam ca . na tādṛśīm prītim upaiti nārī vicitraśayyām śayitā api kāmam .
051.07P: prītiṃ -- pramodam .
051.07P+: vicitraśayyāṃ -- ramaṇīyaśayyām .

051.08F: yathā hi dūrvādivikīrṇabhūmau prayāti saukhyaṃ parakāntisaṅgāt .. 118..
051.08A: yathā hi dūrvādivikīrṇabhūmau prayāti saukhyam parakāntisaṅgāt .. 118..
051.08P: dūrvādi -- dūrvāprabhṛtyāvṛtasthāne .

051.07-08E: Moreover, A woman does not derive that pleasure although lying down on a beautiful bed entirely to her satisfaction as she does in the company of a gallant although lying down on the ground covered over with the Durva grass and other things of that sort.

051.09F: atha kadācitsā daṇḍanāyakaputreṇa saha ramamāṇā tiṣṭhati . atha
051.09A: atha kadā cit sā daṇḍanāyakaputreṇa saha ramamāṇā tiṣṭhati . atha

051.10F: daṇḍanāyako'pi gantuṃ tatrāgataḥ . tamāyāntaṃ dṛṣṭvā tatputraṃ

051.11F: kusūle nikṣipya daṇḍanāyakena samaṃ tathaiva krīḍati . anantaraṃ tasyā

051.11P: kusūle dhānyasthāpanapātraviśeṣe .

051.12F: bhartā gopo goṣṭhātsamāgataḥ . tamālokya gopyoktam --

051.09-12E: One day she was sporting with the magistrate's son, when the magistrate too came there to enjoy her company. Seeing him coming, she put his son in a barn and began to amuse herself with him. After that her husband, the cowherd, returned from the cowpen. On spying him the cowherdess said to the magistrate

051.15F: samāgatotra .

051.13-15E: Oh magistrate, you take a stick and quickly go out as if in a rage. He having acted accordingly the cowherd came in and asked his wife what had brought the justice there.

015.16-19E: She replied -- For some reason or other he is angry with his son, who coming here entered our house and was protected by me by being concealed in the barn. His father searching for him did not find him in the house. Hence it is that the magistrate is going in a rage.

051.20-23E: She then took out the son from the barn and showed him. So it is said -- The food of women is twofold, their readiness of wit fourfold, perseverance sixfold and passion eightfold.

051.25-27E: Karataka observed -- Be it so. But how will it be possible to dissolve the great friendship that has grown up between them by the similarity of their dispositions? Damanaka replied -- Let a remedy be applied. For it is said --

051.33-37E: A pair of crows lived in a certain tree. Their youngs were eaten by a cobra who lived in the hollow of the tree. Thereafter, the female crow, when again breeding said to her mate -- My dear, let us abandon this tree. As long as the serpent lives here, our offspring can never live. For,

052.15-19E: Then all the beasts having assembled together made this representation to the lion -- Sovereign of the beasts, why are so many animals slaughtered at a time? If it please Your Highness, we ourselves shall send one beast every day for your food. To this the lion replied -- If you desire it let it be done. Thenceforth he ate one animal that was offered him.

052.29-33E: Go quickly and show the vile wretch to me. Where does the villain live? Then the hare taking the lion with him set out to show him a deep well. 'Please Your Highness, come here and behold him yourself.' With these words he showed him the lion's own reflection in the water of the well. Thereupon he, being swollen with rage, sprang upon him through arrogagance and lost his life. Therefore I say, he who has talent has strength &c

052.34-37E: The female crow said I have heard everything. Now tell me what I am to do. The crow replied -- The prince comes every day and bathes in the adjacent tank. Hold up in your bill a gold necklace, which is taken off from his person at the time of bathing and placed on a stone of the flight of steps, and put it in this hollow.

053.04-05E: A well-meaning man should give his wholesome counsel even unasked, in the case of a calamity, when a man swerves from the right path, or when the time of taking action is passing away.

053.06-07E: Again, The proper sphere of the king is to enjoy pleasures, while that of the minister is to attend to business. A minister who spoils the business of state is to blame in every way.

053.11-14E: Pingalaka asked him graciously -- Now what do you wish to say? Damanaka replied -- My lord, Samjivaka appears to be acting in an unbecoming manner towards Your Highness. To speak clearly, he, having cast reproach on Your Highness' three powers, wishes to gain the sovereignty itself.

053.18-19E: The goddess of royalty stands having placed her feet on a minister when very highly exalted and the king; but she, unable long to bear the burden, being of the nature of a woman, gives up one of the two.

053.20-21E: Moreover, When a king makes one minister the (sole) authority in a kingdom, vanity takes possession of him through delusion, and he alienates himself (from the king) through indolence brought on by vanity.

053.23P: prāṇāntikaṃ druhyati -- prāṇavināśaṃ yāvadaniṣṭācaraṇaṃ karoti .

053.22-23E: When (once) alienated, a desire for independence springs up in his mind; and then led by the desire for independence he (the minister) acts treacherously even to the extent of robbing the king of his life.

053.25A: amātyasya ca duṣṭasya mūlāt uddharaṇam sukham .. 127..
053.25P: duṣṭasya -- kaluṣitamanasaḥ durāśayasya .
053.25P+: sukhaṃ -- sukhakaram .

053.24-25E: Again, Of rice tainted with poison, of a tooth got loose and of a minister turned a traitor, complete eradication leads to happiness.

054.01F: kiṃ ca . yaḥ kuryātsacivāyattāṃ śriyaṃ tadvyasane sati .
054.01A: kim ca . yaḥ kuryāt sacivāyattām śriyam tadvyasane sati .
; Sriyam f. 2s of srI
054.01P: tadvyasane -- tasya sacivasya vyasane sati tasminnāpaddhaste .

054.02F: so'ndhavajjagatīpālaḥ sīdetsaṃcārakairvinā .. 128..
054.02A: saḥ andhavat jagatīpālaḥ sīdet saṃcārakaiḥ vinā .. 128..
; anDavat = anDa+vat = like 'anDa' (blind man)
054.02P: saṃcārakaiḥ upadeśakaiḥ .

054.01-02E: Also, A king, who places his royal fortune under his minister's control, will, in the event of his (minister's) being in calamity, experience trouble like a blind man without guides.

054.03F: sa ca sarvakāryeṣu
054.03A: saḥ ca sarvakāryeṣu

054.04F: svecchātaḥ pravartate . tadatra pramāṇaṃ svāmī . etacca jānāmi .
054.04A: svecchātaḥ pravartate . tat atra pramāṇam svāmī . etat ca jānāmi .
054.04P: atra pramāṇam svāmī -- parastātkāryanirṇaye iti śeṣaḥ . 

054.03-05E: He proceeds in (conducts) all affairs according to his will. Your Highness, therefore, is the authority is to decide as to what is to be done under these circumstances. As for myself ..

054.05F: na so'sti puruṣo loke yo na kāmayate śriyam .
054.05A: na saḥ asti puruṣaḥ loke yaḥ na kāmayate śriyam .

054.06F: parasya yuvatiṃ ramyāṃ sādaraṃ nekṣate'tra kaḥ .. 129..
054.06A: parasya yuvatim ramyām sādaram na īkṣate atra kaḥ .. 129..

054.05-06E: There is not that man in this world who does not covet riches. Who, in this world, does not wistfully look at the youthful and charming wife of another?

054.07F: siṃho vimṛśyāha -- bhadra
054.07A: siṃhaḥ vimṛśya āha -- bhadra

054.08F: yadyapyevaṃ tathāpi saṃjīvakena saha mama mahānsnehaḥ . paśya .
054.08A: yadi api evam tathā api saṃjīvakena saha mama mahān snehaḥ . paśya .

054.07-08E: The lion observed reflecting -- Dear Damanaka, although such is the case, still great is the affection that I have for Samjivaka. Behold!

054.09F: kurvannapi vyalīkāni yaḥ priyaḥ priya eva saḥ .
054.09A: kurvan api vyalīkāni yaḥ priyaḥ priyaḥ eva saḥ .
054.09P: vyalīkāni aparādhān .

054.10F: aśeṣadoṣaduṣṭo'pi kāyaḥ kasya na vallabhaḥ .. 130..

054.10P: duṣṭaḥ dūṣitaḥ .

054.09-10E: Although committing offences, a favourite is a favourite : who does not like the body although affected with all humours?

054.11F: anyacca . apriyāṇyapi kurvāṇo yaḥ priyaḥ priya eva saḥ .
054.11A: anyat ca. apriyāṇi api kurvāṇaḥ yaḥ priyaḥ priyaḥ eva saḥ .

054.12F: dagdhamandirasāre'pi kasya vahnāvanādaraḥ .. 131..

; vahnO 7s m. vahni (who carries) fire
054.12P: anādaraḥ -- anāsthā .

054.11-12E:  Again, He who is dear is so although doing unpleasant things; who has disregard for (has not to do with) fire although it has consumed all the substance in the house?

054.13F: damanako vadati -- deva sa eva doṣaḥ . yataḥ .
054.13A: damanakaḥ vadati -- deva saḥ eva doṣaḥ . yataḥ .

054.14F: yasminnevādhikaṃ cakṣurāropayati pārthivaḥ .
054.14A: yasmin eva adhikam cakṣuḥ āropayati pārthivaḥ .

054.15F: sute'mātye'pyudāsīne sa lakṣmyāśrīyate janaḥ .. 132..
054.15A: sute amātye api udāsīne saḥ lakṣmī āśrīyate janaḥ .. 132..
054.15P: udāsīne -- parakīye , anyasminkasminścit .

054.13-15E: Damanaka replied. My lord, and just therein lies the fault. For, He on whom the king fixes his eye more (than on others) -- be he a son, or a minister, or a stranger -- is resorted to by the goddess of wealth.

054.16F: śṛṇu deva . apriyasyāpi pathyasya pariṇāmaḥ sukhāvahaḥ .
054.16A: śṛṇu deva . apriyasya api pathyasya pariṇāmaḥ sukhāvahaḥ .

054.17F: vaktā śrotā ca yatrāsti ramante tatra saṃpadaḥ .. 133..
054.17A: vaktā śrotā ca yatra asti ramante tatra saṃpadaḥ .. 133..

054.16-17E: May Your Highness listen -- The result of what is wholesome although unpleasant, is happy: riches delight (to live) there where there is a speaker and a hearer (of things wholesome though disagreeable).

054.18F: tvayā ca mūlabhṛtyānapāsyāyamāgantukaḥ puraskṛtaḥ .
054.18A: tvayā ca mūlabhṛtyān apāsya ayam āgantukaḥ puraskṛtaḥ .

054.19F: etaccānucitaṃ kṛtam . yataḥ .
054.19A: etat ca anucitam kṛtam . yataḥ .

054.18-19E: You, having discarded old servants, advanced this stranger. And this was a wrong step. For,

054.20F: mūlabhṛtyānparityajya nāgantūnpratimānayet .
054.20A: mūlabhṛtyān parityajya na āgantūn pratimānayet .

054.21F: nātaḥ parataro doṣo rājyabhedakaro yataḥ .. 134..
054.21A: na ataḥ parataraḥ doṣaḥ rājyabhedakaraḥ yataḥ .. 134..

054.20-21E: Having cast off old servants one should not honour strangers: because there is no other fault so destructive to royalty than this.

054.22F: siṃho brūte -- kimāścaryam . yanmayāyaṃ
054.22A: siṃhaḥ brūte -- kim āścaryam . yat mayā ayam

054.23F: abhayavācaṃ dattvānītaḥ saṃvardhitaśca tatkathaṃ mahyaṃ druhyati .
054.23A: abhayavācam dattvā ānītaḥ saṃvardhitaḥ ca tat katham mahyam druhyati .

054.22-23E: The lion said -- What wonder! Since he was brought here by me having pledged my word of safety and was well taken care of, how can he turn a traitor to me?

054.24F: damanako brūte -- deva .
054.24A: damanakaḥ brūte -- deva .

054.25F: durjano prakṛtiṃ yāti sevyamāno'pi nityaśaḥ .
054.25A: durjanaḥ prakṛtim yāti sevyamānaḥ api nityaśaḥ .

054.26F: svedanābhyañjanopāyaiḥ śvapucchamiva nāmitam .. 135..
054.26A: svedanābhyañjanopāyaiḥ śvapuccham iva nāmitam .. 135..
; svedana-aByaYjana-upAya

054.24-26E: Damanaka observed -- Sire, A wicked man, even though served every day, reverts to his natural disposition, like a dog's tail resuming (its natural) bent, notwithstanding such remedies as causing sweat (by fumigation) and rubbing it with unguents (for making it straight).

054.27F: aparaṃ ca . svedito marditaścaiva rajjubhiḥ pariveṣṭitaḥ .
054.27A: aparam ca . sveditaḥ marditaḥ ca eva rajjubhiḥ pariveṣṭitaḥ .
; mardita (not MW) from mfd (to squeeze, rub)

054.28F: mukto dvādaśabhirvarṣaiḥ śvapucchaḥ prakṛtiṃ gataḥ .. 136..
054.28A: muktaḥ dvādaśabhiḥ varṣaiḥ śvapucchaḥ prakṛtim gataḥ .. 136..

054.27-28E: A dog's tail, made to sweat, rubbed and bound round with strings, returned to its nature when set free (even) after twelve years.

054.29F: anyacca . vardhanaṃ vātha sanmānaṃ khalānāṃ prītaye kutaḥ .
054.29A: anyat ca . vardhanam vā atha sanmānam khalānām prītaye kutaḥ .
; prItaye = 4s. f. of prIti

054.30F: phalantyamṛtaseke'pi na pathyāni viṣadrumāḥ .. 137..
054.30A: phalanti amṛtaseke api na pathyāni viṣadrumāḥ .. 137..

054.29-30E: Moreover, Whence can advancement or bestowal of honour please the wicked? Poisonous trees, although watered with nectar, do not bring forth fruit wholesome to eat.

054.31F: ato'haṃ bravīmi --
054.31A: ataḥ aham bravīmi --

054.32F: apṛṣṭo'pi hitaṃ brūyādyasya necchet parābhavam .
054.32A: apṛṣṭaḥ api hitam brūyāt yasya na icchet parābhavam .

054.33F: eṣa eva satāṃ dharmo viparītamato'nyathā .. 138..
054.33A: eṣaḥ eva satām dharmaḥ viparītam athaḥ anyathā .. 138..

015.31-33E: Hence my observation -- One should say what is beneficial to him whose ruin one does not wish; this is the duty of the good; the contrary is otherwise (i. e. is the way of action of bad men).

055.01F: tathā coktam --
055.01A: tathā ca uktam --

055.03F: sā strī yātuvidhāyinī sa matimānyaḥ sadbhirabhyarcyate .

055.03P: anuvidhāyinī -- ājñākāriṇī , bhartuścittānusāriṇī vā .

055.01-03E: It is said in connexion with this -- He has affection (for us) who dissuades (us) from evil; that is an act which is pure; she is a wife, who is obedient; he is talented who is esteemed by the good;

055.04F: sā śrīryā na madaṃ karoti sa sukhī yastṛṣṇayā mucyate

055.04P: karoti janayati .

055.04-05E: that is wealth which begets no vanity; he is happy who is free from desire; he is a friend who is sincere (lit. artless); and he is a man who is not troubled by the senses (i. e. has his senses under control).

055.06-07E: If Your Highness who stands in imminent danger from Samjivaka, does not turn back after being warned (lit. informed), then the blame does not lie with a servant like myself.

055.08F: nṛpaḥ kāmāsakto gaṇayati na kārye na ca hitaṃ

055.08-09E: A king who is addicted to carnal pleasures does not mind the business he has to attend to or his good, but led by his free will he acts as he likes like a mad elephant;

055.10F: tato mānadhmātaḥ sa patati yadā śokagahane

055.10P: mānādhmātaḥ -- madoddhataḥ .
055.10P+: śokagahane -- śokāraṇye .

055.11P: avinayam -- anucitācaraṇam .

055.10-11E:  but when, puffed up with pride, he falls into the abyss of sorrow, he casts the blame on his servants, but does not take into account his own misconduct.

055.12F: piṅgalakaḥ svagatam .
055.12A: piṅgalakaḥ svagatam .

055.12-14E: Pingalaka (To himself) -- One should not inflict punishment upon others by (listening to) the adverse representation of another : but having ascertained the truth for oneself, one shonld mete out punishment or praise.

055.15-17E: Similarly it is said -- To award favour or punishment without ascertaining one's merit or fault is not the policy: (such a course) leads to one's destruction like the hand thrust into a serpent's month through vanity.

055.18F: prakāśaṃ brūte -- tadā saṃjīvakaḥ kiṃ pratyādiśyatām .
