055.18-20E: (Aloud) What then, shall Samjivaka be warned (against such a course of conduct)? Damanaka observed in haste -- Not so, not so my lord. This will mean the divulging of counsel. For it is said --

055.21F: mantrabījamidaṃ guptaṃ rakṣaṇīyaṃ tathā yathā .
055.21A: mantrabījam idam guptam rakṣaṇīyam tathā yathā .

055.22F: manāgapi na bhidyeta tadbhinnaṃ na prarohati .. 143..
055.22A: manāk api na bhidyeta tat bhinnam na prarohati .. 143..
055.22P: bhidyeta -- prakāśaṃ gacchet .
055.22P+: na prarohati aṅkuraṃ na prasūte . vistāraṃ prāpya na phalati ityarthaḥ .

055.21-22E: The seed of counsel should be kept concealed in such a way that not even a glimpse of it could get out; if got out it will not thrive.

055.23F: kiṃ ca . ādeyasya pradeyasya kartavyasya ca karmaṇaḥ .

055.24F: kṣipramakriyamāṇasya kālaḥ pibati tadrasam .. 144..
055.24A: kṣipram akriyamāṇasya kālaḥ pibati tat rasam .. 144..

055.23-24E: Moreover, If what is to be taken or given or done be not quickly attended to, time saps its juice.

056.01F: tadavaśyaṃ samārabdhaṃ mahatā prayatnena sampādanīyam . kiṃ ca .

056.01P: sampādanīyam -- nirvartanīyaṃ , samāptiṃ netavyam .

056.02F: mantro yodha ivādhīraḥ sarvāṅgaiḥ saṃvṛtairapi .

056.02P: saṃvṛtaiḥ suguptaiḥ kavacācchāditaiśca .

056.03F: ciraṃ na sahate sthātuṃ parebhyo bhedaśaṅkayā .. 145..

056.03P: bhedaśaṅkayā -- prakāśaśaṅkayā vidāraṇaśaṅkayā ca .

056.01-03E: Therefore what is set on foot should necessarily be accomplished with a mighty effort. Again, Counsel, like a timid warrior, although having all the parts well covered, is not able to keep up long for fear of being penetrated by others (the enemies).

056.04F: yadyasau dṛṣṭadoṣo'pi doṣānnivartya saṃdhātavyastad atīvānucitam .

056.05F: yataḥ .
056.05A: yataḥ .

056.04-05E: And if a reconciliation is to be sought with him (the bull), after his offence has been known, he being made to turn back from such a wrong course of conduct, that would be extremely impolitic. For,

056.06F: sakṛdduṣṭaṃ tu yo mitraṃ punaḥ saṃdhātumicchati .

056.06-07E: He who wishes to conciliate a friend once estranged invites death itself like a she-mule conceiving a fetus.

056.16-17E: My dear, find out a retired place convenient for my delivery. The male said -- My dear, this very place is surely fit for your delivery.

056.18-19E: She replied -- This place is washed over by the tide. The male observed -- What? Am I so powerless that the sea should insult me, stationed in my own house?

056.20-22E: The female said smiling -- My lord, vast is the difference between the sea and yourself. Or rather, It is difficult to form a correct estimate of one's self -- whether one is capable (of achieving a thing) or not.  He who has such knowledge does not experience trouble even in a difficulty.

056.23-24E: The beginning of an unworthy act, opposition to one's relatives, emulation with the stronger, and confidence in young women —- these are four doors to death.

056.25F: tataḥ kṛcchreṇa svāmivacanāttatraiva prasūtā sā . etatsarvaṃ

056.25-26E: Then following (with difficulty) the advice of her husband she laid her eggs there. Having heard all that, the sea too, wishing to know their strength, carried off their eggs.

056.27F: tata ṭiṭṭibhī śokārtā

056.27-28E: Then the female tittibha, smitten with grief, said to her husband -- Lord, evil has befallen us. Those my eggs are lost.

057.13-15E: Damanaka replied -- How can there be any happiness for servants? For, the riches of those who are in royal service are in another's power; their mind is always uneasy, and they have no surety even of their lives.

057.16-17E: Moreover, Who, having obtained wealth, does not become proud? The miseries of what sensualist have come to an end? Whose mind is not wounded by woman? Who is a favourite of kings?

057.18-19E: Who has not fallen into the clutches of Death? What supplicant has met with honour, and what man, fallen into the meshes of the wicked, has escaped unscathed?

057.20F: saṃjīvakenoktam -- sakhe brūhi kimetat .

057.20-21E: Samjivaka said -- Friend, speak out what this means. Damanaka replied -- What should I say, an unfortunate creature! Behold,

057.22-23E: Just as a man plunged into the sea having obtained the support of a serpent, does neither give it up nor hold fast to it, so bewildered am I now.

057.24F: yataḥ . ekatra rājaviśvāso naśyatyanyatra bāndhavaḥ .

057.24-25E:  For, On the one hand is the royal confidence betrayed, on the other, a friend perishes: what shall I do, and where shall I go, I who am fallen into the sea of trouble?

057.26F: ityuktvā dīrghaṃ niḥśvasyopaviṣṭaḥ .

057.26-27E: With these words he heaved a deep sigh and sat down. Samjivaka said -- Still, friend, tell me in detail what you have at heart.

057.28F: damanakaḥ sunibhṛtamāha -- yadyapi rājaviśvāso na kathanīyastathāpi

057.28-29E: Damanaka said with (a show of) great secrecy -- Although I must not betray the king's secret, yet you have come here through confidence in us; and I, as desiring the next world, must necessarily tell you what concerns your welfare.

058.01-02E: Women seek the company of wicked men; a king generally patronizes (or, lavishes wealth upon) the undeserving; wealth seeks a miser; and the god of rain pours the showers on mountains and seas!

058.03-05E: (To himself) Now it is not possible to decide from his manner of acting (or, conversing) whether this is his doing or not. For, Some wicked man possesses splendour (appears good amiable) from the beauty of his master (or patron, lit. the person he depends upon), like fool (black) collyrium when put into their eyes by young women.

058.06-07E: After reflection; he says -- Alas! What is this that has come to pass ! For, A king, though served with assiduity, may not be pleased; where is the wonder in this?

058.08F: ayaṃ tvapūrvapratimāviśeṣo yaḥ sevyamāno riputāmupaiti .. 156..

058.08-09E: But this is some strange pattern of creation, who being served is turned into an enemy!!! So this is a matter (lit. something to be understood by inference) which it is impossible to understand. For,

058.12F: akāraṇadveṣi manastu yasya vai

058.13A: katham janaḥ tam paritoṣayiṣyati .. 157..

058.12-13E:  but how can a man please him whose mind harbours enmity without cause?

058.14F: kiṃ mayāpakṛtaṃ rājñaḥ . athavā nirnimittāpakāriṇaśca bhavanti rājānaḥ .
058.14A: kim mayā apakṛtam rājñaḥ . athavā nirnimittāpakāriṇaḥ ca bhavanti rājānaḥ .
058.14P: nirnimitta - nirgataṃ nimittaṃ yasminkarmaṇi tadyathā tathā kāraṇavyatirekeṇa apakurvanti tādṛśāḥ .

058.15F: damanako brūte -- evametat . śṛṇu .
058.15A: damanakaḥ brūte -- evam etat . śṛṇu .

058.14-15E: What wrong did I do to the king? Or rather, kings are wont to do injury without any cause. Damanaka observed -- It is just so. Listen.

058.16F: vijñaiḥ snigdhairupakṛtamapi dveṣyatāmeti kiṃcit
058.16A: vijñaiḥ snigdhaiḥ upakṛtam api dveṣyatām eti kim cit
058.16P: vijñaiḥ viśeṣaṃ jānantīti vijñāḥ vicakṣaṇāḥ .
058.16P+: taiḥ snigdhaiḥ hitabuddhibhiḥ .
058.16P++: upakṛtamapi kiṃcit upakāratvena kṛtamapi kiṃcit .

058.17F: sākṣādanyairapakṛtamapi prītimevopayāti .
058.17A: sākṣāt anyaiḥ apakṛtam api prītim eva upayāti .

057.16-17E: Even an act of kindness, done by man eminently learned and affectionate, becomes hateful; while an actual injury done by others is just regarded with pleasure:

058.18F: durgrāhyatvānnṛpatimanasāṃ naikabhāvāśrayāṇāṃ
058.18A: durgrāhyatvāt nṛpatimanasām na ekabhāvāśrayāṇām
058.18P: durgrāhyatvāddurjñeyatvāt .
058.18P+: naikabhāvāśrayāṇāṃ asthiracittānāmityarthaḥ . dveṣyatāmeti dveṣaṃ saṃpādayati .

058.19F: sevādharmaḥ paramagahano yogināmapyagamyaḥ .. 158..
058.19A: sevādharmaḥ paramagahanaḥ yoginām api agamyaḥ .. 158..

058.18-19E: on account of difficulty of understanding the minds of kings which are unsteady (lit., not the abode of one feeling); the duty of servitude is extremely difficult, not to be comprehended even by Yogis (those who have attained superhuman powers).

058.20F: anyacca . kṛtaśatamasatsu naṣṭaṃ subhāṣitaśataṃ ca naṣṭamabudheṣu .
058.20A: anyat ca . kṛtaśatam asatsu naṣṭam subhāṣitaśatam ca naṣṭam abudheṣu .
058.20P: kṛtaśatam -- kṛtopakāraśatam .
058.20P+: asatsu -- akṛtajñeṣu .
058.20P++: naṣṭaṃ -- viphalaṃ bhavatīti śeṣaḥ .
058.20P+++: abudheṣu -- kāvyarasānabhijñeṣu .

058.21F: vacanaśatamavacanakare buddhiśatamacetane naṣṭam .. 159..
058.21A: vacanaśatam avacanakare buddhiśatam acetane naṣṭam .. 159..
058.21P: avacanakare -- vākyapālanaparāṅmukhe .
058.21P+: acetane jñānarahite .

058.20-21E: A hundred obligations (or, services rendered) are lost upon the wicked; a hundred fine speeches upon the illiterate; a hundred words of advice upon those who would not act up to them; and a hundred counsels on the senseless.

058.22F: kiṃ ca . candanataruṣu bhujaṅgā jaleṣu kamalāni tatra ca grāhāḥ .
058.22A: kim ca . candanataruṣu bhujaṅgāḥ jaleṣu kamalāni tatra ca grāhāḥ .
058.22P: candanataruṣu -- candanasya ghrāṇatarpaṇaḥ gandhaḥ asti kiṃtu tatra bhujaṃgabhayaṃ ityarthaḥ .
058.22P+: grāhāḥ nakrāḥ .

058.23F: guṇaghātinaśca bhoge khalā na ca sukhānyavighnāni .. 160..
058.23A: guṇaghātinaḥ ca bhoge khalāḥ na ca sukhāni avighnāni .. 160..
058.23P: bhoge amātyapadādīnāmiti śeṣaḥ .
058.23P+: guṇaghātinaḥ -- guṇalopakāriṇaḥ khalāḥ piśunāḥ .

058.22-23E: There are serpents on the sandal trees; lotuses grow in water wherein there are also alligators; and when one is in the enjoyment of a thing there are villains to obscure one's good qualities ; (so) pleasures are not without obstructions!

059.01F: anyacca . mūlaṃ bhujaṅgaiḥ kusumāni bhṛṅgaiḥ śākhāḥ plavaṅgaiḥ śikharāṇi bhallaiḥ .
059.01A: anyat ca. mūlam bhujaṅgaiḥ kusumāni bhṛṅgaiḥ śākhāḥ plavaṅgaiḥ śikharāṇi bhallaiḥ .
059.01P: bhallaiḥ ṛkṣaiḥ .

059.02F: nāstyeva taccandanapādapasya yannāśritaṃ duṣṭataraiśca hiṃsraiḥ .. 161..
059.02A: na asti eva tat candanapādapasya yat na āśritam duṣṭataraiḥ ca hiṃsraiḥ .. 161..
059.02P: duṣṭataraiḥ atiduṣṭaiḥ .

059.01-02E: And further, The root is infested by serpents, the flowers by bees, the branches by monkeys and the tops by bears; thus there is nothing belonging to the sandal tree that is not resorted to by very cruel and murderous animals.

059.03F: ayaṃ tāvatsvāmī vāṅmadhuro viṣahṛdayo mayā jñātaḥ . yataḥ .
059.03A: ayam tāvat svāmī vāṅmadhuraḥ viṣahṛdayaḥ mayā jñātaḥ . yataḥ .

059.04F: dūrād ucchritapāṇirārdranayanaḥ protsāritārdhāsano
059.04A: dūrāt ucchritapāṇiḥ ārdranayanaḥ protsāritārdhāsanaḥ
059.04P: ucchritapāṇiḥ unnamitahastaḥ .
059.04P+: protsārita -- protsāritaṃ utsṛṣṭaṃ ardhāsanaṃ yena .

059.05F: gāḍhāliṅganatatparaḥ priyakathāpraśneṣu dattādaraḥ .
059.05A: gāḍhāliṅganatatparaḥ priyakathāpraśneṣu dattādaraḥ .

059.03-05E: As for our master, I have known him to be honeyed in speech but carrying poison in the heart. For, He raises his hand from a distance (by way of greeting) and has his eyes moist (with tears of joy); he proffers half of his seat, he is ready to give a close embrace, shows great regard in making inquiries and talking about one's beloved persons,

059.06F: antarbhūtaviṣo bahirmadhumayaścātīva māyāpaṭuḥ
059.06A: antarbhūtaviṣaḥ bahiḥ madhumayaḥ ca atīva māyāpaṭuḥ
059.06P: antarbhūtaviṣaḥ -- antarbhūtaṃ viṣaṃ yasya .
059.06P+: madhumayaḥ madhupracuraḥ .
059.06P++: bahiḥ ramaṇīyaṃ vyavaharah ityarthaḥ .
059.06P+++: māyāpaṭuḥ kapaṭajālavistaraṇe kuśalaḥ .

059.07F: ko nāmāyamapūrvanāṭakavidhiryaḥ śikṣito durjanaiḥ .. 162..
059.07A: kaḥ nāma ayam apūrvanāṭakavidhiḥ yaḥ śikṣitaḥ durjanaiḥ .. 162..

059.06-07E: has poison inside, but is all sweetness from outside, and is an expert in deceit (or dissembling ): what pantomimic art is this, unheard of before, that has beon learnt by the wicked ?

059.08F: tathā hi . poto dustaravārirāśitaraṇe dīpo'ndhakārāgame

; vArirASi - great mass of water (sea).
059.08P: potaḥ -- naukā .

; mw has 'sfRi', not 'SfRi'
; upaSAntyEH + sfRiH -> (? Sandhi) upaSAntyE SfRiH
; karin elephant
059.09P: śṛṇiḥ -- aṅkuśaḥ .

059.08-09E: To make matters clear. For crossing the impassable sea there is the boat (provided), the lamp against the approach of darkness, the fan when there is absence of breeze and the goad for quelling the pride of elephants stupified by rut:

059.10F: itthaṃ tadbhuvi nāsti yasya vidhinā nopāyacintā kṛtā
059.10A: ittham tat bhuvi na asti yasya vidhinā na upāyacintā kṛtā manye
; kftA = 3s m. kft (creator)

059.11F: manye durjanacittavṛttiharaṇe dhātāpi bhagnodyamaḥ .. 163..
059.11A: manye durjanacittavṛttiharaṇe dhātāpi bhagnodyamaḥ .. 163..
; DAtA = 1s m. DAtf (creator)
059.11P: bhagnodyamaḥ -- viphalaprayatnaḥ .

059.10-11E: Thus there is nothing on earth, to provide a remedy against which, care has not been taken by the Creator; but, methinks, even the Creator is foiled in his efforts to dispel the (evil) tendencies of the minds of the wicked.

059.12F: saṃjīvakaḥ punarniḥśvasya -- kaṣṭaṃ bhoḥ .
059.12A: saṃjīvakaḥ punaḥ niḥśvasya -- kaṣṭam bhoḥ .

059.13F: kathamahaṃ sasyabhakṣakaḥ siṃhena nipātayitavyaḥ . yataḥ .
059.13A: katham aham sasyabhakṣakaḥ siṃhena nipātayitavyaḥ . yataḥ .

059.12-13E: Samjivaka, heaving a sigh again — Alas! Oh, pity! that I, as corn-eater, should be falled by a lion!! For,

059.14F: yayoreva samaṃ vittaṃ yayoreva samaṃ balam .
059.14A: yayoḥ eva samam vittam yayoḥ eva samam balam .

059.15F: tayorvivādo mantavyo nottamādhamayoḥ kvacit .. 164..
059.15A: tayoḥ vivādaḥ mantavyaḥ na uttamādhamayoḥ kva cit .. 164..
059.15P: uttamādhamayoḥ utkṛṣṭanikṛṣṭayoḥ , hīnādhikabalayoḥ .

059.14-15E: Between those two only whose wealth is equal, or whose power is equal, a dispute can well be understood; but never between the best and the worst.

059.16F: punarvicintya . kenāyaṃ rājā mamopari vikāntito na jāne . bhedamupagatādrājñaḥ
059.16A: punaḥ vicintya . kena ayam rājā mama upari vikāntitaḥ na jāne . bhedam upagatāt rājñaḥ
; vikAntitaH probably wrong. ??
059.16P: bhedamupagatāt -- vikṛtāt vidveṣabhāvaṃ gatāt .

059.17F: sadā bhetavyam . yataḥ .
059.17A: sadā bhetavyam . yataḥ .

059.16-17E: (Reflecting again) I do not know who has set (poisoned the mind of) this king against me. One has to be always in dread of a king whose feelings are estranged. For,

059.18F: mantriṇā pṛthivīpālacittaṃ vighaṭitaṃ kvacit .
059.18A: mantriṇā pṛthivīpālacittaṃ vighaṭitam kvacit .
059.18P: vighaṭitaṃ -- viśleṣitam .

059.19F: valayaṃ sphaṭikasyeva ko hi saṃdhātumīśvaraḥ .. 165 ..
059.19A: valayam sphaṭikasya eva kaḥ hi saṃdhātum īśvaraḥ .. 165 ..
059.19P: īśvaraḥ -- samarthaḥ .

059.18-19E: When a king's mind has once been alienated from his minister who can re-unite it, like a crystal bracelet when broken?

059.20F: anyacca . vajraṃ ca rājatejaśca dvayamevātibhīṣaṇam .
059.20A: anyat ca . vajram ca rājatejaḥ ca dvayam eva atibhīṣaṇam .
059.20P: vajraṃ kuliśam . vidyutpāt iti yāvat .

059.21F: ekamekatra patati patatyanyatsamantataḥ .. 166 ..
059.21A: ekam ekatra patati patati anyat samantataḥ .. 166 ..
059.21P: samantataḥ sarvavyāpīti tato viśiṣyata ityarthaḥ .

059.20-21E: Moreover, The thunderbolt and kingly power -— these two are extremely terrible: but the one falls in one place, the other (exerts its influence) all round.

059.22F: tatsaṃgrāme mṛtyurevāśrīyatām . idānīṃ tadājñānuvartanamayuktam . yataḥ .
059.22A: tat saṃgrāme mṛtyuḥ eva āśrīyatām . idānīm tadā ājñānuvartanam ayuktam . yataḥ .

059.23F: mṛtaḥ prāpnoti vā svargaṃ śatruṃ hatvā sukhāni vā .
059.23A: mṛtaḥ prāpnoti vā svargam śatrum hatvā sukhāni vā .

059.22-23E: Death in battle, therefore, should be accepted. It will not be proper for me, now, to act in obedience to his commands. Because, If dead, he (a brave warrior) attains heaven; if he kills the foe he obtains happiness.

059.24F: ubhāvapi hi śūrāṇāṃ guṇāvetau sudurlabhau .. 167 ..
059.24A: ubhau api hi śūrāṇām guṇau etau sudurlabhau .. 167 ..

059.25F: yuddhakālaścāyam .
059.25A: yuddhakālaḥ ca ayam .

059.24-25E: These two advantages, which the valiant possess, are very rare. And this is the fit time for battle.

059.26F: yatrāyuddhe dhruvaṃ mṛtyuryuddhe jīvitasaṃśayaḥ .
059.26A: yatra ayuddhe dhruvam mṛtyuḥ yuddhe jīvitasaṃśayaḥ .

059.27F: tameva kālaṃ yuddhasya pravadanti manīṣiṇaḥ .. 168 ..
059.27A: tam eva kālam yuddhasya pravadanti manīṣiṇaḥ .. 168 ..

059.26-27E: When out of battle death is certain, but in battle life is doubtful (there is some chance of living), then that, the wise declare to be the time for battle.

059.28F: yataḥ . ayuddhe hi yadā paśyenna kiñcid hitamātmanaḥ .
059.28A: yataḥ . ayuddhe hi yadā paśyet na kim cit hitam ātmanaḥ .

059.29F: yudhyamānastadā prājño mriyate ripuṇā saha .. 169..
059.29A: yudhyamānaḥ tadā prājñaḥ mriyate ripuṇā saha .. 169..

059.28-29E: For, When a wise man sees no benefit accruing to himself from not fighting, he dies fighting the foe.

060.01F: jaye ca labhate lakṣmīṃ mṛtenāpi surāṅganām .
060.01A: jaye ca labhate lakṣmīm mṛtena api surāṅganām .
060.01P: mṛtena -- maraṇena . atrānurūpo bhāvaḥ veṇīsaṃhāre --'atha maraṇamavaśyameva jantoḥ kimiti mudhā malinaṃ yaśaḥ kurudhve' iti .

060.02F: kṣaṇavidhvaṃsinaḥ kāyāḥ kā cintā maraṇe raṇe .. 170 ..
060.02A: kṣaṇavidhvaṃsinaḥ kāyāḥ kā cintā maraṇe raṇe .. 170 ..

060.01-02E: In case of victory, he (a warrior) obtains fortune; if he dies, a heavenly damsel: when the bodies are perishable in a moment, what hesitation should there be about dying in battle?

060.03F: etaccintayitvā saṃjīvaka āha -- bho mitra kathamasau māṃ jighāṃsurjñātavyaḥ . damanako
060.03A: etat cintayitvā saṃjīvakaḥ āha -- bho mitra katham asau mām jighāṃsuḥ jñātavyaḥ . damanakaḥ
060.03P: jighāṃsuḥ hantumicchuḥ .

060.04F: brūte -- yadāsau samuddhatalāṅgūla unnatacaraṇo vivṛtāsyastvāṃ paśyati tadā tvamapi
060.04A: brūte -- yadā asau samuddhatalāṅgūlaḥ unnatacaraṇaḥ vivṛtāsyaḥ tvām paśyati tadā tvam api

060.05F: svavikramaṃ darśayiṣyasi . yataḥ .
060.05A: svavikramam darśayiṣyasi . yataḥ .

060.03-05E: Having pondered thus, Samjivaka said -- Friend, how am I to know that he is bent on (lit., desirous of) killing me? Damanaka replied -- When he, with his tail erect, his (fore)-paws lifted up and his mouth wide open, will look at you, you too should display your prowess. For,

060.06F: balavānapi nistejāḥ kasya nābhibhavāspadam .
060.06A: balavān api nistejāḥ kasya na abhibhavāspadam .
; aBiBavAspadam derivation unclear to me. 'object of contempt'
060.06P: abhibhavāspadam -- parābhavasthānaṃ , kena na parābhūyate sarvaiḥ parābhūyate eva ityarthaḥ .

060.07F: niḥśaṅkaṃ dīyate laukeḥ paśya bhasmacaye padam .. 171 ..
060.07A: niḥśaṅkam dīyate laukeḥ paśya bhasmacaye padam .. 171 ..
060.07P: bhasmacaye bhasmasamūhe .

060.06-07E: To whom is a man, powerful yet void of fire (spirit, energy) not an object of contempt? Lo, people fearlessly set their foot upon a heap of ashes.

060.08F: kiṃtu sarvametatsuguptamanuṣṭhātavyam . no cenna tvaṃ nāham . ityuktvā damanakaḥ
060.08A: kim tu sarvam etat suguptam anuṣṭhātavyam . na cet na tvam na aham . iti uktvā damanakaḥ
060.08P: na tvam nāham -- ubhāvapi vinaṃkṣyāva ityartha .
; vi+naMkzyAvaH  naS fut. ac. du. 1  (we two will perish)

060.09F: karaṭakasamīpaṃ gataḥ . karaṭakenoktam -- kiṃ niṣpannam . damanakenoktam --
060.09A: karaṭakasamīpam gataḥ . karaṭakena uktam -- kim niṣpannam . damanakena uktam --

060.08-09E: ut all this must be done with the strictest privacy; otherwise, not you, not I (i. e., it will be all over with us both). Having said these things Damanaka went to Karataka. Karataka asked him -- What is the outcome (of your efforts)? Damanaka replied --

060.10F: niṣpanno'sāvanyonyabhedaḥ . karaṭako brūte -- ko'tra saṃdehaḥ . yataḥ .
060.10A: niṣpannaḥ asau anyonyabhedaḥ . karaṭakaḥ brūte -- kaḥ atra saṃdehaḥ . yataḥ .

060.11F: bandhuḥ ko nāma duṣṭānāṃ kupyetko nātiyācitaḥ .
060.11A: bandhuḥ kaḥ nāma duṣṭānām kupyet kaḥ na atiyācitaḥ .
; Sampada: 'kupyetko' is confusing.

060.10-11E: A reciprocal breach (of friendship) has been effected as intended. Karataka observed -- What doubt can there be as to that! For, Who, possibly, is a friend of the wicked? Who will not get angry when pressed with great importunity?

060.12F: ko na hṛṣyati vittena kukṛtye ko na paṇḍitaḥ .. 172 ..
060.12A: kaḥ na hṛṣyati vittena kukṛtye kaḥ na paṇḍitaḥ .. 172 ..

060.13F: anyacca . durvṛttaḥ kriyate dhūrtaiḥ śrīmānātmavivṛddhaye .
060.13A: anyat ca . durvṛttaḥ kriyate dhūrtaiḥ śrīmān ātmavivṛddhaye .
; grammatical form of 'durvfttaH' difficult here. why not 'EH' ?

060.13P+: ātmavivṛddhaye ātmana utkarṣasādhanārtham . śrīmān durvṛttaḥ duścaritaḥ kriyate .

060.14F: kiṃ nāma khalasaṃsargaḥ kurute nāśrayāśavat .. 173 ..
060.14A: kim nāma khalasaṃsargaḥ kurute na āśrayāśavat .. 173 ..
060.14P: āśrayāśavat -- āśrayaṃ ādhāraṃ āśnāti bhasmasātkarotīti āśrayāśaḥ agniḥ tena tulyam .

060.12-14E: Who does not become proud on account of wealth, and who is not clever in doing an evil deed? Moreover, A wealthy man is led into vice by artful men for self-aggrandizement: what mischief does not the company of villains do, like fire?

060.15F: tato damanakaḥ piṅgalakasamīpāṃ gatvā deva samāgato'sau pāpāśayaḥ . tatsajjībhūya
060.15A: tataḥ damanakaḥ piṅgalakasamīpām gatvā deva samāgataḥ asau pāpāśayaḥ . tat sajjībhūya

060.16F: sthīyatām ityuktvā pūrvoktākāraṃ kārayāmāsa . saṃjīvako'pyāgatya tathāvidhaṃ
060.16A: sthīyatām iti uktvā pūrvoktākāram kārayāmāsa . saṃjīvakaḥ api āgatya tathāvidham

060.17F: vikṛtākāraṃ siṃhaṃ dṛṣṭvā svānurūpaṃ vikramaṃ cakāra . tatastayoḥ prvṛtte mahāhave
060.17A: vikṛtākāram siṃham dṛṣṭvā svānurūpam vikramam cakāra . tataḥ tayoḥ prvṛtte mahāhave

060.18F: saṃjīvakaḥ siṃhena vyāpāditaḥ .
060.18A: saṃjīvakaḥ siṃhena vyāpāditaḥ .

060.15-18E: Damanaka then repaired to Pingalaka, and saying -- My lord, the villain (lit., the vile intentioned one) is coming; do you therefore prepare yourself and wait -- he made him assume the attitude described before. Samjivaka too, on coming there, saw the lion with altered features in that way and displayed his valour in a manner worthy of himself. Then in the fierce battle that ensued Samjivaka was killed by the lion.

060.19F: atha piṅgalakaḥ saṃjīvakaṃ vyāpādya viśrāntaḥ saśoko iva tiṣṭhati . brūte ca -- kiṃ
060.19A: atha piṅgalakaḥ saṃjīvakam vyāpādya viśrāntaḥ saśokaḥ iva tiṣṭhati . brūte ca -- kim

060.20F: mayā dāruṇaṃ karma kṛtam . yataḥ .
060.20A: mayā dāruṇam karma kṛtam . yataḥ .

060.19-20E: Now Pingalaka, after he had slain Samjivaka and taken rest, stood like one sorrow-smitten and said -- What a cruel deed have I done! For,

060.21F: paraiḥ saṃbhujyate rājyaṃ svayaṃ pāpasya bhājanam .
060.21A: paraiḥ saṃbhujyate rājyam svayam pāpasya bhājanam .
060.21P: parairiti -- rājā dharmātikramataḥ dharmalaṅghanātpāpasya bhājanaṃ bhavati rājyaṃ tu paraiḥ bhujyate .

060.22F: dharmātikramato rājā siṃho hastivadhādiva .. 174 ..
060.22A: dharmātikramataḥ rājā siṃhaḥ hastivadhāt iva .. 174 ..
060.22P: yathā siṃhaḥ kṛtahastivadhapātaka eva tiṣṭhati . hatahastino dantāḥ tadgaṇḍasthalagatāni ca mauktikānyanye eva gṛhṇāti tathā ityarthaḥ .

060.21-22E: When a king transgresses his duty, his kingdom is enjoyed by others; while he himself is the abode of sin, like a lion that kills an elephant. * The lion kills the elephant and remains guilty of the murder, while the tusks and bones of the elephant are obtained by others.
; 08/08/2021 end
060.23F: aparaṃ ca . bhūmyekadeśasya guṇānvitasya
060.23A: aparam ca . bhūmyekadeśasya guṇānvitasya

060.24F: bhṛtyasya vā buddhimataḥ praṇāśe .
060.24A: bhṛtyasya vā buddhimataḥ praṇāśe .
060.24P: praṇāśe -- upasthite iti śeṣaḥ .

060.25F: bhṛtyapraṇāśo maraṇaṃ nṛpāṇāṃ
060.25A: bhṛtyapraṇāśaḥ maraṇam nṛpāṇām

060.26F: naṣṭāpi bhūmiḥ sulabhā na bhṛtyāḥ .. 175..
060.26A: naṣṭā api bhūmiḥ sulabhāḥ na bhṛtyāḥ .. 175..

060.23-26E: When there is loss of a part of one's territory, or, of a servant meritorious and gifted with intellect, the loss of the servant is death to a king: land though lost may easily be acquired, but not servants.

060.27F: damanako brūte -- svāmin ko'yaṃ
060.27A: damanakaḥ brūte -- svāmin kaḥ ayam

060.28F: nūtano nyāyo yadarātiṃ hatvā saṃtāpaḥ kriyate . tathā coktam --
060.28A: nūtanaḥ nyāyaḥ yat arātim hatvā saṃtāpaḥ kriyate . tathā ca uktam --

060.27-28E: Damanaka observed -- My lord, what a novel course of action is this, that having killed an enemy you should be sorrowing over it! For it is said --

060.29F: pitā vā yadi vā bhrātā putrī vā yadi vā suhṛt .
060.29A: pitā vā yadi vā bhrātā putrī vā yadi vā suhṛt .

060.30F: prāṇacchedakarā rājñā hantavyā bhūtimicchatā .. 176..
; icCatA 3s prap of iz 6: desiring
060.30A: prāṇacchedakarā rājñā hantavyā bhūtim icchatā .. 176..

060.29-30E: A king who desires his own welfare should put to death those who aim at his life, whether it be his father, or brother, or son or friend.

060.31F: api ca . dharmārthakāmatattvajño naikāntakaruṇo bhavet .
060.31A: api ca . dharmārthakāmatattvajñaḥ na ekāntakaruṇaḥ bhavet .
060.31P: dharmārthakāmatattvajñaḥ - trivargasādhanapara ityarthaḥ .

060.32F: na hi hastasthamapyannaṃ kṣamāvānrakṣituṃ kṣamaḥ .. 177..
; kzamAvAn (kzamAvat) = patient;
; kzamaH = able
060.32A: na hi hastastham api annam kṣamāvān rakṣitum kṣamaḥ .. 177..

060.31-32E: Moreover, One, who knows the real nature of Dharma, Artha and Kama, should not be exclusively merciful; for a man given to forgiveness is not able to save even the thing in his hand.

061.01F: kiṃ ca . kṣamā śatrau ca mitre ca yatīnāmeva bhūṣaṇam .
061.01A: kim ca . kṣamā śatrau ca mitre ca yatīnām eva bhūṣaṇam .

061.02F: aparādhiṣu sattveṣu nṛpāṇāṃ saiva dūṣaṇam .. 178..
061.02A: aparādhiṣu sattveṣu nṛpāṇām sā eva dūṣaṇam .. 178..

061.01-02E: Also, Forgiveness shown to friend or foe is an ornament in the case of hermits, while the same when shown to offenders by kings is a blemish.

061.03F: aparaṃ ca . rājyalobhādahaṃkārādicchataḥ svāminaḥ padam .
061.03A: aparam ca . rājyalobhāt ahaṃkārāt icchataḥ svāminaḥ padam .

061.04F: prāyaścittaṃ tu tasyaikaṃ jīvotsargo na cāparam .. 179..
061.04A: prāyaścittam tu tasya ekam jīvotsargaḥ na ca aparam .. 179..

061.03-04E: Again, There is only one expiation for him who, through lust of sovereignty or pride, covets his master's post, viz., the relinquishing of life (capital punishment) and none else.

061.05F: anyacca . rājā ghṛṇī brāhmaṇaḥ sarvabhakṣaḥ
061.05A: anyat ca . rājā ghṛṇī brāhmaṇaḥ sarvabhakṣaḥ

061.06P: duṣprakṛtiḥ duṣṭasvabhāvaḥ .
061.06P+: sahāyaḥ sahacaraḥ .

061.07F: preṣyaḥ pratīpo'dhikṛtaḥ pramādī
061.07A: preṣyaḥ pratīpaḥ adhikṛtaḥ pramādī
061.07P: preṣyaḥ bhṛtyaḥ .
061.07P+: pratīpaḥ -- svāminideśalaṅghī pratikūlācaraṇaḥ .
061.07P++: adhikṛtaḥ kāryādhikārī .

061.08F: tyājyā ime yaśca kṛtaṃ na vetti .. 180..
; vetti = 3s pre vid (he knows)
061.08A: tyājyāḥ ime yaḥ ca kṛtam na vetti .. 180..

061.05-08E: A sovereign who is merciful, a Brahmana eating every thing (or, very greedy), a wife not under control, a companion of evil conduct, a servant who is impertinent (lit., going against his master's orders) and an officer who is careless -- these should be abandoned, as well as he who is ungrateful.

061.09F: viśeṣataśca . satyā'nṛtā ca paruṣā priyavādinī ca
061.09A: viśeṣataḥ ca . satyā anṛtāḥ ca paruṣā priyavādinī ca
061.09P: satyānṛtā -- satyaṃ anṛtaṃ ca yasyām .
061.09P+: paruṣā viṣayaviśeṣe kaṭhinā .

061.10F: hiṃsrā dayālurapi cārthaparā vadānyā .
061.10A: hiṃsrā dayāluḥ api ca arthaparāḥ vadānyā .
061.10P: arthaparā svārthasādhanatatparā , dravyārjanatatparā vā .
061.10P+: vadānyā -- kadācit dānaśīlā .

061.09-10E: Particularly, Truthful and (also) false (when necessary), now harsh and now of sweet address, cruel, and also merciful (at times), now economical (lit., devoted to saving money), anon liberal,

061.11F: nityavyayā pracuraratnadhanāgamā ca
061.11A: nityavyayā pracuraratnadhanāgamā ca
061.11P: pracura -- pracurāṇāṃ ratnānāṃ ca āgamaḥ yatra .

061.12F: vārāṅganeva nṛpanītiranekarūpā .. 181..
061.12A: vārāṅganā iva nṛpanītiḥ anekarūpā .. 181..
061.12P: vārāṅganā -- veśyā .

061.11-12E: ever spending and yet getting money and jewels in plenty -- royal policy, like a harlot, puts on a variety of forms.

061.13F: iti damanakena saṃtoṣitaḥ piṅgalakaḥ svāṃ prakṛtimāpannaḥ
061.13A: iti damanakena saṃtoṣitaḥ piṅgalakaḥ svām prakṛtim āpannaḥ

061.14F: siṃhāsane upaviṣṭaḥ . damanakaḥ prahṛṣṭamanāḥ vijayatāṃ
061.14A: siṃhāsane upaviṣṭaḥ . damanakaḥ prahṛṣṭamanāḥ vijayatām

061.15F: mahārājaḥ śubhamastu sarvajagatām ityuktvā yathāsukhamavasthitaḥ .
061.15A: mahārājaḥ śubham astu sarvajagatām iti uktvā yathāsukham avasthitaḥ .

061.13-15E: Thus consoled by Damanaka, Pingalaka regained his natural equanimity and sat on the throne. Damanaka, delighted at heart, said -- Victory to the king! May the worlds be happy! and lived in happiness according to his wishes.

061.16F: viṣṇuśarmovāca -- suhṛdbhedaḥ śrutastāvadbhavadbhiḥ .

061.16-18E: Vishnuskarma said -- You have heard the separation of Friends! The Princes replied-- Yes, we have by your favour, and have been happy. Vishnusharma said -- Let there be this much in addition --

061.19-20E: As for the separation of friends, let it be in the house of your enemies; let villains being drawn away by the god of death meet with destruction day by day;

061.21F: jano nityaṃ bhūyātsakalasukhasampattivasatiḥ

061.21-22E:  may the people ever be the asylum of prosperity and happiness of every kind; and let young boys always sport in the delightful garden of stories.

061.23-23E: Chapter III. WAR.

061.24F: punaḥ kathārambhakāle rājaputrairuktam . ārya

061.24-25E: At the time of narrating the stories again, the princes said -- Venerable Sir, we are princes. We have, therefore, a curiosity to hear about War.

061.26F: viṣṇuśarmaṇoktam -- yadeva bhavadbhyo rocate

061.26-27E:  Vishnusharma said I will relate just what your honours like. Do you hear about (the subject of) War then, of which this is the first Sloka --

061.28F: haṃsaiḥ saha mayūrāṇāṃ vigrahe tulyavikrame .

061.29F: viśvāsya vañcitā haṃsāḥ kākaiḥ sthitvārimandire .. 1..
; viSvAsya? should it be viSvAsyaH ?
061.29A: viśvāsya vañcitāḥ haṃsāḥ kākaiḥ sthitvā arimandire .. 1..

061.28-29E: In the combat between the swans and the peacocks, in which equal valour was displayed, the swans were deceived, their confidence being gained by the crows, having resided in the enemy's house.

062.01F: rājaputrā ūcuḥ -- kathametat . viṣṇuśarmā kathayati --
062.01A: rājaputrāḥ ūcuḥ -- katham etat . viṣṇuśarmā kathayati --

062.02F: asti karpūradvīpe padmakelināmadheyaṃ saraḥ . tatra hiraṇyagarbho nāma
; karpUradvIpa : island of karpUra
062.02A: asti karpūradvīpe padmakelināmadheyam saraḥ . tatra hiraṇyagarbhaḥ nāma

062.03A: rājahaṃsaḥ prativasati . saḥ ca sarvaiḥ jalacarapakṣibhiḥ militvā

062.04F: pakṣirājye'bhiṣiktaḥ . yataḥ .
062.04A: pakṣirājye abhiṣiktaḥ . yataḥ .

062.01-04E: The princes asked -- How was that? Vishnusharma related as follows -- There is, in Karpuradvipa, a lake, known as Padmakeli. In it dwelt a royal swan, Hiranyagarbha by name. He was installed their king by all the aquatic birds having assembled together. For,

062.05F: yadi na syānnarapatiḥ samyaṅnetā tataḥ prajā .
062.05A: yadi na syāt narapatiḥ samyak netā tataḥ prajā .

062.06F: akarṇadhārā jaladhau viplaveteha nauriva .. 2..
062.06A: akarṇadhārā jaladhau viplaveta iha nauḥ iva .. 2..
062.06P: akarṇadhārā nāsti karṇadhāraḥ nāvikaḥ yasyāḥ sā .
062.06P+: viplaveta -- nāśamāpnuyāt . kāmandakanī 1.10.

062.05-06E: If there be no king to guide the subjects properly, they would sink (in misery) in this world, like a boat without a helmsman in the sea.

062.07F: aparaṃ ca . prajāṃ saṃrakṣati nṛpaḥ sā vardhayati pārthivam .
062.07A: aparam ca . prajām saṃrakṣati nṛpaḥ sā vardhayati pārthivam .

062.08F: vardhanādrakṣaṇaṃ śreyastadabhāve sadapyasat .. 3..
062.08A: vardhanāt rakṣaṇam śreyas tat abhāve sat api asat .. 3..
062.08P: vardhanāditi -- prajākṛtarājavardhanādrājakṛtaprajārakṣaṇaṃ śreyaḥ pradhānam .
062.08P+: yataḥ rakṣaṇābhāve sadapi vidyamānamapi vastu asadavidyamānamiva bhavati . apahāraśaṅkayeti bhāvaḥ .

062.07-08E: Moreover, The king protects the subjects; they enrich the king: protection is better than enrichment: for in its absence, even what is, is not (i.e, no property is secure).

062.09F: ekadāsau rājahaṃsaḥ suvistīrṇakamalaparyaṅke sukhāsīnaḥ
062.09A: ekadā asau rājahaṃsaḥ suvistīrṇakamalaparyaṅke sukhāsīnaḥ
062.09P: suvistīrṇa -- suvistīrṇaḥ kamalaghaṭitaḥ paryaṃkaḥ siṃhāsanaṃ suvistīrṇaṃ kamalameva paryaṃkaḥ iti vā tasmin .

062.10F: parivāraparivṛtastiṣṭhati . tataḥ kutaściddeśādāgatya
062.10A: parivāraparivṛtaḥ tiṣṭhati . tataḥ kutaḥ cit deśāt āgatya

062.11F: dīrghamukho nāma bakaḥ praṇamyopaviṣṭaḥ . rājovāca -- dīrghamukha .
062.11A: dīrghamukhaḥ nāma bakaḥ praṇamya upaviṣṭaḥ . rājā uvāca -- dīrghamukha .

062.09-11E: One day that royal swan was sitting at ease on a large lotus-couch surrounded by his retinue, when a crane, Dirghamukha by name, coming from some country, made his obeisance and sat down. Dirghamukha, said the king,

062.12F: daśāntarādāgato'si . vārtāṃ kathaya . sa brūte -- deva asti
062.12A: daśāntarāt āgataḥ asi . vārtām kathaya . saḥ brūte -- deva asti

062.13F: mahatī vārttā . tāmākhyātukāma eva satvaramāgato'ham . śrūyatām . 
062.13A: mahatī vārttā . tām ākhyātukāmaḥ eva satvaram āgataḥ aham . śrūyatām .
; vArttA (Kale has vArtA)
062.13P: ākhyātukāmaḥ -- ākhyātuṃ kāmaḥ yasya . 'tuṃkāmamanasorapi' iti vacanāt makāralopaḥ .

062.12-13E: you have come from a foreign country. Tell us the news. The crane replied, sire, there is great news and I have hastened here to communicate that. May Your Highness listen.

062.14F: asti jambūdvīpe vindhyo nāma giriḥ . tatra citravarṇo nāma mayūraḥ pakṣirājo

062.16F: carannavalokitaḥ . pṛṣṭaśca -- kastvam . kutaḥ samāgato'si .
062.16A: caran avalokitaḥ . pṛṣṭaḥ ca -- kaḥ tvam . kutaḥ samāgataḥ asi .

062.14-16E: There is a mountain, Vindhya by name, in Jambudvipa, where lives a peacock, Chitravarna by name, king of birds. While roaming in Dagdharanya, I was observed by his attendant birds and asked -- Who are you and where have you come from?

062.17F: tadā mayoktam -- karpūradvīpasya rājacakravartino hiraṇyagarbhasya
062.17A: tadā mayā uktam -- karpūradvīpasya rājacakravartinaḥ hiraṇyagarbhasya

062.18F: rājahaṃsasyānucaro'haṃ . kautukāddeśāntaraṃ draṣṭumāgato'smi .
062.18A: rājahaṃsasya anucaraḥ ahaṃ . kautukāt deśāntaram draṣṭum āgataḥ asmi .

062.17-18E: Whereupon I replied -- I am a follower of his Imperial Majesty, the royal swan, Hiranyagarbha, king of Karpuradvipa and have come here out of curiosity to see foreign countries.

062.19F: etacchrutvā pakṣibhiruktam -- anayordeśayoḥ ko deśo bhadrataro
062.19A: etat śrutvā pakṣibhiḥ uktam -- anayoḥ deśayoḥ kaḥ deśaḥ bhadrataraḥ
062.19P: bhadrataraḥ -- anyāpekṣayā śreṣṭhataraḥ . rājā ca bhadrataraḥ .

062.20F: rājā ca . mayoktam -- āḥ kimevamucyate -- mahadantaram .
062.20A: rājā ca . mayā uktam -- āḥ kim evam ucyate -- mahat antaram .

062.19-20E: On hearing this, the birds asked me -- Which of the two countries and kings you think to be the better? I replied -- Why is the question necessary? Great is the difference.

062.21F: yataḥ karpūradvīpaḥ svarga eva rājahaṃsaśca dvitīyaḥ svargapatiḥ .
062.21A: yataḥ karpūradvīpaḥ svargaḥ eva rājahaṃsaḥ ca dvitīyaḥ svargapatiḥ .

062.22F: atra marusthale patitā yūyaṃ kiṃ kurutha .
062.22A: atra marusthale patitāḥ yūyam kim kurutha .
062.22P: marusthale dhanvabhūmau nirjalapradeśe . 'samānau marundhavānau' ityamaraḥ . marubhūmivat nisargasaundaryahīne rūkṣapradeśe ityarthaḥ .
062.22P+: yūyaṃ kiṃ kurutha yūyaṃ duḥkhabhāgina eva ityarthaḥ .

062.21-22E: Karpuradvipa is heaven itself, while the royal swan is the second lord of heaven. Condemned to this desolate place, what do you do here?

062.23F: āgacchatāsmaddeśo gamyatām .

062.24F: tato'smadvacanamākarṇya sarve sakopā babhūvuḥ .
062.24A: tataḥ asmadvacanam ākarṇya sarve sakopāḥ babhūvuḥ .

062.23-24E: Come away; let us go to our country. Then on hearing my words all flew into a passion.

062.25F: tathā coktam --
062.25A: tathā ca uktam --

062.26F: payaḥpānaṃ bhujaṅgānāṃ kevalaṃ viṣavardhanam .
062.26A: payaḥpānam bhujaṅgānām kevalam viṣavardhanam .
062.26P: viṣavardhanaṃ -- śarīrapoṣaṇena viṣopacayāditi bhāvaḥ .

062.27F: upadeśo hi mūrkhāṇāṃ prakopāya na śāntaye .. 4..

062.27P:  prakopāya -- prakopajananārtham .

062.25-27E: For, To feed serpents on milk is simply to add to their poison : advice given to fools leads to provocation and not to satisfaction.

062.28F: anyacca . vidvānevopadeṣṭavyo nāvidvāṃstu kadācana .
062.28A: anyat ca . vidvān eva upadeṣṭavyaḥ na avidvān tu kadācana .

062.29F: vānarānupadiśyātha sthānabhraṣṭā yayuḥ khagāḥ .. 5..
062.29A: vānarān upadiśya atha sthānabhraṣṭāḥ yayuḥ khagāḥ .. 5..

062.28-29E: Moreover, A learned man only should be advised, and never an illiterate one; for having offered advice to monkeys, the birds had to go away being deprived of their place of abode.

062.30F: rājovāca -- kathametat .
062.30A: rājā uvāca -- katham etat .

062.33-34E: There is a large Salmali tree on the bank of the Narmada, in the vicinity of a hill. There, in the interiors of nests built by themselves lived certain birds in happiness even in the monsoons.

062.35-35E: Once in the rainy season, looking like so many dark veils,

063.09-11E: Thereafter, when the downpour of rain had stopped, the monkeys climbed up the tree, and smashed all the nests, so that the eggs of the birds fell down. Hence I say -- A learned man only should be advised &c.

062.12-13E: What did they do then? -- asked the king. The crane replied -- Then the birds said, in anger --

063.14-16E: Who made the royal swan king? Thereupon I too being irritated asked them -- By whom was your peacock made king? Hearing this they all became ready to kill me, whereupon I also displayed my valour.

'dhṛṣṭe dhṛṣṇurviyātaśca' ityamaraḥ . parākramaḥ pauruṣaṃ bhūṣyate'neneti bhūṣaṇamābharaṇam . iti śiśupālavadhe mallināthaḥ . yaḥ ātmanaḥ pareṣāṃ śatrūṇāṃ ca balābalaṃ sāmarthyāsāmarthyaṃ samīkṣya samyak paryālocya antaraṃ na jānāti ātmanaḥ balaṃ kiyat śatrūṇāṃ balaṃ kiyad iti na vicārayati sa śatrubhiḥ paribhūyate .

063.17-19E: For, On other occasions forbearance is an ornament to men as modesty is to women; but on the occasion of an insult a heroic action is an ornament as boldness (absence of modesty) is to a woman at the time of sexual enjoyment.

063.20-22E: The king smiled and observed -- He, who having well considered his own strength or weakness as well as that of his enamies is not at all able to mark the difference, is despised by the enemies.

063.28-30E: There lived, in Hastinapura, a washerman, Vilasa by name. His ass had become feeble on account of carrying burdens too heavy for him and was almost at the point of death. Thereapon the washerman, having wrapped him up in a tiger's skin, let him loose in a corn-field near a forest.

063.31F: tato dūrāt tamavalokya vyāghrabuddhyā kṣetrapatayaḥ satvaraṃ palāyante .

063.31-31E: Now the masters of the field seeing him from a distance used quickly run away taking him for a tiger.

064.01F: athaikadā kenāpi sasyarakṣakeṇa dhūsarakambalakṛtatanutrāṇena

064.01-02E: Then, one day, one of the men setting guard over the corn having protected his body with a dusky blanket and got a bow and arrow ready, remained waiting in a corner with his body bent down (in a bent posture).

064.03-04E: Seeing him from a distance the donkey who had grown stout and gained strength by eating corn at pleasure thought him to be a female ass and setting up a loud bray ran towards her.

064.05-07E: The corn-keeper knowing for certain from his braying that it was an ass killed him easily. Hence I say -- A stupid ass, that daily fed on corn &c. What next?

0564.08-09E: Dirghamukha replied -- Then the birds said -- Ah villain, vile crane, treading on our ground, thou revilest our lord !

064.10-11E: This cannot be borne now. With these words all of them pecked at me with their bills and said wrathfully -- Look here, thou blockhead, that swan, thy king, is extremely mild.

064.12F: tasya rājye'dhikāro eva nāsti . yata ekāntato mṛduḥ karatalagatamapyarthaṃ

064.13F: rakṣitumakṣamaḥ . kathaṃ sa pṛthivīṃ śāsti rājyaṃ vā tasya kim .

064.12-13E: He has no claim at all to sovereignty. For he who is all mildness is not able to save even the thing on the palm of his hand. How can he govern the earth then, or what is a kingdom to him?

064.14F: tvaṃ kūpamaṇḍūkastena tadāśrayamupadiśasi . śṛṇu .

064.14-14E: You too are a frog in a well (an inexperienced fellow) and hence you advise us to seek his shelter. Listen --

064.15F: sevitavyo mahāvṛkṣaḥ phalacchāyāsamanvitaḥ .

064.15-16E: A large tree, endowed with fruit and shade, should be resorted to: if, through ill luck, there be no fruit who can take off the shade?

064.17F: anyacca . hīnasevā na kartavyā kartavyo mahadāśrayaḥ .
064.17A: anyat ca . hīnasevā na kartavyā kartavyaḥ mahadāśrayaḥ .

064.18P+: vāruṇī surā .

064.17-18E: Moreover, A mean person should not be served; shelter should be taken with a great man; (for) even milk in the hands of a liquor-selling-woman is said to be (taken for) wine.

064.19F: anyacca . mahānapyalpatāṃ yāti nirguṇe guṇavistaraḥ .
064.19A: anyat ca . mahān api alpatām yāti nirguṇe guṇavistaraḥ .

064.20F: ādhārādheyabhāvena gajendra iva darpaṇe .. 12..
064.20A: ādhārādheyabhāvena gajendraḥ iva darpaṇe .. 12..
064.20P: ādhārādheyabhāvena -- biṃbakabiṃbitasaṃbandhena .

064.19-20E: The extent (lit, multitude) of merits, although great, shrinks into smallness when coming in contact with one void of merits, by the relation of the receiver and the received, like a large elephant in a mirror.

064.21F: viśeṣataśca . vyapadeśe'pi siddhiḥ syādatiśakte narādhipe .

064.22F: śaśino vyapadeśena śaśakāḥ sukhamāsate .. 13..
064.22A: śaśinaḥ vyapadeśena śaśakāḥ sukham āsate .. 13..

064.21-22E: Especially, When a king is very powerful, success can be obtained even by using a fiction: the hares lived happily by the fiction (fictitiously representing themselves as the servants) of the moon.

064.23-25E: I asked how it was; and the birds related -- FABLE III.

064.26F: kadācidvarṣāsvapi vṛṣṭerabhāvāt
064.26A: kadācit varṣāsu api vṛṣṭeḥ abhāvāt

064.29F: nimajjanābhāvādandhā iva . kva yāmaḥ kiṃ kurmaḥ .
064.29A: nimajjanābhāvāt andhāḥ iva . kva yāmaḥ kim kurmaḥ .

064.26-29E: Once upon a time, as there was no rain even in the rainy season, a herd of elephants, being oppressed with thirst, said to their chief-Lord, what means have we to save our lives? There is a place here (only) for little creatures to bathe; but for want of a bath we are as though blind; so whither can we go? What can we do?

064.30F: tato hastirājo
064.30A: tataḥ hastirājaḥ

064.30-32E: Thereupon the lord of the herd, going to a place not very far off, showed them a pond full of clear water. Then, as days passed on, the little hares that lived on its bank were crushed by the treadings of the elephants.

064.33-34E: Upon this a hare, Silimukha by name, thus deliberated. This herd of elephants, being troubled by thirst, must be coming here every day and thus our race is destroyed.

064.35-39E: Then a certain old hare, Vijaya by name, said -- Be not sorry. I will remedy this. He then set out, having undertaken to achieve that. On his way he reflected. How shall I stand before the herd of elephants and address them -- For,

065.01F: ato'haṃ parvataśikharamāruhya yūthanāthaṃ saṃvādayāmi .

066.25-27E: There is a large fig-tree in a forest bordering on the road leading to Ujjayini, upon which lived a goose and a crow. One day in the sultry season, a traveller, being fatigued, slept under the treo, having placed a bow and arrow by his side.

066.28-31E: After a short while the shadow of the tree moved away from his face. Then, seeing that his face was covered with the sun, a swan, that lived on the tree, through mercy, spread his wings and shaded his face again. Thereafter the traveller, happy in the enjoyment of sound sleep, yawned.

068.27P+: vijñasya prājñasya , paṇḍitasya .

068.28F: vinā hetumapi dvandvametanmūrkhasya lakṣaṇam .. 31..
068.28A: vinā hetum api dvandvam etat mūrkhasya lakṣaṇam .. 31..

067.27-28E: One should give a hundred but not quarrel — this is the opinion of the wise : but a strife without cause is the sign of the foolish.

068.29F: rājāha -- kimatītopālambhanena . prastutamanusaṃdhīyatām .
068.29A: rājā āha -- kim atītopālambhanena . prastutam anusaṃdhīyatām .

068.30F: cakravāko brūte -- deva vijane bravīmi . yataḥ .
068.30A: cakravākaḥ brūte -- deva vijane bravīmi . yataḥ .

068.29-30E: The king remarked -- What is the use of finding fault with the past? Let us attend to the matter in hand. Chakravaka -- My lord, I will speak in private. For,

068.31F: varṇākārapratidhvānairnetravaktravikārataḥ .
068.31A: varṇākārapratidhvānaiḥ netravaktravikārataḥ .
068.31P: varṇākāra -- varṇaḥ mukharāgaḥ .
068.31P+: ākāraḥ -- iṅgitam . 'ākārastviṅga iṅgitam' ityamaraḥ .

068.32F: apyūhanti mano dhīrāstasmādrahasi mantrayet .. 32..
068.32A: api ūhanti manaḥ dhīrāḥ tasmāt rahasi mantrayet .. 32..
068.32P: ūhanti tarkeṇa jānanti .
068.32P+: vijane -- rahasi

068.31-32E: The wise read the thoughts of others from complexion, outward features and the echo of voice, as also from the movements of the eyes and the mouth: one should, therefore, hold a consultation in private.

069.01F: rājā mantrī ca tatra sthitau . anye'nyatra
069.01A: rājā mantrī ca tatra sthitau . anye anyatra

069.02F: gatāḥ . cakravāko brūte -- deva ahamevaṃ jānāmi .
069.02A: gatāḥ . cakravākaḥ brūte -- deva aham evam jānāmi .

069.03F: kasyāpyasmanniyoginaḥ preraṇayā bakenedamanuṣṭhitam . yataḥ .
069.03A: kasya api asmat niyoginaḥ preraṇayā bakena idam anuṣṭhitam . yataḥ .

069.01-03E: The king and the minister remained there; the rest withdrew to other places. The Chakravaka spoke -- Sire, my idea is this -- The crane has done this at the instigation of some one of our officers. For,

069.04F: vaidyānāmāturaḥ śreyānvyasanī yo niyoginām .
069.04A: vaidyānām āturaḥ śreyān vyasanī yaḥ niyoginām .
069.04P: āturaḥ śreyān vaidyā arthalābhādāturaṃ bahu manyante iti bhāvaḥ .
069.04P+: āturaḥ rugṇaḥ .

069.05F: viduṣāṃ jīvanaṃ mūrkhaḥ sadvarṇo jīvanaṃ satām .. 33..
; sadvarRa : 'high caste'
069.05A: viduṣām jīvanam mūrkhaḥ sadvarṇaḥ jīvanam satām .. 33..

069.04-05E: A sick man is most welcome to physicians, and such is one who is vicious (or, one in trouble) to the officers of state: the clever prey upon fools, while one of a high caste is the life of the good.

069.06F: rājābravīt -- bhavatu kāraṇamatra
069.06A: rājā abravīt -- bhavatu kāraṇam atra

069.07F: paścānnirūpaṇīyam . samprati yatkartavyaṃ tan nirūpyatām .
069.07A: paścāt nirūpaṇīyam . samprati yat kartavyam tat nirūpyatām .

069.06-07E: The king remarked -- Be that as it may. The cause may be investigated afterwards. Just now let it be determined what steps we are to take.

069.08F: cakravāko brūte -- deva praṇidhistāvattatra
069.08A: cakravākaḥ brūte -- deva praṇidhiḥ tāvat tatra
069.08P: praṇidhiḥ cāraḥ . 'praṇidhiḥ prārthane care' ityamaraḥ .

069.09F: yātu . tatastadanuṣṭhānaṃ balābalaṃ ca jānīmaḥ . tathā hi .
069.09A: yātu . tataḥ tat anuṣṭhānam balābalam ca jānīmaḥ . tathā hi .
069.09P: anuṣṭhānaṃ vyavasāyam .

069.08-09E: Chakravaka -- My lord, let our spy first go there so that we may know of their doings as well as their strength and weaknees. For,

069.10F: bhavetsvapararāṣṭrāṇāṃ kāryākāryāvalokane .
069.10A: bhavet svapararāṣṭrāṇām kāryākāryāvalokane .

069.11F: cāraścakṣurmahībharturyasya nāstyandha eva saḥ .. 34..
069.11A: cāraḥ cakṣuḥ mahībhartuḥ yasya na asti andhaḥ eva saḥ .. 34..
069.11P: cāraḥ cakṣuḥ -- atra kāmandakaḥ 'gāvaḥ paśyanti gandhena vedaiḥ paśyanti ca dvijāḥ . cāraiḥ paśyanti rājānaścakṣuṣurbhyāmitare janāḥ .' iti . rāmāyaṇepi 'yasmatpaśyanti dūrasthāḥ sarvānarthānnarādhipāḥ . cāreṇa tasmāducyate rājānaścāracakṣuṣaḥ .' iti .

069.10-11E: A spy is the eye of a king in the determination of what policy to pursue or what to abandon with regard to his own kingdom or that of his enemies: he who has it not is quite blind.

069.12F: sa ca dvitīyaṃ viśvāsapātraṃ gṛhītvā yātu .
069.12A: saḥ ca dvitīyam viśvāsapātram gṛhītvā yātu .

069.13F: tenāsau svayaṃ tatrāvasthāya dvitīyaṃ tatratyamantrakāryaṃ
069.13A: tena asau svayam tatra avasthāya dvitīyam tatratyamantrakāryam
069.13P: tatratyamantrakāryam -- pararāṣṭrīyamantraṇāvyāpāram .

069.14F: sunibhṛtaṃ niścitya nigadya prasthāpayati . tathā coktaṃ --
069.14A: sunibhṛtam niścitya nigadya prasthāpayati . tathā ca uktam --
069.14P: sunibhṛtaṃ -- suguptam .
069.14P+: niścitya -- avadharya .

069.12-14E: Let him, too, take with him a second person worthy of confidence, so that himself staying there he might very secretly ascertain the secret measures adopted by the enemy there, and having communicated the same to him, would send him here. For it is said

069.15F: tīrthāśramasurasthāne śāstravijñānahetunā .
069.15A: tīrthāśramasurasthāne śāstravijñānahetunā .

069.16F: tapasvivyañjanopetaiḥ svacaraiḥ saha saṃvaset .. 5..
069.16A: tapasvivyañjanopetaiḥ svacaraiḥ saha saṃvaset .. 35..
069.16P: tapasvi -- tapasvināṃ vyañjanaṃ lakṣaṇaṃ veṣa iti yāvat tena upetaiḥ . varṇiliṅgigabhiḥ ityarthaṃ . 'sa varṇiliṅgī viditaḥ samayāyau' iti kirātārjunīye .
069.16P+: saṃvadet mantrayet . atra kāmandakaḥ -- 'cārānvicārayettīrthe ātmanaśca parasya ca . pāṣaṇḍādīnavijñātānanyonyamitarairapi' iti .

069.15-16E: (A king ) should hold discourse with his spies gathered under the disguise of ascetics at some holy place or a hermitage or a temple with the (outward) object of learning the truths of the sastras.

069.17F: gūḍhacāraśca yo jale sthale
069.17A: gūḍhacāraḥ ca yaḥ jale sthale
069.17P: gūḍhācāraḥ gūḍhaḥ cāraḥ yasya saḥ guptacaraḥ .

069.18F: carati . tato'sāveva bako niyujyatām . etādṛśa eva kaścid
069.18A: carati . tataḥ asau eva bakaḥ niyujyatām . etādṛśa eva kaḥ cid

069.19F: bako dvitīyatvena prayātu . tadgṛhalokāśca rājadvāre tiṣṭhatu . 
069.19A: bakaḥ dvitīyatvena prayātu . tadgṛhalokāḥ ca rājadvāre tiṣṭhatu . 
069.19P: tadgṛhalokaḥ -- tayoḥ bakayoḥ parivāraḥ .
069.19P+: tiṣṭhatu pratibhūtvena vartatām .

069.20F: kiṃtu deva etadapi suguptamanuṣṭhātavyam . yataḥ .
069.20A: kim tu deva etat api suguptam anuṣṭhātavyam . yataḥ .

069.17-20E: A secret spy is one who can move in water or on land. Let that very crane, therefore be appointed. Let some such other crane go with him as his companion; and let the members of their families stay at the royal gate.  But my lord, all thiş should be done, with the profoundest secrecy. For,

069.21F: ṣaṭkarṇo bhidyate mantrastathā prāptaśca vārtayā .
069.21A: ṣaṭkarṇaḥ bhidyate mantraḥ tathā prāptaḥ ca vārtayā .
069.21P: ṣaṭkarṇaḥ ṣaṭkarṇā yasya tṛtīyapuruṣagāmītyarthaḥ .
069.21P+: vārtayā prāptaḥ -- bahujanaśrutiviṣayībhūtaḥ .

069.22F: ityātmanā dvitīyena mantraḥ kāryo mahībhṛtā .. 36..
069.22A: iti ātmanā dvitīyena mantraḥ kāryaḥ mahībhṛtā .. 36..

069.21-22E: Counsel when reaching six ears (if heard by a third person) leaks out as well as that got by hearsay: wherefore a king should deliberate with himself as the second (i. e. with his minister alone).

069.23F: paśya . mantrabhede'pi ye doṣā bhavanti pṛthivīpateḥ .
069.23A: paśya . mantrabhede api ye doṣāḥ bhavanti pṛthivīpateḥ .
069.23P: doṣāḥ anarthāḥ aniṣṭāni .

069.24F: na śakyāste samādhātumiti nītividāṃ matam .. 37..
069.24A: na śakyāḥ te samādhātum iti nītividām matam .. 37..
069.24P: samādhātum pratikartum .

069.23-24E: Observe. The evils resulting to a king from his counsels getting out are not capable of being remedied -- such is the opinion of those who are versed in politics.

069.25F: rājā vimṛśyovāca -- prāptastāvanmayottamaḥ praṇidhiḥ .
069.25A: rājā vimṛśya uvāca -- prāptaḥ tāvat mayā uttamaḥ praṇidhiḥ .

069.26F: mantrī brūte -- tadā saṅgrāmavijayo'pi prāptaḥ .
069.26A: mantrī brūte -- tadā saṅgrāmavijayaḥ api prāptaḥ .

069.25-26E: The king after reflecting -- I have got the best emissary. The minister -- Then success in battle too is got.

069.27F: atrāntare pratīhāraḥ praviśya
069.27A: atra antare pratīhāraḥ praviśya

069.28F: praṇamyovāca deva -- jambudvīpādāgato dvāri śukastiṣṭhati .
069.28A: praṇamya uvāca deva -- jambudvīpāt āgataḥ dvāri śukaḥ tiṣṭhati .

069.29F: rājā cakravākamālokate . cakravākenoktam -- kṛtāvāse tāvadgatvā bhavatu . 
069.29A: rājā cakravākam ālokate . cakravākena uktam -- kṛtāvāse tāvat gatvā bhavatu . 
069.29P: cakravākamālokate -- kartavyanirdeśāpekṣayā tanmukhaṃ paśyatītyarthaḥ .
069.29P+: kṛtāvāse -- praṇidhyarthaṃ nirmite gṛhe .

069.27-29E: Just then the door-keeper, having entered, said after bowing -- Sire, a parrot who has come from Jambudvipa is waiting at the door. The king looked at Chakravaka. Chakravaka said -- let him first go to the residence prepared for him and wait there.

070.01F: paścādānīya draṣṭavyaḥ .
070.01A: paścāt ānīya draṣṭavyaḥ .

070.02F: pratīhārastamāvāsasthānaṃ nītvā gataḥ .
070.02A: pratīhāraḥ tam āvāsasthānam nītvā gataḥ .

070.01-02E: We shall send for him afterwards and grant him an interview. The door-keeper took the parrot to the residence and departed.

070.03F: rājāha -- vigrahastāvadupasthitaḥ .
070.03A: rājā āha -- vigrahaḥ tāvat upasthitaḥ .

070.04F: cakravāko brūte -- deva tathāpi sahasā vigraho na vidhiḥ . yataḥ .
070.04A: cakravākaḥ brūte -- deva tathā api sahasā vigrahaḥ na vidhiḥ . yataḥ .

070.03-04E: The king -- As for war it is imminent. Chakravaka -- Still to go to war all at once is no wise policy. For,

070.05F: sacivaḥ kiṃ sa mantrī vā ya ādāveva bhūpatim .
070.05A: sacivaḥ kim saḥ mantrī vā yaḥ ādau eva bhūpatim .

070.06F: yuddhodyogaṃ svabhūtyāgaṃ nirdiśatyavicāritam .. 38..
070.06A: yuddhodyogam svabhūtyāgam nirdiśati avicāritam .. 38..
070.06P: nirdiśati -- upadiśati .
070.06P+: avicāritam -- avicārya . ślo. 39-40. manu.a.sapta.ślo. 198-99 draṣṭavyau .

070.05-06E: Is he a servant or a counsellor, who, without due consideration, advises his sovereign at the outset to prepare for war or to quit his land?

070.07F: aparaṃ ca . vijetuṃ prayatetārīnna yuddhena kadācana .
070.07A: aparam ca . vijetum prayateta arīn na yuddhena kadācana .

070.08F: anityo vijayo yasmād dṛśyate yudhyamānayoḥ .. 39.
070.08A: anityaḥ vijayaḥ yasmāt dṛśyate yudhyamānayoḥ .. 39.

070.07-08E: Moreover, One should try to put down an enemy but never by means of fight: for victory in the case of combatants is always uncertain.

070.09F: anyacca . sāmnā dānena bhedena samastairathavā pṛthak .
070.09A: anyat ca . sāmnā dānena bhedena samastaiḥ athavā pṛthak .
070.09P: sāmnā -- priyavacanādinā krodhopaśamanaṃ sāma . tacca pañcavidham . taduktam -- 'parasparopakārāṇāṃ darśanaṃ guṇakīrtanam .saṃbandhasya samākhyānamāyatyāḥ saṃprakāśanam . vācā peśalayā sādhu tavāhamiti cārpaṇam . iti sāmavidhānajñaiḥ sāma pañcavidhaṃ smṛtam .'
070.09P+: dānamapi pañcavidham . taduktam -- 'pratidānaṃ tathā tasya gṛhītasyānumocanam . dravyādānamapūrvaṃ ca svayaṃ grāhapravartanam . deyasya pratimokṣaśca dānaṃ pañcavidhaṃ smṛtam .'
070.09P++: bhedaḥ -- śatroramātyādīnāmupāyena parato viśliṣyātmasātkaraṇaṃ bhedaḥ . sa trividhaḥ 'sneharāgāpanayanaṃ saṃharṣotpādanaṃ tathā . saṃtarjanaṃ ca bhedajñairbhedastu trividhaḥ smṛtaḥ .'

070.10F: sādhituṃ prayatetārīn na yuddhena kadācana .. 40..
070.10A: sādhitum prayateta arīn na yuddhena kadācana .. 40..
070.10P: sādhitum -- vaśīkartum .

070.09-10E: Again, One should strive to subdue an enemy by conciliatory means, by gifts, by (sowing seeds of) discord -- by all these simultaneously or singly -- but never by battle.

070.11F: yataḥ . sarva eva janaḥ śūro hyanāsāditavigrahaḥ .
070.11A: yataḥ . sarvaḥ eva janaḥ śūraḥ hi anāsāditavigrahaḥ .
070.11P: sarva eva -- apravṛtte samare sarva eva ātmanaḥ sauryaṃ prastautīti bhāvaḥ .

070.12F: adṛṣṭaparasāmarthyaḥ sadarpaḥ ko bhavenna hi .. 41..
070.12A: adṛṣṭaparasāmarthyaḥ sadarpaḥ kaḥ bhavet na hi .. 41..

070.11-12E: And further, Every man is a hero as long as not engaged in a fight: who will not be proud that has not yet experienced the strength of his enemy (or, of another)?

070.13F: kiṃ ca . na tathotthāpyate grāvā prāṇibhirdāruṇā yathā .
070.13A: kim ca . na tathotthāpyate grāvā prāṇibhiḥ dāruṇā yathā .
070.13P: dāruṇā yathā -- yathā grāvā uttolanadaṇḍena sahāyena sukhenaiva utthāpyate tathā prāṇibhiḥ kevalayā śaktyā na utthāpyate ityarthaḥ .

070.14F: alpopāyānmahāsiddhiretanmantraphalaṃ mahat .. 42..
070.14A: alpopāyāt mahāsiddhiḥ etat mantraphalam mahat .. 42..

070.13-14E: Moreover, A stone is not raised by men so easily as it is with a pole (serving as a lever); great success by trifling means is the great fruit of counsel.

070.15F: kiṃtu vigrahamupasthitaṃ vilokya vyavahriyatām . yataḥ .
070.15A: kim tu vigraham upasthitam vilokya vyavahriyatām . yataḥ .

070.15-15E: But seeing that war is at hand let the necessary steps be taken. For,

070.16F: yathā kālakṛtodyogāt kṛṣiḥ phalavatī bhavet .
070.16A: yathā kālakṛtodyogāt kṛṣiḥ phalavatī bhavet .

070.17F: tadvannītiriyaṃ deva cirāt phalati na kṣaṇāt .. 43..
070.17A: tadvat nītiḥ iyam deva cirāt phalati na kṣaṇāt .. 43..

070.16-17E: As husbandry becomes fruitful from labour spent upon it in due season, so, my lord, this policy (political measures) bears fruit after a long time (when the proper time comes), and not in a moment.

070.18F: aparaṃ ca . mahato dūrabhīrutvamāsanne śūratā guṇaḥ .
070.18A: aparam ca . mahataḥ dūrabhīrutvam āsanne śūratā guṇaḥ .
070.18P: dūrabhīrutvam -- mahān yāvadbhayamanāgataṃ tāvadbibhetīti bhāvaḥ .
070.18P+: āsanne bhayopasthitau . mitralābhe 57 ślo. draṣṭavyaḥ .

070.19F: vipattau hi mahāṃlloke dhīratāmadhigacchati .. 44..
070.19A: vipattau hi mahān loke dhīratām adhigacchati .. 44..

070.18-19E: Again Fearing a danger when at a distance but displaying bravery when it is at hand is a virtue that belongs to the great : a great man, in this world, conducts himself bravely in adversity.
; 12-22-2021 end.
070.20F: anyacca . pratyūhaḥ sarvasiddhīnāmuttāpaḥ prathamaḥ kila .
070.20A: anyat ca . pratyūhaḥ sarvasiddhīnām uttāpaḥ prathamaḥ kila .
070.20P: uttāpaḥ -- cittasaṃkṣobhajanitā naisargikadhairyacyutirityarthaḥ .

070.21F: atiśītalamapyambhaḥ kiṃ bhinatti na bhūbhṛtaḥ .. 45..
070.21A: atiśītalam api ambhaḥ kim bhinatti na bhūbhṛtaḥ .. 45..
070.21P: bhūbhṛtaḥ -- parvatān .
070.21P+: atiśītalami -- śāntacittatayā vyavaharatā vijayaḥ sukhaṃ labhyate iti bhāvaḥ .

070.20-21E: Also, Mental agitation is the first (greatest) obstacle to success of every kind: does not water, even though exceedingly cold, break through a mountain?

070.22F: viśeṣataśca deva mahābalo'sau citravarṇo rājā . yataḥ .
070.22A: viśeṣataḥ ca deva mahābalaḥ asau citravarṇaḥ rājā . yataḥ .

070.22-22E: More particularly because king Chitravarna is very powerful. For,

070.23F: balinā saha yoddhavyamiti nāsti nidarśanam .
070.23A: balinā saha yoddhavyam iti na asti nidarśanam .
070.23P: nidarśanam -- nītiśāstrājñā .

070.24F: tadyuddhaṃ hastinā sārdhaṃ narāṇāṃ mṛtyumāvahet .. 46..
070.24A: tat yuddham hastinā sārdham narāṇām mṛtyum āvahet .. 46..
070.24P: taditi -- yannarāṇāṃ ... tat .

070.23-24E: There is no ordinance to the affect that one should fight with the powerful: that fight which is between men and elephants must result in the destruction of the former.

071.01F: anyacca . sa mūrkhaḥ kālamaprāpya yo'pakartari vartate .
071.01A: anyat ca . saḥ mūrkhaḥ kālam aprāpya yaḥ apakartari vartate .
071.01P: apakartari vartate -- apakartari śatrau viṣaye vartate abhiyogaṃ kurute . yuddhodyoge pravartate ityarthaḥ .

071.02F: kalirbalavatā sārdhaṃ kīṭapakṣodgamo yathā .. 47..
071.02A: kaliḥ balavatā sārdham kīṭapakṣodgamaḥ yathā .. 47..
071.02P: kīṭasya pipīlikādeḥ pakṣodgamaḥ yathā tannāśāya bhavati tathā . pakṣodyama iti pāṭhe sa yathā akiṃcitkarastathā ityarthaḥ .

071.01-02E: Again, He is a fool who without getting the proper opportunity commences operations against his adversary: a strife with the powerful is like an insect getting wings (UAT v. l. like the exertions of an insect's wings, i. e. quite futile ).

071.03F: kiṃ ca . kaurmaṃ saṃkocamāsthāya prahāramapi marṣayet .
071.03A: kim ca . kaurmam saṃkocam āsthāya prahāram api marṣayet .

071.04F: prāptakāle tu nītijña uttiṣṭhetkrūrasarpavat .. 48..
071.04A: prāptakāle tu nītijñaḥ uttiṣṭhet krūrasarpavat .. 48..

071.03-04E:  Moreover, Having recourse to the tortoise's mode of contracting its body one should suffer even a blow: but when the right time comes, one, knowing the policy, should rise like a fierce cobra.

071.05F: śṛṇu deva . mahatyalpe'pyupāyajñaḥ samameva bhavet kṣamaḥ .
071.05A: śṛṇu deva . mahati alpe api upāyajñaḥ samam eva bhavet kṣamaḥ .

071.06F: samunmūlayituṃ vṛkṣāṃstṛṇānīva nadīrayaḥ .. 49..
071.06A: samunmūlayitum vṛkṣān tṛṇāni iva nadīrayaḥ .. 49..

071.05-06E: I invite your attention, my lord, to this, One who knows how to use the proper remedies is able to uproot the great and the small equally, as is the current of a river which sweeps away the trees and grass.

071.07F: atastaddūto'yaṃ
071.07A: ataḥ tat dūtaḥ ayam

071.08F: śuko'trāśvāsya tāvaddhriyatāṃ yāvaddurgaṃ sajjīkriyate . yataḥ .
071.08A: śukaḥ atra āśvāsya tāvat dhriyatām yāvat durgam sajjīkriyate . yataḥ .

071.07-08E: For this purpose, let this parrot, the enemy's emissary, be given assurances and detained here until the fortress is prepared. For, 

071.09F: ekaḥ śataṃ yodhayati prākārastho dhanurdharaḥ .
071.09A: ekaḥ śatam yodhayati prākārasthaḥ dhanurdharaḥ .
071.09P: eka iti - manuḥ 7.74 .

071.10F: śataṃ śatasahasrāṇi tasmād durgaṃ vidhīyate .. 50..
071.10A: śatam śatasahasrāṇi tasmāt durgam vidhīyate .. 50..
071.10P: vidhīyate -- kartavyatayā upadiśyate . durgavidhāne ca manuḥ -- 'dhanurdurgaṃ mahīdurgamabdurgaṃ vārkṣameva vā . nṛdurgaṃ giridurgaṃ vā samāśritya vasetpuram .' iti .

071.09-10E: A single bowman standing on the battlement can fight a hundred, and, a hundred a hundred thousand : hence a fortress is set down (* by writers of military science) as necessary.

071.11F: adurgoviṣayaḥ kasya nāreḥ paribhavāspadam .
071.11A: adurgaḥ viṣayaḥ kasya na areḥ paribhavāspadam .
071.11P: kasyāreḥ -- paṃcamarthe ṣaṣṭhī . rājño viṣayaḥ adurgaḥ syāccet kasmāt śatroḥ tasya parābhavaḥ na syāt . yadvā kasya viṣayaḥ iti yojanā . tadeva spaṣṭayati adurgaḥ rājā potacyutamanuṣyavad anāśrayaḥ nirālambaḥ mriyate ityarthaḥ .

071.12F: adurgo'nāśrayo rājā potacyutamanuṣyavat .. 51..
; pota: ship, cyuta: moved
071.12A: adurgaḥ anāśrayaḥ rājā potacyutamanuṣyavat .. 51..

071.11-12E: The territory of what king which is without strongholds is not liable to be conquered by the enemy? A king who has no fortress is helpless like a man fallen overboard.

071.13F: durgaṃ kuryān mahākhātamuccaprākārasaṃyutam .

071.14P: sayantram -- śatrupīḍanārthamiti bhāvaḥ .

071.13-14E: One should build a castle with a large trench, furnished with lofty battlements, having machines, and a good supply of water and situated in a place sarrounded by hills, rivers and deserts.

071.15-16E: Spaciousness, extreme difficulty of access (lit. ruggedness of the ground), a large store of water, grain and fuel and the means of ingress and egress -- these seven are the precious possessions of a fort.

071.17F: rājāha -- durgānusaṃdhāne ko niyujyatām .

071.18F: cakro brūte --
071.18A: cakraḥ brūte --

071.17-18E: The king -- Who should be entrusted with the work of getting the fortress ready? Chakravaka said --

071.19F: yo yatra kuśalaḥ kārye taṃ tatra viniyojayet .
071.19A: yaḥ yatra kuśalaḥ kārye tam tatra viniyojayet .

071.20F: karmasvadṛṣṭakarmā yaḥ śāstrajño'pi vimuhyati .. 54..

071.19-20E: One should employ a man in that business in which he is skilled. He who has no practical knowledge of a work gets bewildered (when set to it), although well versed in science.

071.21F: tadāhūyatāṃ sārasaḥ . tathānuṣṭhite satyāgataṃ sārasamālokya

071.21-22E: Let Sarasa be called then. That being done, when Sarasa came the king looked at him and said -- Sarasa, quickly attend to the fitting up of a fortress.

071.23F: sārasaḥ praṇamyovāca -- deva durgaṃ tāvadidameva cirāt
071.23A: sārasaḥ praṇamya uvāca -- deva durgam tāvat idam eva cirāt

071.24F: sunirūpitamāste mahatsaraḥ .
071.24A: sunirūpitam āste mahat saraḥ .

; maDyavartidvIpa middle-situated-island

071.23-25E: Sarasa replied after bowing -- As for a fortress, Sire, I have long well marked this large lake as such; only let a stock of provisions be ordered to be laid up in the island which is in its centre. For,

071.26F: dhānyānāṃ saṃgraho rājannuttamaḥ sarvasaṃgrahāt .
071.26A: dhānyānām saṃgrahaḥ rājan uttamaḥ sarvasaṃgrahāt .

071.27F: nikṣiptaṃ hi mukhe ratnaṃ na kuryātprāṇadhāraṇam .. 55..
071.27A: nikṣiptam hi mukhe ratnam na kuryāt prāṇadhāraṇam .. 55..
071.27P: nikṣiptamiti -- ratnaṃ dravyamityarthaḥ . kevalaṃ koṣasaṃvardhaṃ na kāryakaramiti bhāvaḥ .

071.26-27E: The store of grains, O king, is the best of all stores; because a jewel put into the mouth cannot support life.

072.01F: kiṃ ca . khyātaḥ sarvarasānāṃ hi lavaṇo rasa uttamaḥ .
072.01A: kim ca . khyātaḥ sarvarasānām hi lavaṇaḥ rasaḥ uttamaḥ .

072.02F: gṛhītaṃ ca vinā tena vyañjanaṃ gomayāyate .. 56..
072.02A: gṛhītam ca vinā tena vyañjanam gomayāyate .. 56..

072.01-02E: Moreover, Of all spiced things salt is known to be the best : for a condiment taken without it tastes like cowdung (is quite insipid).

072.03F: rājāha -- satvaraṃ gatvā sarvamanutiṣṭha .
072.03A: rājā āha -- satvaram gatvā sarvam anutiṣṭha .

072.03-03E: The king -- Go and attend to everything with despatch.

072.04F: punaḥ praviśya
072.04A: punaḥ praviśya

072.04-06E: The door-keeper having entered again -- Sire, a crow, Meghavarna (cloud-colour) by name, who has come from Ceylon, is waiting at the gate with his retinue and wishes to see Your Majesty's feet.

072.07F: rājāha --
072.07A: rājā āha --

072.07-08E:  The king -- A crow again knows everything and has a wide range of observation and is, for this reason, worthy of being retained.

072.09F: cakro brūte -- deva astyevaṃ . kiṃtu kākaḥ

072.11A: tathā ca uktam --

072.09-11E: Chakravaka observed -- Sire, this may be. But the crow is a land-bird and is consequently set on the side of our enemies. How should he be admitted, then? For it is said --

072.12F: ātmapakṣaṃ parityajya parapakṣeṣu yo rataḥ .

072.12-13E: That fool, who deserting his own side is attached to the enemy's party, is killed by the enemies, like the jackal with the blue colour.

072.14F: rājovāca -- kathametat .

072.14-16E: The king asked how it was. The minister related -- FABLE VII.

072.17F: astyaraṇye kaścicchṛgālaḥ svecchayā nagaropānte bhrāmyan nīlībhāṇḍe patitaḥ . 
072.17A: asti araṇye kaḥ cit śṛgālaḥ svecchayā nagaropānte bhrāmyan nīlībhāṇḍe patitaḥ .

072.18F: paścāttata utthātumasamarthaḥ prātarātmānaṃ mṛtavat saṃdarśya sthitaḥ . 
072.18A: paścāt tataḥ utthātum asamarthaḥ prātaḥ ātmānam mṛtavat saṃdarśya sthitaḥ . 

072.17-18E: A certain jackal that lived in a forest, fell, while wandering on the borders of a town, into an indigo-pot. Thereupon, not being able to get out of it, he feigned himself dead in the morning and so remained.

072.19F: atha nīlībhāṇḍasvāminā mṛta iti jñātvā
072.19A: atha nīlībhāṇḍasvāminā mṛtaḥ iti jñātvā

072.19-20E: Now the master of the indigo-pot, taking him to be dead, lifted him out of it, and carrying him to a distance, cast him off, whence he ran off.

072.21F: tato'sau vanaṃ gatvā svakīyamātmānaṃ nīlavarṇamavalokyācintayat --

072.22P: uttamavarṇaḥ -- svabhāvāpekṣayā sundaravarṇaḥ .

072.21-22E: Then on going into the forest, and finding himself turned blue, he thus meditated -- I have now got the best colour. Why should I not, then, secure my own exaltation?

072.23F: ityālocya
072.23A: iti ālocya

072.23-25E: Having thus cogitated he called together the jackals and said I am installed king of the forest by the revered goddess of the woods with her own hands being anointed with the juice of the sarvaushadhi.

072.26F: tadadyārabhyāraṇye'smadājñayā vyavahāraḥ kāryaḥ .

072.26-27E: Hence, from to-day all business should be carried on in the forest according to my orders. The jackals on their part, observing that he possessed the particular colour, prostrated themselves before him and said --

072.28F: yathājñāpayati deva iti anenaiva krameṇa

072.28-29E: It will be as Your Majesty commands. In the same way his sovereignty was gradually established over the other tenants of the forest.

072.30F: tatastena svajñātibhirāvṛtenādhikyaṃ sādhitam . tatastena vyāghrasiṃhādīn

072.30-33E: Thereafter being surrounded by his brethren he attained supreme power. After a while, having obtained servants of superior rank ench as the tiger, the lion and the like, he was ashamed to find the jackals in the court and discarded them with scorn. Then, finding the jackals dejected, an old jackal thus declared himself --

072.34F:  mā viṣīdata . yadanenānabhjñena
072.34A: mā viṣīdata . yat anena anabhijñena
072.34P: anabhijñena ātmano hitamajānatā .

072.35F: nītivido marmajñā vayaṃ svasamīpātparibhūtāstadyathāyaṃ naśyati tathā vidheyam . 
072.35A: nītividaḥ marmajñāḥ vayam svasamīpāt paribhūtāḥ tat yathā ayam naśyati tathā vidheyam .

072.34-35E: Do not be sorry. Since by him who does not know his interest, we, who are well versed in policy and know his weak points, have been dismissed from his presence, that must be done by which he will perish.

072.36F: yato'mī vyāghrādayo varṇamātravipralabdhāḥ

072.37F: śṛgālamajñātvā rājānamimaṃ manyante . 
072.37A: śṛgālam ajñātvā rājānam imam manyante . 

072.36-37E: For these (nobler animals) the tiger and others, deceived by him mere colour and not recognizing him as a jackal consider him their king.

072.38F: tadyathāyaṃ paricito bhavati tathā kuruta . tatra caivamanuṣṭheyam . 
072.38A: tat yathā ayam paricitaḥ bhavati tathā kuruta . tatra ca evam anuṣṭheyam . 

072.39F: yat sarve saṃdhyāsamaye tatsaṃnidhāne mahārāvamekadaiva kariṣyatha . 
072.39A: yat sarve saṃdhyāsamaye tat saṃnidhāne mahārāvam ekadā eva kariṣyatha . 

072.40F: tatastaṃ śabdamākarṇya jātisvabhāvāttenāpi śabdaḥ kartavyaḥ . yataḥ .
072.40A: tataḥ tam śabdam ākarṇya jātisvabhāvāt tena api śabdaḥ kartavyaḥ . yataḥ .

072.38-40E: Act, therefore, in such a way that he will be found out. To this end this should be done. That at the evening time you shall, all of you, set up a loud yell simultaneously in his hearing (lit. near him); so that on hearing that howl, he too following the natural disposition of his species, will utter a cry. For,

072.41F: yaḥ svabhāvo hi yasyāsti sa nityaṃ duratikramaḥ .
072.41A: yaḥ svabhāvaḥ hi yasya asti saḥ nityam duratikramaḥ .

072.42F: śvā yadi kriyate rājā tat kiṃ nāśnātyupānaham .. 58..
072.42A: śvā yadi kriyate rājā tat kim na aśnāti upānaham .. 58..

072.41-42E: That which is the natural disposition of one is always hard to be got rid of. If a dog were made a king would he not gnaw a shoe?

072.43F: tataḥ śabdādabhijñāya sa vyāghreṇa
072.43A: tataḥ śabdāt abhijñāya saḥ vyāghreṇa

072.44F: hantavyaḥ . tatastathānuṣṭhite sati tad vṛttam . tathā coktam --
072.44A: hantavyaḥ . tataḥ tathā anuṣṭhite sati tat vṛttam . tathā ca uktam --

072.43-44E: Upon this, being discovered by his voice he will be killed by the tiger. Then that being done that happened (i. e. the plan being put into execution the event turned out as anticipated). For it is said --

073.01F: chidraṃ marma ca vīryaṃ ca sarvaṃ vetti nijo ripuḥ .
073.01A: chidram marma ca vīryam ca sarvam vetti nijaḥ ripuḥ .
