073.01P+: marma -- rahasyam .
073.01P++: nijo ripuḥ -- sajātīyaḥ svapakṣāntargato va śatruḥ .

073.02F: dahatyantargataścaiva śuṣkaṃ vṛkṣamivānalaḥ .. 59..
073.02A: dahati antargataḥ ca eva śuṣkam vṛkṣam iva analaḥ .. 59..

073.03F: ato'haṃ bravīmi -- ātmapakṣaṃ parityajya ityādi .
073.03A: ataḥ aham bravīmi -- ātmapakṣam parityajya ityādi .

072.01-03E: An enemy of our own tribe knows our weak points, our secrets, our valour - our everything, and when such a one is in our midst he burns, as fire in the interior does a dry tree. I say, therefore, -- That fool who having left off his own side &c.

073.04F: rājāha -- yadyevaṃ tathāpi
073.04A: rājā āha -- yadi evam tathā api

073.05F: dṛśyatāṃ tāvadayaṃ dūrād āgataḥ . tatsaṃgrahe vicāraḥ kāryaḥ .
073.05A: dṛśyatām tāvat ayam dūrāt āgataḥ . tat saṃgrahe vicāraḥ kāryaḥ .

073.04-05E: The king -- Although this is the case, still he must be seen as he has come from a distance. We shall consider the question of his being retained here.

073.06F: cakro brūte -- deva praṇidhiḥ
073.06A: cakraḥ brūte -- deva praṇidhiḥ

073.07F: prahito durgśca sajjīkṛtaḥ . ataḥ śuko'pyālokya prasthāpyatām . kiṃ tu
073.07A: prahitaḥ durgaḥ ca sajjīkṛtaḥ . ataḥ śukaḥ api ālokya prasthāpyatām . kim tu .

073.06-07E: The minister -- Please Your Highness, the emissary has been sent and the castle put in readiness. Let the parrot, therefore, be granted an interview and dismissed. But,

073.08F: nandaṃ jaghāna cāṇakyastīkṣṇadūtaprayogataḥ .
073.08A: nandam jaghāna cāṇakyaḥ tīkṣṇadūtaprayogataḥ .
073.08P: cāṇakyaḥ -- tannāmā brāhmaṇaḥ candraguptasyāmātyaḥ .
073.08P+: tīkṣṇadūta -- prāṇaharasya dūtasya prayogataḥ viṣakanyāprayogeṇa iti yāvat .

073.09F: tacchūrāntaritaṃ dūtaṃ paśyeddhīrasamanvitaḥ .. 60..
073.09A: tat śūrāntaritam dūtam paśyet dhīra-samanvitaḥ .. 60..
073.09P: śūrāntaritam . dūtaviśeṣaṇaṃ kriyāviśeṣaṇaṃ vedam .
073.09P+: dhīrasamanvitaḥ -- nītikuśalaiḥ sahetyarthaḥ .

073.08-09E: Chanakya killed Nanda through the agency of a sharp spy: one should, therefore, see an emissary, accompanied by wise men and with brave men intervening.

073.10F: tataḥ sabhāṃ kṛtvāhūtaḥ śukaḥ kākaśca . śukaḥ kiṃcidunnataśirā
073.10A: tataḥ sabhām kṛtvā āhūtaḥ śukaḥ kākaḥ ca . śukaḥ kim cit unnataśirāḥ

073.11F: dattāsana upaviśya brūte -- bho hiraṇyagarbha tvāṃ mahārājādhirājaḥ
073.11A: dattāsane upaviśya brūte -- bho hiraṇyagarbha tvām mahārājādhirājaḥ

073.12F: śrīmaccitravarṇaḥ samājñāpayati . 
073.12A: śrīmat citravarṇaḥ samājñāpayati . 

073.10-12E: Thereafter a council being called, the parrot and the crow were sent for. The parrot, with his neck raised a little, sat on the seat that was offered him and said -- His Imperial Majesty, the great Chitravarna commands you --

073.13F: yadi jīvitena śriyā vā prayojanamasti tadā satvaramāgatyāsmaccaraṇau praṇama . 
073.13A: yadi jīvitena śriyā vā prayojanam asti tadā satvaram āgatya asmat caraṇau praṇama . 

073.14F: no ced avasthātuṃ sthānāntaraṃ cintaya .
073.14A: no ced avasthātum sthānāntaram cintaya .

073.13-14E: If you care anything for your life or wealth, come quickly and bow to our feet; or else think of some other place to live in.

073.15F: rājā sakopamāha -- āḥ
073.15A: rājā sakopam āha -- āḥ

073.16F: sabhāyāṃ ko'pyasmākaṃ nāsti ya enaṃ galahastayati . 
073.16A: sabhāyām kaḥ api asmākam na asti yaḥ enam galahastayati . 
073.16P: galahastayati -- galahastaṃ datvā niṣkāsayati .

073.15-16E: The king said in a rage -- Is there none among our servants here who will seize him by the neck (and turn him out)?

073.17F: utthāya meghavarṇo brūte -- deva ājñāpaya . hanmi duṣṭaṃ śukam .
073.17A: utthāya meghavarṇaḥ brūte -- deva ājñāpaya . hanmi duṣṭam śukam .

073.18F: sarvajño rājānaṃ
073.18A: sarvajñaḥ rājānam

073.19F: kākaṃ ca sāntvayanbrūte --  śṛṇu tāvat .
073.19A: kākam ca sāntvayan brūte -- śṛṇu tāvat .

073.17-19E: Meghavarna rising -- Sire, give but your command and I will kill the vile parrot. Sarvajna, having pacified the king and the crow, said -- Please listen --

073.20F: na sā sabhā yatra na santi vṛddhā vṛddhā na te ye na vadanti dharmam .
073.20A: na sā sabhā yatra na santi vṛddhāḥ vṛddhāḥ na te ye na vadanti dharmam .

073.21F: dharmaḥ sa no yatra na satyamasti satyaṃ na tadyacchalamabhyupaiti .. 61..
073.21A: dharmaḥ saḥ no yatra na satyam asti satyam na tat yat chalam abhyupaiti .. 61..
073.21P: chalamabhyupaiti -- kapaṭamāśrayate . yatkapaṭena saṃkīryate ityarthaḥ . bhayamiti pāṭhe prakāśaśaṅkāmityarthaḥ .

073.20-21E: That is not an assembly which has no old men in it; those are not old men who do not declare what is just. That is no justice which has no truth in it; and that is not truth which borders on (leaves room for, partakes of) fraud.

073.22F: yato dharmaścaiṣaḥ . dūto mleccho'pyavadhyaḥ syādrājā dūtamukho yataḥ .
073.22A: yataḥ dharmaḥ ca eṣaḥ . dūtaḥ mlecchaḥ api avadhyaḥ syāt rājā dūtamukhaḥ yataḥ .

073.23F: udyateṣvapi śastreṣu dūto vadati nānyathā .. 62..
073.23A: udyateṣu api śastreṣu dūtaḥ vadati na anyathā .. 62..

073.22-23E: And justice requires this -- A messenger, even though he be a Mlechchha (an out-caste) is exempt from being put to death; for a king has a messenger for his mouth (i.e. it is the king who speaks through his messenger). A messenger, does not speak otherwise (than directed) although weapons be raised against him.
; 12-25-2021
073.24F: aparaṃ ca . svāpakarṣaṃ parotkarṣaṃ dūtoktairmanyate tu kaḥ .
073.24A: aparam ca . svāpakarṣam parotkarṣam dūtoktaiḥ manyate tu kaḥ .

073.25F: sadaivāvadhyabhāvena dūtaḥ sarvaṃ hi jalpati .. 63..
073.25A: sadā eva avadhyabhāvena dūtaḥ sarvam hi jalpati .. 63..

073.24-25E: Moreover, Who believes in his own inferiority or his enemy's superiority from the words of a messenger? For, from his nature of not being punishable by death, a messenger speaks anything and everything.

073.26F: tato rājā kākaśca svāṃ
073.26A: tataḥ rājā kākaḥ ca svām

073.27F: prakṛtimāpannau . śuko'pyutthāya calitaḥ . paścāccakravākeṇānīya
073.27A: prakṛtim āpannau . śukaḥ api utthāya calitaḥ . paścāt cakravākeṇa ānīya
073.27P: prakṛtim -- svābhāvikamanaḥsvāsthyam .
073.27P+: āpannau prāptau .

073.28F: prabodhya kanakālaṅkārādikaṃ datvā saṃpreṣito yayau .
073.28A: prabodhya kanakālaṅkārādikam datvā saṃpreṣitaḥ yayau .
073.28P: prabodhya -- sarvaṃ vṛttāntaṃ yathāvadavagamayya , taṃ sāntvayitvā ityarthaḥ .

073.26-28E: On hearing this the king and the crow were pacified (lit. were themselves again). The parrot, too, got up and went away. He was, however, brought back by Chakravaka, and after matters had been explained to him, was presented with gold ornaments and the like and dismissed, upon which he departed.

073.29F: śuko'pi vindhyācalaṃ gatvā  rājānaṃ praṇatavān .
; vinDya+acala
073.29A: śukaḥ api vindhyācalam gatvā rājānam praṇatavān .

073.30F: tamālokya citravarṇo rājovāca -- śuka kā vārtā . kīdṛśo'sau deśaḥ .
073.30A: tam ālokya citravarṇaḥ rājā uvāca -- śuka kā vārtā . kīdṛśaḥ asau deśaḥ .

073.29-30E: The parrot having returned to the Vindhya mountain paid his respects to his sovereign. Seeing him the king Chitravarna asked him -- What is the news? What sort of country is that?

073.31F: śuko brūte -- deva saṃkṣepādiyaṃ vārtā . saṃprati yuddhodyogaḥ
073.31A: śukaḥ brūte -- deva saṃkṣepāt iyam vārtā . saṃprati yuddhodyogaḥ

073.32F: kriyatām . deśaścāsau karpūradvīpaḥ svargaikadeśaḥ
073.32A: kriyatām . deśaḥ ca asau karpūradvīpaḥ svargaikadeśaḥ

073.33F: kathaṃ varṇayituṃ śakyate . 
073.33A: katham varṇayitum śakyate . 

073.31-33E: The parrot replied -- Sire, in brief this is the news. Let preparations be made for war. As for the country of Karpuradvipa, it is (as it were) a part of heaven; how can it be possible to describe it?

073.34F: tataḥ sarvān śiṣṭānāhūya rājā mantrayitumupaviṣṭaḥ . āha ca -- saṃprati
073.34A: tataḥ sarvān śiṣṭān āhūya rājā mantrayitum upaviṣṭaḥ . āha ca -- saṃprati

073.35F: kartavyavigrahe yathākartavyamupadeśaṃ brūta . vigrahaḥ punaravaśyaṃ
073.35A: kartavyavigrahe yathākartavyam upadeśam brūta . vigrahaḥ punaḥ avaśyam

073.36F: kartavyaḥ . tathā coktam --
073.36A: kartavyaḥ . tathā ca uktam --

073.34-36E: The King, on hearing this, summoned all the principal persons together and sat down to deliberate with them. Said he -- With reference to the war presently to be carried on, advise me as to what is proper to be done. As for war it is absolutely determined upon. For it is said: --

073.37F: asaṃtuṣṭā dvijā naṣṭā saṃtuṣṭāśca mahībhujaḥ .
073.37A: asaṃtuṣṭāḥ dvijāḥ naṣṭāḥ saṃtuṣṭāḥ ca mahībhujaḥ .

073.38F: salajjā gaṇikā naṣṭā nirlajjāśca kulastriyaḥ .. 64..
; Kale typo? sallajjA -> salajjA

073.37-38E: Brahmanas are ruined when discontented, and kings when contented, a harlot full of modesty is ruined and so are ladies of family, if without modesty.

074.01F: dūradarśī nāma gṛdhro brūte --
074.01A: dūradarśī nāma gṛdhraḥ brūte --

074.02F: deva vyasanitayā vigraho na vidhiḥ . yataḥ .
074.02A: deva vyasanitayā vigrahaḥ na vidhiḥ . yataḥ .
074.02P: vyasanitayā -- vyasanamasyāstīti vyasanī tasya bhāvaḥ tattā tayā . vyasanābhibhūtaiḥ iti yāvat .

074.01-02E: The vulture named Duradarsi (Far-seeing) observed -- My lord it is not advisable to enter upon war under adverse circumstances. For,

074.03F: mitrāmātyasuhṛdvargā yadā syurdṛḍhabhaktayaḥ .
074.03A: mitrāmātyasuhṛdvargāḥ yadā syuḥ dṛḍhabhaktayaḥ .

074.04F: śatrūṇāṃ viparītāśca kartavyo vigrahastadā .. 65..
074.04A: śatrūṇām viparītāḥ ca kartavyaḥ vigrahaḥ tadā .. 65..
074.04P: śatrūṇām viparītāḥ -- teṣu adṛṣḍhabhaktayaḥ . araktā vā sukhabhedyā ityarthaḥ .

074.03-04E: When one's friends, ministers and allies are deeply attached, and of the enemy the reverse of this (i. e. disaffected with their sovereign), then only should war be made.

074.05F: anyacca . bhūmirmitraṃ hiraṇyaṃ ca vigrahasya phalaṃ trayam .
074.05A: anyat ca . bhūmiḥ mitram hiraṇyam ca vigrahasya phalam trayam .
074.05P: trayam -- etat trayaṃ vigrahasya phalam . yadaitanniyataṃ bhāvi tadā vigrahamācaret iti kāmandakanītisāre dvitīyacaraṇasya pāṭhaḥ .

074.06F: yadaitanniścitaṃ bhāvi kartavyo vigrahastadā .. 66..
; BAvi : inj-p 3s BU  OR? neut 1s of BAvin
074.06A: yadā etat niścitam bhāvi kartavyaḥ vigrahaḥ tadā .. 66..

074.05-06E: Moreover, (The acquisition of) land, an ally and gold -- these three are the benefits accruing from war; when these can be counted upon as sure then only war should be made.

074.07F: rājāha --
074.07A: rājā āha --

074.08F: mama balāni tāvadavalokayatu mantrī . tadaiteṣāmupayogo jñāyatām .
074.08A: mama balāni tāvat avalokayatu mantrī . tat eteṣām upayogaḥ jñāyatām .

074.09F: evamāhūyatāṃ mauhūrtikaḥ . nirṇīya śubhalagnaṃ yātrārthaṃ dadātu .
074.09A: evam āhūyatām mauhūrtikaḥ . nirṇīya śubhalagnam yātrārtham dadātu .
074.09P: mauhūrtikaḥ -- muhūrtaṃ adhikṛtya kṛtaṃ granthaṃ adhīte iti .
074.09P+: muhūrtajñaḥ -- jyautiṣikaḥ .
074.09P++: śubhalagnaṃ -- śubhaṃ śubhaphalapradaṃ lagnaṃ rāśīnāṃ udayaḥ .
074.09P+++: yātrārtham -- abhiyānārtham .

074.07-09E: The King observed -- Let the minister first inspect my forces, so that it may be known how far they will be useful. Similarly, let the astrologer be called who will determine and tell us the lucky time for starting.

074.10F: mantrī brūte --
074.10A: mantrī brūte --

074.11F: tathāpi sahasā yātrākaraṇamanucitam . yataḥ .
074.11A: tathā api sahasā yātrākaraṇam anucitam . yataḥ .

074.10-11E: The minister -- Still, to begin the expedition all at once is not advisable. For,

074.12F: viśanti sahasā mūḍhā ye vicārya dviṣadbalam .
; viSanti 3p viS
; dvizadbala: dvizat + bala : enemy + army
074.12A: viśanti sahasā mūḍhāḥ ye vicārya dviṣadbalam .

074.13F: khaḍgadhārāpariṣvaṅgaṃ labhante te suniścitam .. 67..
074.13A: khaḍgadhārāpariṣvaṅgam labhante te suniścitam .. 67..

074.12-13E: Those fools, who without taking counsel rashly enter into the enemy's army, are sure to get an embrace with the edges of their swords.

074.14F: rājāha -- mantrin mamotsāhabhaṅgaṃ sarvathā
074.14A: rājā āha -- mantrin mama utsāhabhaṅgam sarvathā

074.15F: mā kṛthāḥ . vijigīṣuryathā parabhūmimākramati tathā kathaya .

074.15P: vijigīṣuḥ -- vijetumicchuḥ .

074.14-15E: The king said -- Minister, do not at all damp my spirits. Tell me how one wishing for conquest invades his enemy's territory.

074.16F: gṛdhro brūte -- tatkathayāmi .
074.16A: gṛdhraḥ brūte -- tat kathayāmi .

074.17F: kiṃtu tadanuṣṭhitameva phalapradam . tathā coktam --
074.17A: kim tu tat anuṣṭhitam eva phalapradam . tathā ca uktam --

074.16-17E: The vulture replied I will tell you that. But it will yield fruit (prove beneficial) only if acted upon. For it is said --

074.18F: kiṃ mantreṇānanuṣṭhāne śāstravatpṛthivīpateḥ .
074.18A: kim mantreṇa ananuṣṭhāne śāstravat pṛthivīpateḥ .
074.18P: ananuṣṭhāne akaraṇe sati pṛthivīpateḥ mantreṇa kiṃ korthaḥ śāstravat . yathā prayogaṃ vinā kevalaṃ śāstrajñānam akiṃcitkaraṃ tathā kevalamantraṇayā rājñāṃ kāryaṃ na sidhyatītyarthaḥ . yadvā śāstravat yathāśāstramuktena mantreṇa kiṃ iti śāstravadananuṣṭhāne kimiti vā yojyam .

; Kale typo: hyozaDa -> hyOzaDa
074.19F: na hyauṣadhaparijñānādvyādheḥ śāntiḥ kvacid bhavet .. 68..
074.19A: na hi auṣadhaparijñānāt vyādheḥ śāntiḥ kvacit bhavet .. 68..

074.18-19E: What is the use of counsel given according to the Sastras (or, like the knowledge of the Sastras) to a king, if it be not acted upon? In no case can a disease be cured by the mere knowledge of medicine.

074.20F: rājādeśaścānatikramaṇīya iti yathāśrutaṃ nivedayāmi . śṛṇu .
074.20A: rājādeśaḥ ca anatikramaṇīya iti yathāśrutam nivedayāmi . śṛṇu .

074.20-20E: But as the command of a king is not to be transgressed, I will relate what I have learnt from the tests on the subject. Please to listen --

074.21F: nadyadrivanadurgeṣu yatra yatra bhayaṃ nṛpa .
074.21A: nadyadrivanadurgeṣu yatra yatra bhayam nṛpa .

074.22F: tatra tatra ca senānīryāyādvyūhīkṛtairbalaiḥ .. 69..
074.22A: tatra tatra ca senānīḥ yāyāt vyūhīkṛtaiḥ balaiḥ .. 69..
074.22P: vyūhīkṛtairbalaiḥ -- balāni vyūhīkṛtya ityarthaḥ .
074.22P+: vyūhaḥ -- senāvinyāsaḥ . vyūhaḥ syādbalavinyāse nirmāṇe vṛndatarkayoḥ . iti medinī . eteṣāṃ bhūyāṃsaḥ ślokāḥ kāmandakanītiśāstrādudhṛtāḥ .

074.21-22E: In rivers, mountains, wilds and difficult passes, wherever there is danger, O king, there the general should march with his forces drawn in battle-array.

074.23F: balādhyakṣaḥ puro yāyātpravīrapuruṣānvitaḥ .
074.23A: balādhyakṣaḥ puras yāyāt pravīrapuruṣānvitaḥ .
074.23P: balādhyakṣaḥ -- tattatsenāvibhāgasyādhyakṣaḥ .

074.24F: madhye kalatraṃ svāmī ca kośaḥ phalgu ca yad balam .. 70..
074.24A: madhye kalatram svāmī ca kośaḥ phalgu ca yat balam .. 70..
074.24P: kalatram -- strīvargaḥ .
074.24P+: phalgu -- kṣīṇasattvaṃ , nirarthakaḥ janasamudāyaśca . nāgānāṃ ca padātayaḥ ityatra cāṭavībalam iti kāmandakoktaḥ pāṭhaḥ .

074.23-24E: The commander of the forces should march in the van, accompained by the flower of the army; in the middle should be stationed the women, the king, the treasury and the unimportant sections of the army.

074.25F: pārśvayorubhayoraśvā aśvānāṃ pārśvato rathāḥ .
074.25A: pārśvayoḥ ubhayoḥ aśvāḥ aśvānām pārśvataḥ rathāḥ .

074.26F: rathānāṃ pārśvayornāgā nāgānāṃ ca padātayaḥ .. 71..
074.26A: rathānām pārśvayoḥ nāgāḥ nāgānām ca padātayaḥ .. 71..

074.25-26E: On each flank the horse; on the sides of the horse the chariots; on both sides of the chariots the elephants, and on the flanks of the elephants the foot-soldiers.

074.27F: paścātsenāpatiryāyātkhinnānāśvāsayañchanaiḥ .
074.27A: paścāt senāpatiḥ yāyāt khinnān āśvāsayan śanaiḥ .
074.27P: khinnān -- śrāntān sainikān .
074.27P+: āśvāsayan -- protsāhayan .

074.28F: mantribhiḥ subhaṭairyuktaḥ pratigṛhya balaṃ nṛpa .. 72..
074.28A: mantribhiḥ subhaṭaiḥ yuktaḥ pratigṛhya balam nṛpa .. 72..

074.27-28E: In the rear should slowly march, O king, the commander-in-chief, accompained by ministers and brave warriors, cheering those that are fatigued and backing the army.

075.01F: sameyādviṣamaṃ nāgairjalāḍhyaṃ samahīdharam .
075.01A: sameyāt viṣamam nāgaiḥ jalāḍhyam samahīdharam .
; sameyAt sam+A+i  opt. 3s
075.01P: viṣamaṃ i° -- pradeśaṃ  iti śeṣaḥ .

075.02F: samamaśvairjalaṃ naubhiḥ sarvatraiva padātibhiḥ .. 73..
075.02A: samam aśvaiḥ jalam naubhiḥ sarvatra eva padātibhiḥ .. 73..

075.01-02E: One should traverse uneven ground abounding in water and full of hills by means of elephants, plains by means of horses, and rivers by means of boats, while the infantry should be employed in all place.

075.03F: hastināṃ gamanaṃ proktaṃ praśastaṃ jaladāgame .
075.03A: hastinām gamanam proktam praśastam jaladāgame .
075.03P: hastināṃ -- gajasainikānām .

075.04F: tad anyatra turaṅgāṇāṃ pattīnāṃ sarvadaiva hi .. 74..
075.04A: tat anyatra turaṅgāṇām pattīnām sarvadā eva hi .. 74..

075.03-04E: A march with elephants is said to be advantageous at the approach of the rainy season, with the horse at other times, and with foot-soldiers in all seasons.

075.05F: śaileṣu durgamārgeṣu vidheyaṃ nṛparakṣaṇam .
075.05A: śaileṣu durgamārgeṣu vidheyam nṛparakṣaṇam .

075.06F: suyodhai rakṣitasyāpi śayanaṃ yoganidrayā .. 75..
075.06A: suyodhaiḥ rakṣitasya api śayanam yoganidrayā .. 75..
075.06P: śayanam yoganidrayā -- ardhaprabodhayuktanidrā yoganidrā tayā . nṛpaḥ suptopi sāvadhānaṃ varteta iti bhāvaḥ .

076.05-06E: In hills and difficult passes the king should be protected; and he should sleep wakefully even though guarded by brave men.

075.07F: nāśayet karṣayecchatrūndurgakaṇṭakamardanaiḥ .
075.07A: nāśayet karṣayet śatrūn durgakaṇṭakamardanaiḥ .
075.07P: karṣayet -- kleśayet .
075.07P+: durgakaṇṭakamardanaiḥ -- durgakaṇṭakeṣu saṃkaṭamārgeṣu mardanaiḥ nāśanaiḥ .

075.08F: paradeśapraveśe ca kuryādāṭavikānpuraḥ .. 76..
075.08A: paradeśapraveśe ca kuryāt āṭavikān puraḥ .. 76..

075.07-08E: One should destroy and harass the enemy by hard-pressing him in difficult places; and at the time of entering into the enemy's country, the foresters should be placed foremost.

075.09F: yatra rājā tatra kośo vinā kośānna rājatā .
075.09A: yatra rājā tatra kośaḥ vinā kośāt na rājatā .

075.10F: svabhṛtyebhyastato dadyātko hi dāturna yudhyate .. 77..
075.10A: svabhṛtyebhyaḥ tataḥ dadyāt kaḥ hi dātuḥ na yudhyate .. 77..

075.10P: ko hi dātuḥ na yudhyate -- yaḥ nṛpaḥ dravyadānena suyodhān toṣayati tadarthaṃ ko na yudhyate . sarva eva yudhyate iti bhāvaḥ . atra bṛhaspatiḥ -- niyuktaḥ karmaniṣpattau vijñaptau ca yadṛcchayā . bhṛtyāndhanairmānayaṃstu navopyakṣobhyatāṃ vrajet . iti .

076.09-10E: Where the king is, there the treasure should also be; without the treasure there can be no royalty: from it (the treasure) the king should make payments to his servants: for who does not fight for one who gives (freely)?

075.11F: yataḥ . na narasya naro dāso dāsastvarthasya bhūpate .
075.11A: yataḥ . na narasya naraḥ dāsaḥ dāsaḥ tu arthasya bhūpate .

075.12F: gauravaṃ lāghavaṃ vāpi dhanādhananibandhanam .. 78..
075.12A: gauravam lāghavam vā api dhanādhananibandhanam .. 78..
075.12P: dhanādhananibandhanam -- dhanādhananiṣṭam .

075.11-12E: For, Man is not the servant of men, O king, but he is the servant of money. Greatness or littleness too depends on the possession or absence of wealth.

075.13F: abhedena ca yudhyeran rakṣeyuśca parasparam .
075.13A: abhedena ca yudhyeran rakṣeyuḥ ca parasparam .
075.13P: abhedena -- aikyena , parasparāviyogena .

075.14F: phalgu sainyaṃ ca yatkiṃcinmadhye vyūhasya kārayet .. 79..
075.14A: phalgu sainyam ca yat kim cit madhye vyūhasya kārayet .. 79..

075.13-14E: They (the warriors) should fight in a compact body and defend one another; and whatever worthless portion of the army there may be should be placed in the middle of the column.

075.15F: padātīṃśca mahīpālaḥ puro'nīkasya yojayet .
075.15A: padātīn ca mahīpālaḥ puraḥ anīkasya yojayet .

075.15P: anīkasya -- sainyasya . anīkaṃ tu raṇe sainye iti viśvaḥ .

075.16F: uparudhyārimāsīta rāṣṭraṃ cāsyopapīḍayet .. 80..
; AsIta: opt-2m 3s As
075.16A: uparudhya arim āsīta rāṣṭram ca asya upapīḍayet .. 80..

075.15-16E: A king should place the infantry in the front of the army (or, send the infantry ahead of the army); he should wait having blocked up the enemy and also harass his country.

075.17F: syandanāśvaiḥ same yudhyedanūpe naudvipaistathā .
075.17A: syandanāśvaiḥ same yudhyet anūpe naudvipaiḥ tathā .
075.17P: anūpe jalaprāyadeśe . anūpo mahiṣe nāmbuprāyadeśe tu vācyavat . iti medinī .

075.18F: vṛkṣagulmāvṛte cāpairasicarmāyudhaiḥ sthale .. 81..
075.18A: vṛkṣagulmāvṛte cāpaiḥ asicarmāyudhaiḥ sthale .. 81..

075.17-18E: Upon even ground he should fight with chariots and horses; in a place overflowing with water with boats and elephants; in a place covered with trees and shrubs, with bows; and on open land with swords, shields and other weapons.

075.19F: dūṣayeccāsya satataṃ yavasānnodakendhanam .
075.19A: dūṣayet ca asya satatam yavasānnodakendhanam .
; dUzayet: (Huet) duz: ca. opt. ac. sg. 3
; yavasAnnodakenDanam : yavasa+anna+udaka+inDana
075.19P: dūṣayet -- nāśayet , anupayogi vā kuryāt .
075.19P+: yavasaḥ -- ghāsaḥ .

075.20F: bhindyāccaiva taḍāgāni prākārān parikhāstathā .. 82..
075.20A: bhindyāt ca eva taḍāgāni prākārān parikhāḥ tathā .. 82..

075.19-20E: He should ever and anon spoil his (enemy's) fodder, food, water and firewood; and demolish his tanks, ramparts and ditches.

075.21F: baleṣu pramukho hastī na tathānyo mahīpateḥ .
075.21A: baleṣu pramukhaḥ hastī na tathā anyaḥ mahīpateḥ .

075.22F: nijairavayavaireva mātaṅgo'ṣṭāyudhaḥ smṛtaḥ .. 83..
075.22A: nijaiḥ avayavaiḥ eva mātaṅgaḥ aṣṭāyudhaḥ smṛtaḥ .. 83..

075.21-22E: The elephant forms the chief factor in a king's army: there is none other like him, because the elephant is said to possess eight weapons in his very limbs.

075.23F: balamaśvaśca sainyānāṃ prākāro jaṅgamo yataḥ .
075.23A: balam aśvaḥ ca sainyānām prākāraḥ jaṅgamaḥ yataḥ .
075.23P: balamaśvaśca -- aśvaḥ sainyānāṃ balaṃ mukhyādhāraḥ yataḥ jaṃgamaḥ prākāraḥ .

075.24F: tasmādaśvādhiko rājā vijayī sthalavigrahe .. 84..
075.24A: tasmāt aśvādhikaḥ rājā vijayī sthalavigrahe .. 84..

075.23-24E: The cavalry is the strength of the army inasmuch as it forms a moving bulwark; a king, therefore, who is rich in cavalry, is victorious in a land-fight.

075.25F: tathā coktam . yudhyamānā hayārūḍhā devānāmapi durjayāḥ .
075.25A: tathā ca uktam . yudhyamānāḥ hayārūḍhāḥ devānām api durjayāḥ .

075.26F: api dūrasthitāsteṣāṃ vairiṇo hastavartinaḥ .. 85..
075.26A: api dūrasthitāḥ teṣām vairiṇaḥ hastavartinaḥ .. 85..

075.25-26E: For it is said -- Warriors fighting on horseback are difficult to be conquered even by the gods; the enemies, even though stationed at a distance, are (as it were) in their hands.
; 12-26-2021
075.27F: prathamaṃ yuddhakāritvaṃ samastabalapālanam .
075.27A: prathamam yuddhakāritvam samastabalapālanam .
075.27P: yuddhakāritvaṃ -- yodhakāryam . yuddhena śatrunirodha ityarthaḥ .

075.28F: diṅmārgāṇāṃ viśodhitvaṃ pattikarma pracakṣate .. 86..
075.28A: diṅmārgāṇām viśodhitvam pattikarma pracakṣate .. 86..

075.27-28E: Striking the first blow in a battle, taking care of the whole army, and the clearing of roads in all directions -- (these three) they say, form the duty of the infantry.

076.01F: svabhāvaśūramastrajñamaviraktaṃ jitaśramam .
076.01A: svabhāvaśūram astrajñam aviraktam jitaśramam .
076.01P: aviraktaṃ -- svasvāmini dṛḍhabhaktimat .

076.02F: prasiddhakṣatriyaprāyaṃ balaṃ śreṣṭhatamaṃ viduḥ .. 87..
076.02A: prasiddhakṣatriyaprāyam balam śreṣṭhatamam viduḥ .. 87..

076.01-02E: That army they declare to be the best, the soldiers in which are naturally brave, skilled in the use of weapons, loyal (lit. attached to their master), inured to fatigue and mostly drawn from the ranks of renowned Kshatriyas.

076.03F: yathā prabhukṛtānmānādyudhyante bhuvi mānavāḥ .
076.03A: yathā prabhukṛtāt mānāt yudhyante bhuvi mānavāḥ .

076.04F: na tathā bahubhirdattairdraviṇairapi bhūpate .. 88..
076.04A: na tathā bahubhiḥ dattaiḥ draviṇaiḥ api bhūpate .. 88..

076.03-04E: As men fight in this world, O king, by honour being shown to them by their lord, so they do not, even by large sums of money being given to them.

076.05F: varamalpabalaṃ sāraṃ na kuryānmuṇḍamaṇḍalīm .
076.05A: varam alpabalam sāram na kuryāt muṇḍamaṇḍalīm .
076.05P: varamiti -- sāraṃ śauryadhairyādiguṇavat alpabalaṃ kṣudrasaṃkhyākamapi balaṃ varaṃ .
076.05P+: muṇḍamaṇḍalī śiraḥparamparā kevalaṃ saṃkhyāpūrakā narā iti yāvat .

076.06F: kuryādasārabhaṅgo hi sārabhaṅgamapi sphuṭam .. 89..
076.06A: kuryāt asārabhaṅgaḥ hi sārabhaṅgam api sphuṭam .. 89..
076.06P: bhaṅgaḥ -- parājayaḥ palāyanaṃ vā .
076.06P+: sphuṭam , spaṣṭaṃ , asaṃśayam .
076.06P++: hi -- hetau niścaye vā .

076.05-06E: It is better to have a small army of chosen men than a multitude of heads: for the defeat of the weak will evidently lead to that of the strong.

076.07F: aprasādo'nadhiṣṭhānaṃ deyāṃśaharaṇaṃ ca yat .
076.07A: aprasādaḥ anadhiṣṭhānam deyāṃśaharaṇam ca yat .
076.07P: aprasādaḥ -- prasādakaraṇavaimukhyaṃ , apuraskāradānamityarthaḥ .
076.07P+: anadhiṣṭhānam -- balavibhāgādīnāmadhyakṣādipadālābhaḥ , adhikārapadāt cyutirvā .
076.07P++: deyāṃśaharaṇaṃ -- deyasya dānocitasya aṃśasya loptrāṃśasya haraṇaṃ ādānamātmasātkaraṇamityarthaḥ .

076.08F: kālayāpo'pratīkārastadvairāgyasya kāraṇam .. 90..
076.08A: kālayāpaḥ apratīkāraḥ tat vairāgyasya kāraṇam .. 90..
076.08P: kālayāpaḥ -- aniyogena vṛthā kālapekṣaḥ .
076.08P+: apratīkāraḥ -- kṛtamānabhaṅgāderaniryātanaṃ , apakārāśodhanam .
076.08P++: vairāgyasya -- sainikānāmiti śeṣaḥ .

076.07-08E: Witholding of favour, not getting posts of honour [* Lit. non-leadership], seizing the portion due (to any one), delay (in payment or advancement) and non-retaliation (or, not redressing wrongs) -- these are the causes of the disaffection of the troops.

076.09F: apīḍayanbalaṃ śatrūñjigīṣurabhiṣeṇayet .
076.09A: apīḍayan balam śatrūn jigīṣuḥ abhiṣeṇayet .
076.09P: apīḍayan i° ātmanaḥ sainyaṃ dīrghaprayāṇādinā apīḍayan akleśayan .
076.09P+: śatrūn abhiṣeṇayet , abhidravet , abhiyāyena pīḍayediti yāvat .

076.10F: sukhasādhyaṃ dviṣāṃ sainyaṃ dīrghayānaprapīḍitam .. 91..
076.10A: sukhasādhyam dviṣām sainyam dīrghayānaprapīḍitam .. 91..
076.10P: yataḥ dīrghayānaprapīḍitaṃ -- dūrākramaṇakhinnaṃ balaṃ śatrūṇāṃ sukhasādhyamanāyāsena jayyam . atiśrameṇa kṣīṇabalasya sainyasya parābhavaḥ sulabha iti bhāvaḥ .
076.10P+: atra manuḥ -- 'yadā manyeta bhāvena hṛṣṭapuṣṭabalaṃ svakam . parasya viparītaṃ cettadā yāyādarīnprati . yadā ca syātparikṣīṇo vāhanena balena ca . tadāsīta prayatnena śanakaiḥ sāntvayannarīn .' iti .
; Sampada: 'dIrGayAnapraapIqitam' there is a typo. (jim - yes '...prapIqitam')

076.09-10E: One wishing to gain victory should attack his enemies without hard-pressing his own army: for the army of the enemies, when extremely wearied by long marches, can be easily overpowered.

076.11F: dāyādād aparo mantro nāsti bhedakaro dviṣām .
076.11A: dāyādāt aparaḥ mantraḥ na asti bhedakaraḥ dviṣām .
076.11P: dāyādāt -- dāyaṃ paitṛkadhanasya vibhāgaṃ gṛhṇātīti dāyādaḥ sagotraḥ .
076.11P+: bhedakaro mantro nāsti - dāyāda eva śatrugṛhavicchede mukhyaṃ sādhanamityarthaḥ . ataḥ dāyādottejanaṃ kāryamityāha -- tasmāditi .

076.12F: tasmādutthāpayed yatnāddāyādaṃ tasya vidviṣaḥ .. 92..
076.12A: tasmāt utthāpayet yatnāt dāyādam tasya vidviṣaḥ .. 92..

076.11-12E: There is no cleverer stroke of policy than a kinsman (of the enemy won over) causing the over-throw of an enemy: one should, therefore, set up, by all means, a kinsman of the enemy against him.

076.13F: sandhāya yuvarājena yadi vā mukhyamantriṇā .
076.13A: sandhāya yuvarājena yadi vā mukhyamantriṇā .
076.13P: yuvarājena arāti -- nṛpaputreṇa iti yāvat .
076.13P+: mukhyamantriṇā śatroriti śeṣaḥ .

076.14F: antaḥ prakopanaṃ kāryamabhiyoktuḥ sthirātmanaḥ .. 93..
076.14A: antaḥ prakopanam kāryam abhiyoktuḥ sthirātmanaḥ .. 93..
076.14P: antaḥ prakopanaṃ -- gṛhakaliḥ .
076.14P+: abhiyoktuḥ -- sthirātmanaḥ . tṛtīyārthe ṣaṣṭhī .
076.14P++: dhīracetasā abhiyoktṛśatrugṛhe antarbhedaḥ prakṛtivyākopo vā kāryaḥ .

076.13-14E: Having entered into a league with the heir-apparent or the principal minister (of the enemy), [* Or, one should cause internal discord (in the camps of) an invader who is &c.] an invader who is steady of purpose, should cause internal dissentions (in his enemy's camps).

076.15F: krūraṃ mitraṃ raṇe cāpi bhaṅgaṃ dattvābhighātayet .

076.16F: athavā gograhākṛṣṭyā tanmukhyāśritabandhanāt .. 94..

076.16P: atha vā gavāṃ grahaḥ gograhastena yā ākṛṣṭistayā . athavetyanuvartanīyam .
076.16P+: tasya ye mukhyāḥ pradhānapuruṣāḥ āśritaḥ sevakāśca teṣāṃ bandhanāt tadghātayet . yadermitraṃ bhedākṣamaṃ tatpakṣapātācca samabhūmau krūraparākramaṃ tajjetuṃ sarvathā prayatitavyamiti bhāvaḥ .

076.15-16E: One should cause the destruction of a formidable ally (of his enemy) by giving him a defeat on the battlefield (or by fleeing before him and then suddenly turning upon him), or by seizing his cattle and capturing his principal men and dependants.

077.01F: svarājyaṃ vāsayedrājā paradeśāpavāhanāt .
077.01A: svarājyam vāsayet rājā paradeśāpavāhanāt .
077.01P: rājā paradeśāpavāhanāt śanoḥ deśasya apavāhanāttasmādbandibhāvena prajāḥ ānīya athavā dānamānābhyāṃ vanadānena satkāreṇa ca ānīya svarājyaṃ vāsayet -- svarājye niveśayet .

077.02F: athavā dānamānābhyāṃ vāsitaṃ dhanadaṃ hi tat .. 95..

077.02P: hi yataḥ tathā vāsitaṃ vṛddhaprajaṃ rājyaṃ dhanadaṃ samṛddhikaram .

077.01-02E: A king should cause his country to be populated by men brought forcibly from other countries, or rather, by means of gifts and the bestowal of honour; for when replenished with subjects it proves prosperous.

077.03F: rājāḥa -- āḥ kiṃ bahunoditena .

077.03-03E: The king observed -- Ah, why waste more words on this?

077.04-05E: The aggrandizement of one's power and the decline of that of the enemy -- the accomplishment of these two is all policy : having put forth this pre-eminently, those versed in policy display great eloquence (lit. play the Brihaspati).

077.06-06E: The minister observed with a smile -- All this is true, but --

077.07F: anyad ucchṛṅkhalaṃ sattvamanyacchāstraniyantritam .

077.07-08E: Unrestrained might is one thing, while might guided (or governed) by (the principles of) science is quite another: for whence can there be the existence of light and darkness in one and the same place?

077.09-10E: Then the king, having got up set out at the auspicious hour declared by the astrologers. Now the spy despatched by his emissary came to Hiranyagarbha and said --

077.15F: yadanena ko'pyasmaddurge prāgeva niyuktaḥ .
077.15A: yat anena kaḥ api asmat durge prāk eva niyuktaḥ .

077.11-15E: Sire, king Chitavarna is almost arrived. Now he is on the table-land of the Malaya mountain with his army encamped there. The castle should be carefully searched every moment: for, the vulture is a great statesman and in the course of his confidential talk with some one, I came to know his secret that he had already placed some one in our castle.

077.16F: cakro brūte -- deva kāka evāsau saṃbhavati .
077.16A: cakraḥ brūte -- deva kākaḥ eva asau saṃbhavati .

077.17F: rājāha -- na kadācid etat . yadyevaṃ tadā kathaṃ
077.17A: rājā āha -- na kadā cit etat . yadi evam tadā katham

077.16-17E: My lord, said Chakravaka, that could be the crow alone. It can never be, remarked the king. For, if this were the case, how

078.01F: tena śukasyābhibhavāyodyogaḥ kṛtaḥ . 
078.01A: tena śukasya abhibhavāya udyogaḥ kṛtaḥ . 
078.01P: abhibhavāya -- nigrahārtham .

078.02F: aparaṃ ca . śukasya gamanāt tasya vigrahotsāhaḥ . sa cirād atrāste .

; vigraha-utsAha.  Another edition has AgamanAt namely
; cf."Hitopadesha- Abhinava Rajalakshmi, With Hindi Translation" by Guru Prasad Shastri

078.01-02E: could he have shown readiness to punish the parrot?  Besides, it was after the departure of the parrot, that an eagerness for war was displayed there, while he is here for a long time.

078.03F: mantrī brūte -- tathāpyāgantukaḥ śaṅkanīyaḥ .
078.03A: mantrī brūte -- tathā api āgantukaḥ śaṅkanīyaḥ .

078.04F: rājāha --
078.04A: rājā āha --

078.05A: āgantukāḥ api kadācit upakārakāḥ dṛśyante . śṛṇu .

078.03-05E: The minister remarked -- Still a stranger must be suspected. The king rejoined -- Even strangers are sometimes observed to be benefactors. Listen --

078.06F: paro'pi hitavānbandhurbandhurapyahitaḥ paraḥ .
; print unclear: apyahitaH
078.06A: paraḥ api hitavān bandhuḥ bandhuḥ api ahitaḥ paraḥ .

078.07F: ahito dehajo vyādhirhitamāraṇyamauṣadham .. 98..
078.07A: ahitaḥ dehajaḥ vyādhiḥ hitam āraṇyam auṣadham .. 98..

078.06-07E: Even a stranger doing good is a relative, while a relative doing harm is a stranger (an enemy); a disease taking its birth in the body is injurious, while a medicinal herb produced in the forest is salutary.

078.08F: aparaṃ ca . āsīdvīravaro nāma śūdrakasya mahībhṛtaḥ .
078.08A: aparam ca . āsīt vīravaraḥ nāma śūdrakasya mahībhṛtaḥ .

078.09A: sevakaḥ svalpakālena saḥ dadau sutam ātmanaḥ .. 99..

078.08-09E: Moreover, There was a servant of the king Sudraka, Viravara by name, who in a short time, offered up his son.

078.13F: ahaṃ purā śūdrakasya rājñaḥ krīḍāsarasi karpūrakelināmno
078.13A: aham purā śūdrakasya rājñaḥ krīḍāsarasi karpūrakelināmnaḥ

078.14F: rājahaṃsasya putryā karpūramañjaryā sahānurāgavānabhavam . 
078.14A: rājahaṃsasya putryā karpūramañjaryā saha anurāgavān abhavam . 

078.13-14E: Formerly I fell in love with Karpuramanjari, daughter of the royal gander, Karpurakeli by name, who lived in the pleasure-lake of king Sudraka.

078.15F: tatra vīravaro nāma rājaputraḥ kutaściddeśādāgatya rājadvāramupagamya pratīhāramuvāca --

078.15-16E: A certain prince, Viravara by name, coming from some country, approached the royal gate and addressed the porter thus -- I, for one, am a prince whose object is wages (to seek service); procure me the sight of the king.

078.17F: tatastenāsau rājadarśanaṃ kārito brūte -- deva
078.17A: tataḥ tena asau rājadarśanam kāritaḥ brūte -- deva

078.18F: yadi mayā sevakena prayojanamasti tadāsmadvartanaṃ kriyatām .

078.18P: vartanam -- pṛ. 14 draṣṭavyam .

078.17-18E: Thereupon, he, being ushered into the royal presence by him, said -- Sire, if you wish to engage me as a servant fix my salary.

078.19F: śūdraka uvāca -- kiṃ te vartanam .
078.19A: śūdrakaḥ uvāca -- kim te vartanam .

078.20F: vīravaro brūte -- pratyahaṃ suvarṇaśatacatuṣṭayam  .
078.20A: vīravaraḥ brūte -- pratyaham suvarṇaśatacatuṣṭayam  .

078.19-20E: Sudraka asked -- What is your salary? Viravara replied -- Four hundred gold coins per day.

078.21F: rājāha -- kā te sāmagrī .
078.21A: rājā āha -- kā te sāmagrī .

078.22F: vīravaro brūte -- dvau bāhū . tṛtīyaśca khaḍgaḥ .
078.22A: vīravaraḥ brūte -- dvau bāhū . tṛtīyaḥ ca khaḍgaḥ .

078.21-22E: The king demanded -- What are your accoutrements? Viravara replied -- my two arms, and the third, my sword.

078.23F: rājāha -- naitacchakyam .
078.23A: rājā āha -- na etat śakyam .

078.24F: tacchrutvā vīravaraḥ praṇamya calitaḥ . atha mantribhiruktam --
078.24A: tat śrutvā vīravaraḥ praṇamya calitaḥ . atha mantribhiḥ uktam --

078.23-24E: The king said -- This is not possible. On hearing that he bowed and departed. Now the ministers observed --

078.25F: deva dinacatuṣṭayasya vartanaṃ dattvā jñāyatāmasya
078.25A: deva dinacatuṣṭayasya vartanam dattvā jñāyatām asya

078.26F: svarūpam . kimupayukto'yametāvadvartanaṃ gṛhṇātyanupayukto veti .
; Kale print unclear: kimupayukto

078.25-26E: Sire, having given him his four days' pay let us know his characteristic nature -- whether he receives such salary usefully (deservedly), or without being of use.

078.27F: tato mantrivacanād āhūya vīravarāya tāmbūlaṃ dattvā
078.27A: tataḥ mantrivacanāt āhūya vīravarāya tāmbūlam dattvā

078.28F: suvarṇaśatacatuṣṭayaṃ dattam . tadviniyogaśca rājñā sunibhṛtaṃ nirūpitaḥ .
078.28A: suvarṇaśatacatuṣṭayam dattam . tat-viniyogaḥ ca rājñā sunibhṛtam nirūpitaḥ .
078.28P: viniyogaḥ -- vyayakaraṇam .

078.27-28E: Then, in accordance with the ministers' advice, Viravara was called back and given a betel-nut-roll and four hundred coins of gold. The king very secretly watched the use he made of them.

078.29F: tadardhaṃ vīravareṇa devebhyo brāhmaṇebhyaśca dattam . 
078.29A: tat-ardham vīravareṇa devebhyaḥ brāhmaṇebhyaḥ ca dattam . 

078.30F: sthitasyārdhaṃ duḥkhitebhyaḥ . tadavaśiṣṭaṃ bhojyavyayavilāsavyayena vyayitam . 
078.30A: sthitasya ardham duḥkhitebhyaḥ . tat-avaśiṣṭam bhojyavyayavilāsavyayena vyayitam . 

078.29-30E: Half of the money Viravara gave to the gods and the Brahmanas; half of what remained to the distressed, and the remainder he spent in food and amusements.

078.31F: etatsarvaṃ nityakṛtyaṃ kṛtvā rājadvāramaharniśaṃ khaḍgapāṇiḥ sevate .
078.31A: etat sarvam nityakṛtyam kṛtvā rājadvāram ahaḥ niśam khaḍgapāṇiḥ sevate .

078.32F: yadā ca rājā svayaṃ samādiśati tadā svagṛhamapi yāti . 
078.32A: yadā ca rājā svayam samādiśati tadā svagṛham api yāti . 

078.31-32E: Having done all these daily duties he attended, sword in hand, at the king's door, day and night. He also went home whenever the king ordered him to do so.

078.33F: athaikadā kṛṣṇacaturdaśyāṃ rātrau rājā sakaruṇaṃ krandanadhvaniṃ
078.33A: atha ekadā kṛṣṇacaturdaśyām rātrau rājā sakaruṇam krandanadhvanim

078.34F: śuśrāva . śudraka uvāca -- kaḥ ko'tra dvāri .
078.34A: śuśrāva . śudrakaḥ uvāca -- kaḥ kaḥ atra dvāri .

078.33-34E: Once, on the fourteenth night of the dark half of a month, the king heard a plaintive sound of lamentation. Sudraka asked -- Who waits at the door?

078.35F: tenoktaṃ -- deva ahaṃ vīravaraḥ .
078.35A: tena uktam -- deva aham vīravaraḥ .

078.36F: rājovāca -- krandanānusaraṇaṃ kriyatām .

078.36P: krandanānusaraṇam -- krandanaśabdānurodhena gamanam .

078.35-36E: He replied -- I, Viravara. The king said -- Follow the sound of wailing.

078.37F: vīravaraḥ yathājñāpayati deva ityuktvā calitaḥ .
078.37A: vīravaraḥ yathā ājñāpayati devaḥ iti uktvā calitaḥ .

078.38F: rājñā ca cintitam -- naitaducitam . ayamekākī rājaputro mayā sūcībhedye tamasi
078.38A: rājñā ca cintitam -- na etat ucitam . ayam ekākī rājaputraḥ mayā sūcībhedye tamasi
078.38P: sūcībhedye tamasi gāḍhāndhakāre .

078.39F: preritaḥ . tadanu gatvā kimetaditi nirūpayāmi .
078.39A: preritaḥ . tad-anu gatvā kim etat iti nirūpayāmi .

078.38-39E: Saying, 'As Your Majesty commands', away went Viravara. Now the king reflected -- It is not proper that I sent this prince, all alone, in the pitchy darkness. I will, therefore, go after him and see what this might mean.

078.40F: tato rājāpi
078.40A: tataḥ rājā api

078.41F: khaḍgamādāya tadanusaraṇakrameṇa nagarādbahirnirjagāma . 
078.41A: khaḍgam ādāya tadanusaraṇakrameṇa nagarāt bahiḥ nirjagāma . 

078.40-41E: So the king, too, took his sword and went out of the city, following his course.

078.42F: gatvā ca vīravareṇa sā rudatī rūpayauvanasaṃpannā sarvālaṅkārabhūṣitā kācit
078.42A: gatvā ca vīravareṇa sā rudatī rūpayauvanasaṃpannā sarvālaṅkārabhūṣitā kā-cit

078.42-43E: Viravara, on reaching the place, saw a woman, endowed with beauty and youth and decorated with ornaments of every description, crying; and asked her -- Who are you? Why do you weep? 

078.44F: striyoktam -- ahametasya śūdrakasya rājño lakṣmīḥ . 
078.44A: striyā uktam -- aham etasya śūdrakasya rājñaḥ lakṣmīḥ .

; CAyA shade

078.44-45E: The woman replied -- I am the goddess of royalty of this king, Sudraka. I have long lived in great happiness under the shadow of his arms, but now I shall (have to) go elsewhere.

078.46F: vīravaro brūte -- yatrāpāyaḥ saṃbhavati tatropāyo'pyasti .
078.46A: vīravaraḥ brūte -- yatra apāyaḥ saṃbhavati tatra upāyaḥ api asti .

078.47F: tatkathaṃ syāt punarihāvalambanaṃ bhagavatyāḥ .
078.47A: tat katham syāt punar iha avalambanam bhagavatyāḥ .
078.47P: avalambanaṃ sthitiḥ avasthānam .

078.47-34E: Viravara said -- Where there is a possibility of danger there is also a remedy. By what means then will the stability of your divine self here be ensured?

078.48F: lakṣmīruvāca -- yadi tvamātmanaḥ putraṃ śaktidharaṃ
078.48A: lakṣmīḥ uvāca -- yadi tvam ātmanaḥ putram śaktidharam

078.49F: dvātriṃśallakṣaṇopetaṃ bhagavatyāḥ sarvamaṅgalāyā upahārīkaroṣi
078.49A: dvātriṃśat lakṣaṇopetam bhagavatyāḥ sarvamaṅgalāyāḥ upahārīkaroṣi
078.49P: dvātriṃśallakṣaṇopetam dve ca triṃśacca yadvā dyadhikā triṃśadyāni lakṣaṇāni taiḥ upetam .

078.49P++: upahārīkaroṣi -- baliṃ dadāsi .

078.50F: tadāhaṃ punaratra suciraṃ sukhaṃ nivasāmi . ityuktvādṛśyābhavat .
078.50A: tadā aham punaḥ atra suciram sukham nivasāmi . iti uktvā adṛśyā abhavat .

078.48-50E: The goddess of royalty said -- If you will offer up your son, Saktidhara, endowed with thirty-two auspicious marks, to the goddess Sarvamangala (presiding over all blessings), then I can again live here happily for a long time. Saying so she disappeared from view.

079.01F: tato vīravareṇa svagṛhaṃ
079.01A: tataḥ vīravareṇa svagṛham

079.02F: gatvā nidrāṇā svavadhūḥ prabodhitā putraśca . 
079.02A: gatvā nidrāṇā svavadhūḥ prabodhitā putraḥ ca . 

079.01-02E: Viravara then went home and roused his wife, who was asleep, and his son.

079.03F: tau nidrāṃ parityajyotthāyopaviṣṭau . vīravarastatsarvaṃ lakṣmīvacanamuktavān .
079.03A: tau nidrām parityajya utthāya upaviṣṭau . vīravaraḥ tat sarvam lakṣmīvacanam uktavān .

079.01-03E: They having shaken off their sleep rose and sat down. Viravara communicated to them all that the goddess had said to him.

079.04F: tacchrutvā sānandaḥ śaktidharo brūte -- dhanyo'hamevambhūtaḥ .
079.04A: tat śrutvā sānandaḥ śaktidharaḥ brūte -- dhanyaḥ aham evam bhūtaḥ .

079.05F: svāmirājyarakṣārthaṃ yasyopayogaḥ . tattāta ko'dhunā vilambasya hetuḥ . 
079.05A: svāmirājyarakṣārtham yasya upayogaḥ . tat tāta kaḥ adhunā vilambasya hetuḥ . 

079.04-05E: Hearing that Saktidhara, being full of joy, said -- Blessed am I, being such as will be useful for the preservation of our lord's sovereignty. Then father, what occasion is there for delay?

079.06F: kadāpi tāvadevaṃvidha eva karmaṇyetasya dehasya viniyogaḥ ślāghyaḥ . yataḥ .
079.06A: kadā api tāvat evaṃvidhe eva karmaṇi etasya dehasya viniyogaḥ ślāghyaḥ . yataḥ .

079.06-06E: The use of this body, in such a cause as this, whenever it may be, is praiseworthy, For --

079.07F: dhanāni jīvitaṃ caiva parārthe prājña utsṛjet .
079.07A: dhanāni jīvitam ca eva parārthe prājñaḥ utsṛjet .
079.07P: dhanāni i° sannimittaṃ satkāryāya .

079.08F: sannimittaṃ varaṃ tyāgo vināśe niyate sati .. 100..
079.08A: sannimittam varam tyāgaḥ vināśe niyate sati .. 100..
079.08P: tyāgaḥ -- jīvitasya dhanasya ca . gatapūrvoyaṃ ślo. mi. 22 .

079.07-08E: A wise man should give up his wealth and life for others; their abandonment in a good cause is better when destruction is certain.
; 01-03-2022 end

079.09F: śaktidharamātovāca -- yadyetanna kartavyaṃ tatkenānyena

079.10F: karmaṇā mukhyasya mahāvartanasya niṣkrayo bhaviṣyati .

079.10P: niṣkrayaḥ -- nistāraṃ , ānṛṇyam .

079.09-10E: Saktidhara's mother remarked -- If this is not to be done, then by what other act can a return be made for the high salary paid in gold?

079.11F: ityālocya sarve sarvamaṅgalāyāḥ sthānaṃ gatāḥ . tatra sarvamaṅgalāṃ saṃpūjya
079.11A: iti ālocya sarve sarvamaṅgalāyāḥ sthānam gatāḥ . tatra sarvamaṅgalām saṃpūjya

079.12F: vīravaro brūte -- devi prasīda . vijayatāṃ vijayatāṃ śūdrako mahārājaḥ .
079.12A: vīravaraḥ brūte -- devi prasīda . vijayatām vijayatām śūdrakaḥ mahārājaḥ .

079.11-12E: Having thus deliberated they all went to the temple of Sarvamangala. There having offered worship to the goddess, Viravara said –-  goddess, be propitiated. May the great king Sudraka be ever triumphant (prosper)!

079.13F: gṛhyatāmayamupahāraḥ . ityuktvā putrasya śiraściccheda . tato
079.13A: gṛhyatām ayam upahāraḥ . iti uktvā putrasya śiraḥ ciccheda . tataḥ

079.14F: vīravaraścintayāmāsa -- gṛhītarājavartanasya tāvannistāraḥ kṛtaḥ .
079.14A: vīravaraḥ cintayāmāsa -- gṛhītarājavartanasya tāvat nistāraḥ kṛtaḥ .

079.13-14E: Accept this offering. With these words he cut off his son's head. Then Viravara thought to himself -- As for the salary received from the king, it has been repaid.

079.15F: adhunā niṣputrasya me jīvanaṃ viḍambanam . ityālocyātmanaḥ śiraścinnavān .
079.15A: adhunā niṣputrasya me jīvanam viḍambanam . iti ālocya ātmanaḥ śiraḥ cinnavān .
079.15P: viḍambanam -- garhaṇamātram .

079.16F: tataḥ striyāpi svāminaḥ putrasya ca śokārtayā tad anuṣṭhitam . 
079.16A: tataḥ striyā api svāminaḥ putrasya ca śokārtayā tat anuṣṭhitam . 

079.15-16E: Now that I have become sonless, life is but a mockery (miserable) with me. Thinking so he cut off his own head. Then his wife, too, being oppressed with grief for her husband and son, did the same.

079.17F: etatsarvaṃ śrutvā dṛṣṭvā ca sa rājā sāścaryaṃ cintayāmāsa --
079.17A: etat sarvam śrutvā dṛṣṭvā ca saḥ rājā sa-āścaryam cintayāmāsa --

079.17-17E: Having heard and seen all that, the king, filled with astonishment, said to himself --

079.18F: jīvanti ca mriyante ca madvidhāḥ kṣudrajantavaḥ .
079.18A: jīvanti ca mriyante ca madvidhāḥ kṣudrajantavaḥ .

079.19F: anena sadṛśo loke na bhūto na bhaviṣyati .. 101..
079.19A: anena sadṛśaḥ loke na bhūtaḥ na bhaviṣyati .. 101..

079.18-19E: Insignificant creatures, like myself, live and die: but there never has been nor will ever be, in this world, one like unto him.

079.20F: tadetatparityaktena mama rājyenāpi aprayojanam . tataḥ
079.20A: tat etat-parityaktena mama rājyena api kim prayojanam . tataḥ

079.21F: svaśiraśchettumullāsitaḥ khaḍgaḥ śūdrakeṇāpi . 
079.21A: svaśiraḥ chettum ullāsitaḥ khaḍgaḥ śūdrakeṇa api . 
079.21P: ullāsitaḥ -- uddhṛtaḥ .

079.20-21E: So I shall have nothing to do with my kingdom, which is deserted by him. Then the sword was raised by Sudraka also to lop off his head.

079.22F: atha bhagavatyā sarvamaṅgalayā pratyakṣabhūtayā rājā haste dhṛta uktaśca --
079.22A: atha bhagavatyā sarvamaṅgalayā pratyakṣabhūtayā rājā haste dhṛtaḥ uktaḥ ca --

079.23F: putra prasannāsmi te .
079.23A: putra prasannā asmi te .

079.22-23E: Now the goddess Sarvamangala, appearing in a visible form, seized the king by the hand and said -- Son, I am pleased with thee.
